Variables modeled: `accounts` (Domains → [balance] — collapsed from the full AccountState since the nonce / stake / ed_pub side is FB7 / FB8 / FB5 territory; the cross-shard outbound apply path only consults the `balance` field), `accumulated_outbound` (Nat — matches `Chain::accumulated_outbound_` at `src/chain/chain.cpp:1394`; the chain-level counter that aggregates per-block `block_outbound` advances), `pending_receipts` (Seq(Receipt) — the producer-side `b.cross_shard_receipts` field; the model collapses the 11-field CrossShardReceipt struct to the (to, amount) pair since FB18 only cares about apply-side emission count + amount accumulation), `pending_txs` (Seq(Transfer) — the per-block tx queue), `height` (Nat — action counter bounding TLC). Actions modeled: `SubmitTransfer` (adversarial/user surface — any well-formed Transfer may be queued), `ApplyLocalTransfer` (same-shard branch at chain.cpp:752-761; debit sender, credit recipient, fee absorbed by creators), `ApplyCrossShardTransfer` (cross-shard branch at chain.cpp:762-766 + producer emission at producer.cpp:459-465; debit sender, increment accumulated_outbound, emit receipt, NO local credit), `ApplyInsufficientBalance` (the `continue` silent-skip at chain.cpp:744 — no mutation, no orphan emission), `FinalizeBlock` (block-finalize tail at chain.cpp:1393-1394 — the model's "block flushed to chain" transition).

This spec is the source-side companion to FB14 (CrossShardReceiptDedup — destination-side dedup) and FB17 (AppliedReceiptRestore — snapshot lifecycle of the destination dedup set). The triangle FB2 ↔ FB14 ↔ FB18 covers the cross-shard mechanism from three complementary angles: receipt-flow soundness (FB2 — emitted + admitted), per-block dst-dedup (FB14 — applied set monotonicity), and per-block source debit + accumulator (FB18 — A1 source-mass departure). FB17 (AppliedReceiptRestore) sits orthogonal at the snapshot/restore lifecycle. The structural asymmetries between source-side (FB18) and destination-side (FB14):

1. **No dedup primitive on source.** FB18 has no `applied_outbound_receipts` analog because the source emits each cross-shard receipt exactly once per source tx (V12 — Lemma L-7.1 — binds receipts 1:1 to txs). The model's `pending_receipts.Append` is the structural witness — every successful ApplyCrossShardTransfer extends the receipt seq by exactly one entry.
2. **No idempotency contract on source.** A double-submit of the same tx (same from/to/amount/fee tuple) on source produces two debits and two receipts — the nonce gate at chain.cpp:739 catches this in production (FB7 territory); FB18 abstracts the nonce as the SubmitTransfer's adversarial freedom but doesn't model the gate (orthogonal concern).
3. **No snapshot survival concern on source.** Pre-S-037 the destination's dedup set was at risk on restore (FB17 closure); the source's `accumulated_outbound` field has always survived restore because it's a single Nat-typed accumulator covered by the safety-critical state_root namespace at chain.cpp:408. FB18 confirms this via the absence of a Snapshot/Restore action pair in its action set.

Companion prose proof: `docs/proofs/CrossShardOutboundApply.md` (separately written by a parallel agent).
### NefPoolDrain.tla → E1 NEF pool drain state machine (SubmitRegister / ApplyFirstRegister / ApplyReRegister)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `Inv_TypeOK` | shape of `registrants` (SUBSET Domains), `balances` (AllAddresses → 0..InitialNefPool — includes ZerothAddress as the pool home), `pending_register` (Seq(Domains)), `height` (Nat action counter) |
| `Inv_PoolNonNegative` | `balances[ZerothAddress] >= 0` at every reachable state — the floor-half drain (`P \div 2`) is closed on Nat; once the pool reaches 0, the terminal `0 \div 2 = 0` keeps it there |
| `Inv_GeometricExhaustion` | T-N1 quantified upper bound: for every `k \in 0..|Domains|`, if `|registrants| >= k` then `2^k * balances[ZerothAddress] <= InitialNefPool`. The K-th distinct first-time register applies the K-th floor-half; arithmetic gives `pool <= floor(P / 2^K)`. The headline geometric-drain witness — pre-existing FB11 had only the non-negativity floor, not the upper-bound progression |
| `Inv_A1Conservation` | T-N5 supply identity: `balances[ZerothAddress] + sum_{d \in Domains} balances[d] = InitialNefPool` at every reachable state. Every NEF action is an internal pool→domain redistribution; no action mints or destroys. The sentinel-balance pattern collapses the FB11 `nef_pool` + `accounts` two-variable identity into a single sum-of-balances identity |
| `Inv_DrainOnlyOnFirstRegister` | T-N2 action-level invariant: any `balances'[ZerothAddress] < balances[ZerothAddress]` step must be paired with a fresh domain entering `registrants`. The headline defense against the registration-churn drain attack — re-register cannot drain. Matches the `first_time_register` bool gate at `src/chain/chain.cpp:795-796` |
| `Prop_EventualExhaustion` (temporal) | T-N6 eventual-progress: under fairness on SubmitRegister + ApplyFirstRegister, eventually `balances[ZerothAddress] = 0` OR `|registrants| = |Domains|` (all domains have first-registered and the pool has drained as far as the model's domain budget permits). The escape branch is required because TLC operates on bounded models — for `InitialNefPool = 8, |Domains| = 3`, the pool reaches 1 (not 0) after 3 first-registers; further drain requires more domains |
| `Prop_RegistrationIsTerminal` (temporal) | T-N7 action-level: `d \in registrants => d \in registrants'` across every `[Next]_vars` step. Once a domain enters registrants, it stays. No Deregister action is modeled in this scope — for the NEF drain surface, registration is one-way and permanent. The temporal witness that the floor-half drain is monotone over the registrants partial order |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other eleven specs above). The configuration in `NefPoolDrain.cfg` (3 domains {a, b, c}, InitialNefPool=8, MaxHeight=4, ZerothAddress=zeroth sentinel) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. Variables modeled: `registrants` (SUBSET Domains — the set of domains that have first-registered), `balances` (AllAddresses → Nat — collapses the C++ `accounts_` map + the ZEROTH-address pool into a single function indexed by Domains \cup {ZerothAddress}; the sentinel-pattern lifts the A1 supply identity into a sum-of-balances over the lifted index set), `pending_register` (Seq(Domains) — the submitted-but-not-applied register-tx queue; matches the C++ apply order at chain.cpp:734 `for (auto& tx : b.transactions)`), `height` (Nat — action counter bounding TLC). Actions modeled: `SubmitRegister` (any caller can submit any domain for register — the adversarial surface), `ApplyFirstRegister` (the first-time apply branch at chain.cpp:813-833 — drains pool by floor-half, credits drained amount, adds domain to registrants), `ApplyReRegister` (the already-registered apply branch — consumes from pending without mutating drain state, witnesses T-N3). InitialNefPool=8 lets the floor-half drain fire 4 times (8 → 4 → 2 → 1 → 0) before reaching the absorbing 0-state; with 3 domains the model exhausts at pool=1 after 3 first-registers (T-N1 K=3 case). The T-N4 zero-pool noop branch (pool=0 → ApplyFirstRegister with 0 drain) is not reachable in the 3-domain InitialNefPool=8 cfg but is structurally witnessed by the ApplyFirstRegister action body — the same `drain = pool \div 2` formula, evaluated at pool=0, yields 0 with no further mutation; reproducibly reachable in a 4-domain InitialNefPool=8 or 3-domain InitialNefPool=4 cfg variant.

**Distinction from FB11 SubsidyDistribution.tla:** the two specs together cover the NEF drain from complementary angles. FB11 models the NEF drain alongside block-subsidy distribution and collapses Submit + Apply into a single Register action (the apply-side enforcement is the focus); FB19 zooms in on the NEF-only surface and pulls the submit/apply lifecycle into an explicit pending sequence so the apply-order semantics + the re-register stutter are observable at the state-machine layer. The FB11 `Inv_NefDrainsOnceperDomain` is the action-level pair (registered FALSE→TRUE) witness; FB19's `Inv_DrainOnlyOnFirstRegister` is the same claim restated in terms of the registrants-set delta (set-membership growth). The headline FB19-specific invariant is `Inv_GeometricExhaustion` — the quantified upper bound `2^k * pool <= InitialNefPool` is not present in FB11; FB19 elevates the floor-half drain semantics to a parametric inequality over the number of distinct first-registers.

Companion prose proof: `docs/proofs/NefPoolDrain.md` (separately tracked; the prose track is being assembled in parallel).
### MultiEventComposition.tla → composed per-block apply pipeline (Construct / Apply / AdvanceHeight)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `Inv_TypeOK` | T-MC1: shape of `balances` (Domains → Nat), `stakes` (Domains → Nat), `applied_receipts` (SUBSET DedupKey — shared with FB14), `accumulated_outbound` (Nat — write-only outbound counter), `accumulated_slashed` (Nat — shared FB15+FB16 accumulator), `height` (0..MaxHeight*3), `pending_block` (PendingBlock record with four sub-event SUBSET fields, or NoPendingBlock sentinel) |
| `Inv_A1Conservation` | T-MC2: supply-axis identity across composed apply. `SumStakes + accumulated_slashed <= Cardinality(Domains) * MaxStake` — slashing rebooks stake mass into the accumulator; total stake-axis mass is preserved across every ApplyBlock step. The composed step decrements stakes[d] by `abort_slash + equiv_slash` and increments accumulated_slashed by the same sum across all domains, preserving the bound. The transfer + receipt + subsidy side of the supply identity is FB5 / FB10 / FB11 territory and inherited via the per-event-invariants-compose conjunction |
| `Inv_DeterministicOrder` | T-MC3: the headline composition contract. When `pending_block /= NoPendingBlock`, ConstructBlock is structurally disabled (its pre-condition requires `pending_block = NoPendingBlock`), so the only balance/stake-mutating action is the deterministic ApplyBlock. Apply order within the block is fixed at the C++ source-line level (chain.cpp:734 tx loop → 1313 abort loop → 1344 equiv loop → 1363 receipt loop → 1286 distribution loop); the spec's single-step ApplyBlock transition is the state-machine witness of that fixed ordering |
| `Inv_PerEventInvariantsCompose` | T-MC4: the conjunction of the most-load-bearing single-event invariants, each lifted from its source spec. (a) `balances[d] >= 0` (FB5 / FB10), (b) `stakes[d] >= 0` (FB15 / FB16), (c) `accumulated_slashed >= 0` (FB15 / FB16), (d) `accumulated_outbound >= 0` (FB2 / FB14), (e) every dedup-key has the DedupKey shape (FB14 T-R3). The invariant is the structural witness that COMPOSITION does not break ANY single-event invariant — TLC exhausts every ConstructBlock + ApplyBlock interleaving within the model bound |
| `Inv_AppliedReceiptsMonotonic` | FB14 T-R4 lifted to the composition layer: applied_receipts is set-only-grows. ApplyBlock only extends (via `applied_receipts \cup {DedupKeyOf(r) : r \in fresh_receipts}`); ConstructBlock and AdvanceHeight preserve. The structural witness of cross-block dedup persistence under composition |
| `Inv_SlashedMonotonic` | FB15 / FB16 lifted: `accumulated_slashed >= 0` and no action decreases it. The shared slash-accumulator's monotonicity holds across all four sub-event apply paths (transfers, receipts, subsidies do not touch it; aborts + equivocations only add) |
| `Inv_OutboundMonotonic` | FB2 / FB14 lifted: `accumulated_outbound >= 0`. The write-only outbound counter is preserved by ApplyBlock (the spec's apply path does not emit cross-shard outbound — that surface is the source-chain's block-finalize stage, modeled in the companion `MultiEventComposition.md` prose proof) |
| `Prop_EventualApply` (temporal) | T-MC6: under WF on ApplyBlock, any pending block eventually drains. The state-level form: `pending_block /= NoPendingBlock => <>(pending_block = NoPendingBlock)`. Combined with the AdvanceHeight stutter, gives the eventual-apply progress guarantee under fairness |
| `Prop_ReplayMatch` (temporal) | T-MC5: after ApplyBlock fires, `applied_receipts` contains every dedup-key from the block's receipts sub-event set. A hypothetical re-apply of the same block would route every receipt through the duplicate branch (FB14 dedup gate), preserving the end-state. The structural witness of the apply-idempotency contract that snapshot/restore + replay depend on |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other eleven specs above). The configuration in `MultiEventComposition.cfg` (3 domains, MaxAmount=2, MaxStake=5, MaxHeight=3, 2 hashes, 2 shards) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under a minute on a single core. Variables modeled: `balances` (Domains → Nat — per-domain balance ledger), `stakes` (Domains → Nat — per-domain locked stake), `applied_receipts` (SUBSET DedupKey — cross-block dedup set; shape shared with FB14), `accumulated_outbound` (Nat — write-only outbound counter), `accumulated_slashed` (Nat — shared FB15+FB16 accumulator at chain.cpp:1395), `height` (Nat — action counter), `pending_block` (PendingBlock record or NoPendingBlock sentinel). Actions modeled: `ConstructBlock(ts, abs, eqs, rs)` (non-deterministic block admission with bounded sub-event set sizes; the ONLY non-determinism point per T-MC3), `ApplyBlock` (the canonical apply pipeline — composes transfers, aborts, equivocations, and receipts into a single deterministic transition matching the C++ chain.cpp:734-1305 apply loop order), `AdvanceHeight` (temporal driver / stutter). The four sub-event classes are bounded at ConstructBlock admission (transfers <= 2, aborts <= 1, equivs <= 1, receipts <= 1) to keep the SUBSET state-space tractable.

This spec is the FB-track composition of FB5 (AccountState — transfers), FB14 (CrossShardReceiptDedup — receipts), FB15 (EquivocationApply — equivocations), FB16 (AbortApply — aborts), and FB10 (FeeAccounting) + FB11 (SubsidyDistribution) — fee + subsidy distribution. Each prior spec verifies its sub-event class in isolation; FB20 verifies that COMPOSITION does not break any single-event invariant AND that the canonical apply order is fixed at the C++ source-line level. The deterministic-pipeline contract (T-MC3) is the headline composition-spec property — validators receiving sub-event sequences in any interleaving across producer-aggregation + gossip + admission ALL produce the same post-apply state because the C++ apply path replays in the canonical order regardless of arrival order. The DedupKey type is shared verbatim with FB14, ensuring the cross-block dedup-set's structure is preserved under composition.

Companion prose proof: `docs/proofs/MultiEventComposition.md` (separately tracked; the prose track is being assembled in parallel).

### StakeForfeitureCascade.tla → STAKE / DEREGISTER / UNSTAKE / Equivocate cascade state machine

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `Inv_TypeOK` | T-C1: shape of `accounts` (Domains → [balance, stake_locked]), `registrants` (Domains → [active, inactive_from]), `unlock_heights` (Domains → 0..Sentinel), `accumulated_slashed` (0..INITIAL_TOTAL_VALUE), `height` (0..MaxHeight), `pending` (Seq(Event) with kind ∈ {STAKE, DEREGISTER, UNSTAKE, EQUIVOCATE}) |
| `Inv_StakeNonNegative` | T-C2: `accounts[d].stake_locked >= 0` at every reachable state — the composed cascade never drives the field negative. Nat-typed; documents the contract. ApplyStake adds, UnstakePost zeroes, ApplyEquivocate zeroes; no action subtracts below 0 |
| `Inv_NoBalanceOnSlashedAccount` | T-C3: structural witness that an Equivocate-deactivated registry entry (active=FALSE AND inactive_from /= Sentinel AND inactive_from = height OR inactive_from = height + 1) has stake_locked = 0 post-slash — the headline "slash is one-way, full-forfeiture is permanent" claim lifted into the cascade |
| `Inv_A1Conservation` | T-C6: composed cascade supply identity: `SumBalances + SumStakes + accumulated_slashed = INITIAL_TOTAL_VALUE` at every reachable state. The headline supply-conservation claim for the full cascade. Every action preserves the sum: ApplyStake is balance → stake_locked, UnstakePost is stake_locked → balance, ApplyEquivocate is stake_locked → accumulated_slashed (rebooking), all other actions are stutters on the value-bearing variables |
| `Inv_UnstakePostSlashIsNoOp` | T-C4: post-slash UnstakePost is harmless. Action-form: applying UnstakePost when stake_locked[d] = 0 is a stutter on (balance, stake_locked) — balance' = balance + 0 = balance. The structural witness that the post-slash UnstakePost compose-then-fire ordering does not double-credit the offender. Matches the C++ apply-path's `sit->second.locked -= amount` reduction at locked=0 |
| `Inv_OrderSensitivity` | T-C5: action-form witness that Equivocate-then-UnstakePost vs UnstakePost-then-Equivocate yield diverging (balance) end-states. The composed cascade is order-sensitive on (balance) but order-insensitive on (stake_locked, accumulated_slashed-sum). TLC enumerates both branches under the action interleaving and verifies the two distinct end-states are reachable. The headline "composition outcome depends on event order" claim of FB21 |
| `Inv_SlashedMonotonic` | FB15 lifted to the cascade: `accumulated_slashed >= 0` and no action decreases it. ApplyEquivocate only adds, all other actions preserve. Cross-cascade verification that the FB15 monotonicity is robust under the cascade interleaving |
| `Inv_UnlockMonotonic` | FB8 lifted to the cascade: per-domain `unlock_heights[d]` is monotone non-decreasing across every `[Next]_vars` step. ApplyDeregister arms, UnstakePost clears-to-Sentinel (the largest possible value, > MaxHeight + UnstakeDelay + 1 by ConfigOK). Cross-cascade verification of FB8's headline non-decrease claim |
| `Prop_EventualResolution` (temporal) | T-C7: under WF on AdvanceHeight + each Apply* action, the pending queue eventually drains to empty OR the model bound is reached (`height >= MaxHeight`). Apply-time progress guarantee for the full cascade; the bounded-model escape clause keeps TLC tractable |
| `Prop_NoDoubleForfeit` (temporal) | T-C8: across every `[Next]_vars` step, a single domain contributes at most pre-step `stake_locked[d]` to accumulated_slashed. The second equivocation for the same offender hits the ApplyEquivocateGhost branch and contributes 0 — the structural witness of FB15 T-E4 lifted into the cascade. Combined with `Inv_SlashedMonotonic`, gives the full "an account can only be fully-slashed once" guarantee |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twelve specs above). The configuration in `StakeForfeitureCascade.cfg` (2 domains {a, b}, MaxHeight=4, MaxStake=5, UnstakeDelay=2, Sentinel=1000) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under a minute on a single core. Variables modeled: `accounts` (Domains → [balance: Nat, stake_locked: Nat] — collapses the C++ `accounts_` balance + `stakes_` locked fields into a single record per domain since the cascade is the smallest scope where they must be tracked atomically), `registrants` (Domains → [active: BOOLEAN, inactive_from: 0..Sentinel] — same shape as FB8 + FB15), `unlock_heights` (Domains → 0..Sentinel — the FB8 unlock-arming field), `accumulated_slashed` (Nat — shared with FB15 / FB16 / FB20 via the chain.cpp:1395 accumulator), `height` (Nat — chain-height action counter, bounds TLC), `pending` (Seq(Event) — admission queue with FIFO drain). Actions modeled: `SubmitStake`, `SubmitDeregister`, `SubmitUnstake`, `SubmitEquivocate` (adversarial admission — the validator could be byzantine; the apply-layer guards filter out the truly invalid claims), `ApplyStake` (balance → stake_locked move on success), `ApplyStakeReject` (insufficient-balance silent-skip stutter), `ApplyDeregister` (arms unlock_height = height + 1 + UnstakeDelay), `ApplyDeregisterRejectAlreadyInactive` (second-DEREGISTER stutter — FB8 stricter model), `UnstakePre` (pre-unlock fee-refund branch at chain.cpp:881-888), `UnstakePost` (post-unlock refund branch at chain.cpp:889-893), `ApplyEquivocate` (full forfeiture + registry deactivation — chain.cpp:1344-1356), `ApplyEquivocateGhost` (stake_locked = 0 second-equivocation no-op — FB15 T-E4), `AdvanceHeight` (temporal driver). UnstakeDelay=2 + MaxHeight=4 gives the model enough headroom to exercise both pre-unlock and post-unlock UNSTAKE attempts under either ordering with Equivocate.

The headline cross-domain coverage matrix:

  * **Stake → Deregister → wait → Unstake** (happy path; FB8 territory verified as the no-slash baseline)
  * **Stake → Equivocate** (immediate slash; stake_locked → 0 / accumulated_slashed += stake)
  * **Stake → Deregister → Equivocate → UnstakePost** (order A — slash first; UnstakePost is no-op per T-C4)
  * **Stake → Deregister → UnstakePost → Equivocate** (order B — Unstake first; Equivocate hits ghost branch per T-C8)
  * **Stake → UnstakePre (pre-unlock)** (fee-refund stutter; FB8 UnstakeFailEarly lifted)
  * **Stake → Equivocate → Equivocate** (second equivocation hits ghost branch; T-C8 verifies it contributes 0)
  * **Two-domain isolation**: cross-domain "slash one, don't touch the other" — Inv_A1Conservation across the second domain witnesses the slash is account-scoped

The order-sensitivity contract (T-C5) is the distinguishing claim of FB21 against its predecessors. FB8 verifies the happy-path lifecycle in isolation (no equivocation surface). FB15 verifies the slash lifecycle in isolation (no UNSTAKE surface). FB16 verifies bounded slashing in isolation (no full-forfeiture surface; the `std::min` floor). FB20 verifies the composed pipeline at the block level, but the four sub-event classes apply within a single canonical step and there is no in-block ordering ambiguity to observe. FB21 zooms in on the STAKE-axis specifically and admits the cross-event interleaving across BLOCK boundaries — the same account can have a STAKE event admitted in block N, a DEREGISTER in block N+1, an EQUIVOCATE and an UNSTAKE both submitted (in either order) for block N+2 — and TLC exhausts every reachable ordering. The diverging end-states (balance = pre-stake-balance vs balance = pre-stake-balance + amount) witness that the cascade is composition-order-sensitive on value but composition-order-invariant on slash mass.

Companion prose proof: `docs/proofs/StakeForfeitureCascade.md` (separately tracked; the prose track is being assembled in parallel).

### F2ViewReconciliation.tla → v2.7 F2 view-reconciliation primitives (compute_view_root / reconcile_union / reconcile_intersection + V21..V26)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `contribs` (MemberIds → ContribMsg with three (root, list) pairs), `block_eq` / `block_abort` / `block_inbound` (each `\subseteq Hashes`), `generated` (BOOLEAN bit gating the post-enumeration invariants) |
| `INV_UnionMonotonic` | INV-1: adding any honest member's list to the K-committee can only GROW the union. State-form: every hash committed by any member appears in `block_eq`. Structural witness of the reconcile_union loop body at `src/node/producer.cpp:347-350` (`for (auto& list : member_lists) for (auto& h : list) u.insert(h);`) — SET semantics dedupes, but each member's contribution can only ADD to the running set, never subtract |
| `INV_IntersectionAntiMonotonic` | INV-2: adding any list (including an EMPTY one) can only SHRINK the intersection. State-form: every hash in `block_inbound` appears in EVERY member's `view_inbound_list`. Structural witness of the reconcile_intersection iterative-shrink loop at `src/node/producer.cpp:362-369` (`std::set_intersection` produces `tmp ⊆ isect` on every iteration, and the early-exit at `isect.empty()` confirms the empty-set absorbing element) |
| `INV_OrderIndependent` | INV-3: ReconcileUnion(perm(L)) = ReconcileUnion(L) for every permutation P of the member ordering; same for ReconcileIntersection. The Q3 canonical-sort guarantee — producer's choice of member ordering does not change the canonical lists every validator re-derives. SET-based primitives over an indexed family are intrinsically domain-permutation-invariant (the SET of mapped values is unchanged); the C++ side's `std::set` insertion + `std::set_intersection` both produce sorted outputs regardless of input iteration order |
| `INV_UnionIdempotent` | INV-4: if every member commits the same list (as a SET), the canonical union equals that single member's SET. The duplicate-merge contract — three members all observing `{ev1, ev2}` produces `{ev1, ev2}` (not `{ev1, ev1, ev1, ev2, ev2, ev2}`). Structural witness of the `std::set<Hash>` container's idempotent insertion at producer.cpp:347 — `u.insert(h)` on an already-present element is a no-op |
| `INV_UnionCensorshipResistant` | INV-5: F2 censorship resistance (FA2 lift). If AT LEAST ONE member committed `h` in their view_eq_list, `h` must be in the F2 canonical equivocation set. The Q1 union-rule contract: a single honest observer is sufficient to land slashing evidence. Combined with FA6 equivocation-slashing soundness, gives the end-to-end "one honest committee member suffices to slash an equivocating offender" property. Structural witness: every `h` in any member's list flows through the producer.cpp:349 insertion into the merged set |
| `INV_IntersectionConservative` | INV-6: F2 conservative inbound — `h ∈ block_inbound` IFF EVERY member's list contains `h`. The Q1 intersection-rule biconditional: one bad relayer cannot unilaterally cause credit (⇒ direction), AND a unanimous observation guarantees inclusion (⇐ direction). Structural witness: the producer.cpp:357-372 iterative `std::set_intersection` reduces to the K-fold intersection, which by definition contains exactly the elements present in all K input sets |
| `INV_AllContribsValid` | V21..V24 reachability: every generated contrib passes the per-contrib well-formedness check. V21: each `view_X_list` length ≤ CAP = 64. V22..V24: each claimed root equals `ComputeViewRoot(view_X_list)`. The HonestContrib helper enforces V22..V24 by construction (each root field is computed from its paired list); the BoundedSeqs ceiling enforces V21. Matches the validator's per-contrib gate at `src/node/producer.cpp:391-436` (validate_contrib_view_roots) |
| `INV_BlockReconcilesContribs` | V25..V26 reachability: the block's canonical lists exactly match the F2 reconciliation of the K contribs. V25 (union over equivocation_events + abort_events) + V26 (intersection over inbound_receipts). The DeriveCanonical helper enforces this by construction; the GenerateHonest action sets `block_X' = canonical.X` after enumerating the per-member views. Matches the validator's composite gate at `src/node/producer.cpp:458-496` (validate_view_reconciliation) |
| `INV_BandwidthCapHonored` | F2-SPEC §Q3 bandwidth budget: every view-list ≤ F2_VIEW_LIST_CAP = 64. Holds by construction of `BoundedSeqs` (which is bounded above by `|Hashes|` ≤ CAP in the recommended .cfg). Matches the C++ guard at producer.cpp:407-417 (`if (msg.view_X_list.size() > F2_VIEW_LIST_CAP) return false;`) and the F2_VIEW_LIST_CAP constant at `include/determ/node/producer.hpp:212` |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other thirteen specs above). The recommended `F2ViewReconciliation.cfg` (K=3, Hashes={h1, h2, h3}, CAP=64) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The reconciliation primitives are pure functions; the algebraic invariants (INV-1..INV-6) hold structurally, so the GenerateHonest action's job is to enumerate every reachable per-member assignment over the bounded Hash universe and let TLC verify the invariants against each one. Variables modeled: `contribs` (function MemberIds → ContribMsg with three `[root, list]` field-pairs — matches the C++ `ContribMsg` extension at `include/determ/node/types.hpp` view_eq_root + view_eq_list etc.), `block_eq` / `block_abort` / `block_inbound` (SETs of Hashes — the spec-layer representation of the canonical lists; the C++ side's sorted-vector representation is bijective on sets), `generated` (BOOLEAN bit — TRUE once GenerateHonest fires, gates the post-enumeration invariants from spuriously firing at the empty-Init state). Actions modeled: `GenerateHonest` (single non-deterministic enumeration of K honest contribs + the F2-derived canonical block lists; produces ONLY V21..V26-passing tuples by construction), `Stutter` (post-generation no-op; TLC verifies the invariants persist at the reachable end-state).

The state-machine driver is intentionally minimal because the primitives under test are pure functions — the algebraic claims being verified hold over EVERY possible per-member assignment, not just the ones produced by a particular protocol trace. The enumeration covers every reachable `(eq_assign, ab_assign, inb_assign) ∈ [MemberIds → BoundedSeqs]³` tuple within the bounded Hash universe; for |Hashes|=3 and K=3, BoundedSeqs has 1 + 3 + 9 + 27 = 40 elements (sequences of length 0, 1, 2, 3 with replacement), giving 40^9 ≈ 2.6×10^14 raw assignments before TLC's symmetry-reduction. The SET-form invariants collapse this dramatically: any two assignments producing the same per-member SETs are equivalent for INV-1..INV-6, so the practical state-space TLC explores is at the level of distinct per-member SET-tuples — roughly 2^|Hashes| = 8 per slot, giving 8^9 ≈ 1.3×10^8 distinct equivalence classes. Even under the worst-case enumeration, the per-state INV-* check is constant-time over the K-member committee.

This spec captures the consensus-view soundness of the v2.7 F2 ship that closes the S-030 D2 footnote in `Safety.md` §5.3 and the open audit finding in `SECURITY.md` §S-030. Combined with the apply-layer S-033 + S-038 closure (the producer's `body.state_root` population per the S-038 wiring) and FA1's existing per-height safety machinery, F2 lifts FA1's conclusion from "≤ 1 digest per height + footnote" to "≤ 1 block instance per height" — the consensus + apply layers now jointly cover every consensus-bound field of the Block record. The reconciliation primitives are the structural witnesses of that lift: they are deterministic, order-independent, and idempotent over the K contributors' view commitments, so every honest validator re-derives the same canonical lists from the same K Phase-1 commits regardless of gossip arrival order.

Companion prose specification: `docs/proofs/F2-SPEC.md` (the design document; this TLA+ spec formalizes the §Q1 reconciliation rules + §Q3 bandwidth cap + §Q5 Phase-2 signature semantics at the state-machine layer). The FA1 safety proof (`docs/proofs/Safety.md` §5.3) will be updated to remove the D2 footnote once F2 ships; the prose update is tracked separately under the v2.7 ship workstream.

### FrostVerify.tla → FA-Crypto-Verify (FROST-Ed25519 verify soundness via Ed25519 delegation)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `key_pubs` (total function `Keys → GroupPubKeyT` with each pub a 32-element sequence over Bytes), `generated` (SUBSET of Keys — tracks which identifiers have been bound by `GenKeypair`), `signed_sigs` (SUBSET of `Keys × Messages × FrostSigT` — the canonical-aggregate set produced by `SignMessage`), `valid_pairs` (SUBSET of `GroupPubKeyT × Messages × FrostSigT` — the abstract `Ed25519Verify` acceptance relation populated only by honest signing per EUF-CMA A2), `tampered_sigs` (SUBSET of FrostSigT — byte-tampered variants), `verify_log` (Seq of records `[pub, msg, sig, result, case]` — the observable history of verify calls indexed by scenario tag), `scenario` (∈ {"init", "keygen", "signed", "verified"} — phase marker) |
| `INV_RoundTripSoundness` | INV-1: for any canonical aggregate signature produced by `SignMessage` over `msg` under `key_pubs[k]`, `FrostVerify(sig, key_pubs[k], msg)` returns TRUE. Models T-1 forward direction in `FrostVerifyDelegation.md` §3 (the analytic proof's L-1 + L-2 + delegation chain). State-form: every `verify_log` entry with `case = "canonical"` has `result = TRUE`. Structural witness of the runtime regression at `src/main.cpp` scenario 27 assertion 1 (`frost_verify: round-trip with real Ed25519 sig PASSES`) |
| `INV_TamperRejection` | INV-2: for any byte-tampered sig (`sig' ≠ canonical sig`), `FrostVerify(sig', pub, msg) = FALSE`. Models corollary T-1.1 (tampered-signature rejection) under the Ed25519 EUF-CMA assumption A2 (forging an Ed25519 sig under an honest key has probability ≤ 2⁻¹²⁸ per attempt; the spec abstracts that bound to determinism via `valid_pairs` membership). State-form: every `verify_log` entry with `case = "tampered_sig"` has `result = FALSE`. The `Tamper` action's universal-quantifier clause `\A k2 ∈ generated : \A m2 ∈ Messages : <<key_pubs[k2], m2, sig_prime>> \notin valid_pairs` makes the rejection structural. Structural witness of the runtime regression at scenario 27 assertion 2 (`frost_verify: tampered signature byte REJECTED`) |
| `INV_WrongKeyRejection` | INV-3: for any canonical aggregate produced under `group_pub_A`, verification against any distinct `group_pub_B` returns FALSE. Models corollary T-1.2 (wrong-key rejection) under Ed25519 EUF-CMA. State-form: every `verify_log` entry with `case = "wrong_key"` has `result = FALSE`. The `VerifyWrongKey` action filters `k_other` by `key_pubs[k_other] ≠ key_pubs[k]`; `valid_pairs` only contains `<<key_pubs[k], msg, sig>>` (not `<<key_pubs[k_other], msg, sig>>`), so the membership check returns FALSE by construction. Structural witness of the runtime regression at scenario 27 assertion 3 (`frost_verify: wrong group pubkey REJECTED`) |
| `INV_TamperedMsgRejection` | INV-4: for any canonical aggregate produced over `msg`, verification against any distinct `msg' ≠ msg` returns FALSE. Models corollary T-1.3 (tampered-message rejection) under Ed25519 EUF-CMA + SHA-512 collision resistance (the challenge `c = H2(R ‖ group_pubkey ‖ msg')` differs from `c(msg)` except in the negligible 2⁻²⁵⁶ collision case). State-form: every `verify_log` entry with `case = "tampered_msg"` has `result = FALSE`. The `VerifyTamperedMsg` action filters `msg_other` by `msg_other ≠ msg`; `valid_pairs` only contains the original-message triple, so the membership check returns FALSE by construction. Structural witness of the runtime regression at scenario 27 assertion 4 (`frost_verify: tampered message REJECTED`) |
| `INV_EmptyMsgWellDefined` | INV-5: the `FrostVerify` operator is total over `(FrostSigT × GroupPubKeyT × Messages)`, including the empty-message case (RFC 8032 §5.1 PureEdDSA explicitly supports zero-length input). The C++ implementation at `src/crypto/frost.cpp:117` passes `message.data(), message.size()` directly into `determ::crypto::verify` without an early-return on `message.empty()`; the spec-layer assertion is "every `verify_log` entry has `result ∈ BOOLEAN`" — well-typedness of the verify result regardless of `|msg|`. Guards against any future regression that would split the verify path on message length. Structural witness of the runtime regression at scenario 27 assertion 5 (`frost_verify: empty-message round-trip PASSES`) |
| `INV_TypeContract` | INV-6: the structural type contract pinned by the two `static_assert` clauses at `src/crypto/frost.cpp:108` (`sizeof(FrostSig) == sizeof(Signature)` — both 64 bytes, `R ‖ z`) and `:113` (`sizeof(Point) == sizeof(PubKey)` — both 32 bytes, Ed25519 compressed point). Every FrostSig in the model is a 64-element sequence over Bytes; every GroupPubKey is a 32-element sequence. RFC 9591 §6.6 + RFC 8032 §5.1.7 fix these encoded sizes; the static_asserts give compile-time evidence at the C++ layer; the TLA+ assertion is a sequence-length invariant on `signed_sigs[3]`, `tampered_sigs`, `key_pubs[k]`, and the `pub` / `sig` fields of every `verify_log` entry |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-one specs above). The recommended `FrostVerify.cfg` (Keys = {k1, k2}, Messages = {m1, m2}, Bytes = {b0, b1}) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 10 seconds on a single core. The five-action workflow (GenKeypair → SignMessage → Tamper → Verify{Canonical, Tampered, WrongKey, TamperedMsg}) enumerates every reachable combination of (signed-set × tampered-set × verify-call) up to the bounded universe; the four phase markers in `scenario` ({"init", "keygen", "signed", "verified"}) sequence the actions and bound the state space. Variables modeled: `key_pubs` (function `Keys → GroupPubKeyT` — the modeled pubkey value for each generated keypair identifier; `[k \in Keys |-> ZeroPubBytes]` at Init, overwritten by `GenKeypair`'s `EXCEPT` clause), `generated` (SUBSET of Keys — tracks which identifiers have been bound, distinct from `DOMAIN key_pubs` because the function is total at Init), `signed_sigs` (SUBSET of `Keys × Messages × FrostSigT` — the canonical-aggregate set), `valid_pairs` (SUBSET of `GroupPubKeyT × Messages × FrostSigT` — the abstract Ed25519Verify acceptance relation populated only by honest signing), `tampered_sigs` (SUBSET of FrostSigT — byte-tampered variants guaranteed disjoint from any canonical triple under any `(pub, msg)` combination), `verify_log` (Seq of records — the observable history; indexed by scenario tag so INV-1..INV-5 can be evaluated per-case), `scenario` (∈ {"init", "keygen", "signed", "verified"}). Actions modeled: `GenKeypair` (nondeterministically pick a fresh key identifier + a 32-byte pubkey value), `SignMessage` (atomically populate `signed_sigs ∪= {<<k, msg, sig>>}` and `valid_pairs ∪= {<<key_pubs[k], msg, sig>>}` — the joint extension captures RFC 9591 §3 Theorem 1's "aggregate is a structural Ed25519 sig" property), `Tamper` (extend `tampered_sigs` with a byte-tampered variant + universally assert non-membership in `valid_pairs`), `VerifyCanonical` / `VerifyTampered` / `VerifyWrongKey` / `VerifyTamperedMsg` (call `FrostVerify` and log the result under the appropriate scenario tag).

The state-machine driver is intentionally minimal because the property under test is the soundness of a pure-function delegation contract — `FrostVerify(sig, pub, msg) == Ed25519Verify(pub, msg, sig)` per the analytic proof's L-2 — and the algebraic claims (INV-1..INV-6) hold over every reachable `(signed_sigs, valid_pairs, tampered_sigs)` tuple. The `valid_pairs` set is the spec-layer abstraction of the Ed25519 EUF-CMA assumption A2 (Preliminaries §2.2): only honestly-signed `(pub, msg, sig)` triples are in the set, and any triple absent from it represents the "forgery fails" branch (concrete bound ≤ 2⁻¹²⁸ per attempt; the spec abstracts to determinism). The `Tamper` action's universal-quantifier clause is the structural enforcement of EUF-CMA at the state-machine layer: every byte-tampered sig is explicitly excluded from `valid_pairs` under every `(pub, msg)` combination, capturing the "no polynomial-time adversary can forge" assumption deterministically. The state-space TLC explores is at the level of the workflow trace through the four scenario phases × the bounded keypair / message / byte universes; the recommended config gives roughly `2 keys × 2 messages × 2^64 sigs × 2^32 pubs = 2^99` raw triples, but TLC's symmetry reduction + the canonical-set semantics collapses this to under 10³ distinct reachable workflow states.

This spec captures the verify-side soundness of the v2.10 Phase A `frost_verify` primitive — the first FROST-Ed25519 primitive shipped end-to-end (per `F2-V210-IMPLEMENTATION-PLAN.md` Phase A §123). The primitive is a thin delegation to `determ::crypto::verify` (the existing OpenSSL EVP_PKEY_ED25519 wrapper at `src/crypto/keys.cpp:79-91`); the soundness reduces to L-1 (RFC 9591 §3 Theorem 1: FROST aggregate is a structural Ed25519 sig) + L-2 (`determ::crypto::verify` wraps RFC 8032 §5.1.7 cofactored verify). Combined with the existing FA6 equivocation-slashing proof (which already depends on Ed25519 EUF-CMA over honest validator keys) and the upcoming FA-Crypto-DKG + FA-Crypto-Sign tracks (v2.10 Phases B + D), this spec gives the verify-side state-machine soundness that future v2.10 randomness-binding consumers (block-validation under `randomness_root`; FA3 selective-abort proof regression) can be drafted against.

**Out of scope** (consistent with `FrostVerifyDelegation.md` §5):
- DKG ceremony soundness (`v2.10-DKG-SPEC.md` + future FA-Crypto-DKG proof when Phase B ships).
- Threshold-signing protocol soundness (v2.10 Phase D — future FA-Crypto-Sign proof).
- Side-channel resistance of the underlying Ed25519 implementation (OpenSSL's constant-time guarantee is per their documentation; not modeled at the TLA+ layer).
- Byte-level enumeration of the Ed25519 verify equation (`[8 · z] · G == [8] · R + [8 · c] · group_pubkey`) — the spec models `Ed25519Verify` as an abstract acceptance relation, not as the elliptic-curve arithmetic. The FA-Crypto-Verify analytic proof (`FrostVerifyDelegation.md`) cites the RFC 9591 / RFC 8032 algebraic argument; the FB-track here checks the state-machine consistency of the delegation abstraction.

Companion analytic proof: `docs/proofs/FrostVerifyDelegation.md` (the FA-Crypto-Verify proof shipped in Round 18 deliverable; T-1 + L-1 + L-2 + corollaries T-1.1 / T-1.2 / T-1.3). This TLA+ spec formalizes the state-machine layer of that proof's adversary model (§5): tampered-signature, wrong-public-key, and tampered-message surfaces are each closed by `valid_pairs` non-membership; round-trip soundness is closed by `SignMessage`'s joint extension of `signed_sigs` and `valid_pairs`; the empty-message corollary is closed by `INV_EmptyMsgWellDefined`'s well-typedness assertion; the structural-type corollary (the two `static_assert` clauses) is closed by `INV_TypeContract`'s sequence-length predicates.

### MakeContribCommitment.tla → FA-Crypto-MakeContrib (v1-byte-identity + DTM-F2-v1 replay defense)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `record` (total function `InputTuple → OutputRange` where OutputRange is `{SENTINEL} ∪ {V1Commit(...)} ∪ {F2Commit(...)}`), `generated` (SUBSET of InputTuple — tracks which input tuples have been enumerated by the `Generate` action) |
| `INV_V1ByteIdentity` | INV-1: for every generated `(idx, prev, txs, dh, ZERO, ZERO, ZERO)` tuple, `record[t] = V1Commit(t.idx, t.prev, t.txs, t.dh)`. Lifts T-1 (v1 byte-identity) of `MakeContribCommitmentBackwardCompat.md` §1. The C++ short-circuit at `src/node/producer.cpp:242-258` (the `if (any_view)` body is skipped when `is_zero_hash(view_eq_root) && is_zero_hash(view_abort_root) && is_zero_hash(view_inbound_root)`) is the structural witness; the spec layer captures this as `MakeCommit` reducing to `V1Commit` when `AllViewsZero` holds. Runtime regression: `src/main.cpp` assertion `make_contrib_commitment: all-zero views == v1 short-circuit` (line 9608) |
| `INV_F2PathTriggered` | INV-2: when at least one view root is non-zero, `MakeCommit` evaluates to `F2Commit(...)` and is distinct from `V1Commit(...)` on the same `(idx, prev, txs, dh)` prefix. Lifts T-2 forward direction. The C++ `if (any_view)` branch at producer.cpp:249-258 appends the `"DTM-F2-v1"` literal plus the three view roots; the spec layer captures the disjoint-pre-image-families argument via the `"V1"` vs `"F2"` discriminator tag in the output tuple. The cryptographic underpinning is L-3 of the companion proof (length argument: 104 vs 209 bytes ⇒ distinct SHA-256 inputs ⇒ distinct outputs under A2) |
| `INV_PerRootBinding` | INV-3: each individual non-zero view root in any single position (eq only, abort only, or inbound only) produces a distinct `MakeCommit` output. The three slots are bound at distinct field positions in the SHA-256 input, so a non-zero value in one slot cannot collide with the same non-zero value in another slot. Per-root domain separation. Structural witness: the F2 branch at producer.cpp:255-257 appends each root in fixed order (`view_eq_root` first, then `view_abort_root`, then `view_inbound_root`); the position of the non-zero byte run differs across the three single-non-zero shapes. Runtime regressions: `make_contrib_commitment: {eq,abort,inbound}_root binds the hash` + `make_contrib_commitment: each root contributes independently` (src/main.cpp:9626-9633) |
| `INV_DomainSeparation` | INV-4: no v1-shape pre-image equals any F2-shape pre-image. Lifts T-2 + L-3 — the `"DTM-F2-v1"` literal at the start of the F2 extension makes the two families syntactically disjoint. State-form: for every pair of generated input tuples `(t1, t2)` where `t1` has all-zero views (= v1 family) and `t2` has any non-zero view (= F2 family), `record[t1] ≠ record[t2]`. The spec-layer abstraction is the `"V1"` vs `"F2"` discriminator distinctness; the C++ side's structural witness is the length difference (104 vs 209 bytes) + the literal-tag defense-in-depth |
| `INV_Determinism` | INV-5: `MakeCommit` applied twice to the same input tuple yields the same output. Captures L-2 of the companion proof (SHA256Builder is deterministic via OpenSSL's `EVP_DigestUpdate` byte-stream determinism at `src/crypto/sha256.cpp:25-28`). State-form: `record[t] = MakeCommit(t.idx, t.prev, t.txs, t.dh, t.eq, t.ab, t.inb)` for every generated `t`. The pure-function property holds by definitional substitution at the spec layer; TLC verifies the invariant against every reachable enumeration |
| `INV_FieldBinding` | INV-6: every consensus-bound v1-prefix field (idx, prev, txs, dh) binds the hash — the output changes if that field changes. Captures the field-binding contract that the analytic proof's L-2 establishes via SHA-256 collision resistance (content-bound). State-form: for each generated `t` and each candidate replacement value `idx2 / prev2 / txs2 / dh2 ≠ t.idx / t.prev / t.txs / t.dh`, `MakeCommit(replacement, ...) ≠ record[t]`. The three view-root slots are not retested here because INV-3 (PerRootBinding) covers them more tightly. The cryptographic underpinning is A2 + L-2; the spec layer captures it via the InnerRoot + V1Commit + F2Commit operators embedding every field directly into the output tuple |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-two specs above). The recommended `MakeContribCommitment.cfg` (BlockIdx = {i1, i2}, Hashes = {ZERO, h1, h2}, TxLists = {nil, t1, t2}, MaxTxs = 2) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The state-machine driver is intentionally minimal because the function under test is pure — every algebraic invariant (INV-1..INV-6) holds over every reachable input tuple, not just the ones produced by a particular protocol trace. The single non-deterministic `Generate` action picks an input tuple, computes `MakeCommit(t.*)`, stores the result in a `record` map keyed by the tuple, and TLC verifies the invariants hold against the accumulated map at every reachable state. Variables modeled: `record` (total function `InputTuple → OutputRange` — the accumulated output map; at Init every key maps to a sentinel `<<"unset">>` 1-tuple, every `Generate` step overwrites one key with a real `V1Commit` or `F2Commit` tuple), `generated` (SUBSET of InputTuple — the set of keys that have been assigned a real value; used to gate the invariants from spuriously firing at Init). Actions modeled: `Generate` (non-deterministically pick an unenumerated input tuple + record the MakeCommit value), `Saturate` (post-enumeration stutter when every tuple has been seen).

The SHA-256 abstraction. The C++ `SHA256Builder` at `src/crypto/sha256.cpp:25-28` forwards every `append(...)` call to OpenSSL's `EVP_DigestUpdate`, which per FIPS 180-4 §6.1.2 incorporates each byte into the message schedule in the order received; identical append-sequences produce identical outputs, byte-distinct sequences produce distinct outputs except with probability ≤ 2⁻¹²⁸ per attempt (the A2 / Preliminaries §2.1 collision-resistance assumption + the L-4 cumulative bound). The spec-layer abstraction lifts this to determinism on the bounded pre-image universe: `V1Commit` and `F2Commit` are pure TLA+ operators that return structurally distinct tuples for structurally distinct pre-images, and identical tuples for identical pre-images. This is the same "abstract hash = pre-image identity" pattern that `Consensus.tla` uses for `Digest`, `Snapshot.tla` uses for `state_root`, and `FrostVerify.tla` uses for `valid_pairs`. The `"V1"` vs `"F2"` discriminator tags in the output tuples capture the disjoint-pre-image-families contract (L-3 of the companion proof: 104-byte v1 pre-image vs 209-byte F2 pre-image ⇒ distinct lengths ⇒ distinct SHA-256 inputs).

This spec captures the commit-side of the v2.7 F2 wire change: the `make_contrib_commitment` primitive at `src/node/producer.cpp:219-260` extends the pre-F2 (v1) commit shape with three view roots under a `"DTM-F2-v1"` domain tag. Two paired properties are pinned: (T-1) v1 backward compatibility — a call with all three view roots equal to `Hash{}` (= the 32-zero `ZERO` element in the spec) produces a hash byte-identical to the pre-F2 implementation, so pre-F2 ContribMsg signatures continue to verify under the extended primitive without protocol-version negotiation; (T-2) DTM-F2-v1 replay defense — a signature produced under one commit shape cannot be replayed under the other shape except with cryptographically negligible probability under A2. The runtime regressions at `src/main.cpp` (cited in §7 of `MakeContribCommitmentBackwardCompat.md`) cover the bidirectional cross-shape verification matrix that an external implementer needs to reproduce: T-1.1 (v1 sig valid under v2 verifier when all-zero views), T-2.1 (F2 sig invalid under v1 verifier shape).

Combined with the apply-layer S-033 + S-038 closure (the producer's `body.state_root` population per the S-038 wiring) and FB22 `F2ViewReconciliation.tla` (the validator-side reconciliation primitives that consume the view roots this commit binds), the consensus-layer half of S-030 D2 closure is now end-to-end at both the FA-track (analytic) and FB-track (state-machine) layers. The downstream signature-side claims T-1.1 and T-2.1 are downstream compositions of this spec's INV-1 / INV-2 / INV-4 + `FrostVerify.tla`'s INV-RoundTripSoundness / INV-TamperedMsgRejection under A1 (Ed25519 EUF-CMA); the spec layer establishes the commit-side distinctness algebraically and the cryptographic-soundness analytic proof in `MakeContribCommitmentBackwardCompat.md` §4 + §5 gives the sig-side closure.

**Out of scope** (consistent with `MakeContribCommitmentBackwardCompat.md` §6):
- Byte-level enumeration of the SHA-256 compression function. A2 abstracts the cryptographic content into "distinct pre-images map to distinct hashes"; the spec layer models that abstraction via the `"V1"` vs `"F2"` discriminator tags.
- Side-channel resistance of the underlying SHA-256 implementation (OpenSSL's constant-time guarantee is per their documentation; not modeled at the TLA+ layer).
- The Ed25519 sig-side reduction in T-1.1 / T-2.1 (signature compatibility / non-replayability corollaries). Those depend on Ed25519 EUF-CMA and are `FrostVerify.tla` (FB23) / FA-Crypto-Verify territory. This spec covers only the commit-binding state machine; the sig-side reduction is a downstream composition of this spec + `FrostVerify.tla` under A1.
- The validator-side reconciliation that consumes the view roots this primitive binds. That is `F2ViewReconciliation.tla` (FB22) / F2-SPEC.md §Q1 territory.

Companion analytic proof: `docs/proofs/MakeContribCommitmentBackwardCompat.md` (the FA-Crypto-MakeContrib proof shipped in Round 18 deliverable; T-1 + T-2 + L-1..L-4 + corollaries T-1.1 / T-2.1). This TLA+ spec formalizes the state-machine layer of that proof: INV-1 lifts T-1 (the all-zero-views short-circuit identity at producer.cpp:242-258); INV-2 + INV-3 + INV-4 lift T-2 (the disjoint-pre-image families argument via L-3's length-distinguishing property); INV-5 lifts L-2 (SHA256Builder determinism); INV-6 lifts the field-binding content-bound contract from L-2. The T-1.1 and T-2.1 corollaries are downstream compositions with FB23 `FrostVerify.tla` under A1 (Ed25519 EUF-CMA).

### RateLimiterEviction.tla → FA-RateLimiter F-1 closure (idle-bucket eviction in `net::RateLimiter`)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `buckets` (function `ActiveKeys → [tokens, last_touch]`), `next_sweep_at` (Nat), `now` (`0..MaxTimeSteps`), `evicted_count` (Nat), `was_evicted` (SUBSET Keys) |
| `INV_BucketLifetimeBounded` | INV-1 / T-1: every active bucket has been touched within the last `EvictionThreshold + SweepInterval` time units. Captures point 6 of the F-1 "Closure (shipped)" subsection in `S014RateLimiterSoundness.md` §6.2 (the memory bound: a bucket survives at most `eviction_threshold_sec_ + sweep_interval_sec_` seconds without being touched). Structural witness: the C++ amortized-sweep branch at `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:95-103` fires at most every `sweep_interval_sec_` seconds, and the eviction predicate at line 135 (`now - it->second.last > threshold`) catches every bucket past its individual threshold at the cadence boundary. Fires only when `EvictionThreshold > 0` (disabled-eviction mode is covered by INV-5) |
| `INV_EvictionMonotone` | INV-2 / T-3: `evicted_count` never decreases across any step. Captures audit-trail soundness — operators can read `evicted_count` over time and observe a monotone counter. Structural witness: `SweepIdle` and the amortized-sweep branch of `Consume` only ADD to `evicted_count` (by `Cardinality(StaleKeys) >= 0`); no action decrements it. State-form: `evicted_count \in Nat` (Nat-typed; documents the contract). The action-level monotonicity is captured by the absence of any action that decrements |
| `INV_ResurrectionSafe` | INV-3 / T-2: if a key was evicted (k ∈ `was_evicted`) and is currently in `buckets` (k ∈ `ActiveKeys`), the bucket starts at FULL capacity. Captures point 4 of the F-1 closure ("semantic safety: an evicted bucket re-creates as full-capacity on next touch"). Structural witness: the C++ first-touch branch at `rate_limiter.hpp:106-108` sets `b.tokens = burst_` when `b.last.time_since_epoch().count() == 0` (the just-inserted default-constructed Bucket). Observationally indistinguishable from the un-evicted bucket having refilled — the default `eviction_threshold_sec_ = 600s` gives at least 60× safety factor over realistic refill times (`burst_/rate_per_sec_` ~= 10s with default config) |
| `INV_SweepIdempotent` | INV-4 / T-4: SweepIdle applied twice with no intervening time advance and no Consume yields the same `buckets` the second time. Captures the erase-or-skip loop body at `rate_limiter.hpp:134-141` (`if (now - it->second.last > threshold) { erase; ++evicted; } else { ++it; }` — each entry is decided independently, so a re-sweep finds no fresh deletions). State-form: after any sweep firing (forced or amortized), any key whose `last_touch` predates the most recent sweep window must have been re-touched after — captured via the bound `(next_sweep_at > SweepInterval ∧ buckets[k].last_touch < next_sweep_at - SweepInterval) ⇒ (now - buckets[k].last_touch <= EvictionThreshold)`. Fires only when `EvictionThreshold > 0` |
| `INV_ConfigureEvictionZeroDisables` | INV-5 / T-5: when `EvictionThreshold = 0`, no key is ever evicted. Captures the legacy unbounded-growth behavior pinned as a config option per `rate_limiter.hpp:56` (`configure_eviction(double threshold_sec, double interval_sec = 60.0)` — passing `threshold_sec <= 0` DISABLES eviction entirely) and the disabled-eviction short-circuit at `rate_limiter.hpp:129` (`if (eviction_threshold_sec_ <= 0.0) return 0;` in `sweep_idle_locked`). Structural witness: `SweepIdle`'s IF-branch at the spec layer short-circuits when `EvictionThreshold = 0`, leaving `buckets`, `evicted_count`, and `was_evicted` UNCHANGED. State-form: `evicted_count = 0 ∧ was_evicted = {}` whenever `EvictionThreshold = 0` |
| `INV_AmortizedSweepLowerBoundsResidual` | INV-6 / T-6: at any time t, the number of stale keys still resident in `buckets` is bounded by the cadence-fresh count. Captures the amortization argument — a key past `EvictionThreshold` idle seconds was either (a) caught by the most recent sweep (so it's not in `buckets`) or (b) only just became stale in the current `SweepInterval` window. Structural witness: the amortized-sweep cadence at `rate_limiter.hpp:99-101` (`next_sweep_at_ = now + sweep_interval_sec_;`) ensures the next sweep fires no later than `SweepInterval` seconds after the previous one. State-form: for every stale key k, `now - buckets[k].last_touch <= EvictionThreshold + SweepInterval`. Fires only when `EvictionThreshold > 0` |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-three specs above). The recommended `RateLimiterEviction.cfg` (Keys = {k1, k2, k3}, MaxTimeSteps = 10, EvictionThreshold = 3, SweepInterval = 2, MaxTimeStep = 2) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The three-action state machine (Consume, AdvanceTime, ForcedSweep) exercises every reachable interleaving of bucket-touch, clock-advance, and operator-triggered eviction within the bounded universe. Variables modeled: `buckets` (function `ActiveKeys → Bucket` where Bucket = `[tokens: {FULL, EMPTY}, last_touch: Nat]` — matches the C++ `std::map<std::string, Bucket> buckets_` at rate_limiter.hpp:151 with the token level collapsed to FULL/EMPTY since the F-1 invariants depend on `last_touch` not on the precise integer-fractional token amount), `next_sweep_at` (Nat — the time the next amortized sweep fires; matches `std::chrono::steady_clock::time_point next_sweep_at_` at rate_limiter.hpp:149), `now` (Nat — the abstract monotonic clock matching `std::chrono::steady_clock::now()` at rate_limiter.hpp:89; the RFC-mandated monotonicity is enforced by the AdvanceTime action's `now' = now + delta` with `delta >= 1`), `evicted_count` (Nat — spec-only cumulative counter; the C++ side returns per-call evicted counts from `sweep_idle_locked` but doesn't maintain a cumulative counter, so the spec lifts them to a cumulative for INV-2 monotonicity), `was_evicted` (SUBSET Keys — spec-only audit set of keys evicted at least once; lets INV-3 observe resurrection across the trace, where the C++ side has no equivalent set because eviction is destructive on `buckets_`). Actions modeled: `Consume(k)` (touch key k; if `now >= next_sweep_at` run the amortized sweep first then bucket-touch — mirrors the C++ flow at lines 95-117 with the sweep-before-touch ordering), `AdvanceTime` (monotonic clock advance bounded by MaxTimeStep per step to keep the state space tractable), `ForcedSweep` (external `sweep_idle()` call from the public API at rate_limiter.hpp:79-82 — no-op when eviction is disabled), `SaturateClock` (stutter at the time horizon).

The state-machine driver exercises the F-1 mitigation's hot path (Consume's sweep-before-touch branching) and the two operator-facing surfaces (`configure_eviction` parameterized via spec constants + `sweep_idle` exposed as `ForcedSweep`). The token level is abstracted to FULL/EMPTY because the F-1 invariants (lifetime-bound, resurrection-safety, sweep-idempotence, configure-zero-disables, amortization) depend only on `last_touch`, not on the precise refill arithmetic — L-1 of `S014RateLimiterSoundness.md` already gives `tokens ∈ [0, C]` orthogonally. The clock is modeled as Nat-typed monotonic time units rather than the C++ `std::chrono::steady_clock::duration` because the bound arithmetic (`now - last_touch <= EvictionThreshold + SweepInterval`) is the same up to unit conversion; L-5 of the prose proof gives the C++ side's monotonicity, the spec layer enforces it via the AdvanceTime action's `delta >= 1` clause.

This spec captures the just-shipped F-1 mitigation that closes the long-standing unbounded-`buckets_`-growth finding in `S014RateLimiterSoundness.md` §6.2. Pre-F-1 the `std::map<std::string, Bucket> buckets_` grew monotonically: every distinct key ever consumed created an entry, with no path to remove entries. An attacker with access to many distinct source IPs (e.g., IPv6 /64 — `2^64` addresses per residential prefix, or /48 — `2^80` addresses in others) could grow `buckets_` arbitrarily by sending one consume-triggering request per unique IP, at ~64 bytes per entry — 100M unique requests would reach ~6.4 GB RAM. The F-1 closure adds time-decay eviction: every `consume()` opportunistically checks if `now >= next_sweep_at_`; if so, walks the map and erases entries whose `b.last` is older than `eviction_threshold_sec_`. Cost: O(N) per prune trigger, amortized O(1) per consume. The default config (`eviction_threshold_sec_ = 600`, `sweep_interval_sec_ = 60`) bounds `buckets_.size()` to the per-bucket worst-case lifetime — a bucket survives at most `600 + 60 = 660` seconds without being touched.

**Out of scope** (consistent with `S014RateLimiterSoundness.md` §6.2):
- The pre-F-1 soundness theorems T-1 (bounded burst), T-2 (no DoS amplification), T-3 (per-IP independence), T-4 (HELLO-exemption safety), T-5 (refill monotonicity), T-6 (capacity-vs-rate trade-off). All remain valid under the F-1 mitigation because the eviction policy operates on `last_touch` only, leaving the token-bucket refill arithmetic at rate_limiter.hpp:109-113 untouched. The prose proof's §6 covers these theorems in detail.
- Concurrent-mutex correctness. The C++ side serializes via `std::mutex mu_` at rate_limiter.hpp:150; the spec uses TLA+ atomic actions to model the serialized window. The Preliminaries.md §3 network model assumption (asio thread-pool concurrency) is what makes the mutex sufficient at the C++ layer; the FA-track prose proof covers the mutex argument.
- Per-second-precision floating-point arithmetic. The C++ `elapsed * rate_per_sec` calculation at line 111 is modeled at the spec layer as a FULL/EMPTY transition because the F-1 invariants depend on `last_touch`, not on the precise integer-fractional token amount. L-1 of the prose proof gives the `[0, C]` interval bound for token levels.
- HELLO-exemption gate at `src/net/gossip.cpp:148`. That is FA-track T-4 territory (the HELLO size + idempotence + connection-rate-throttle bound); orthogonal to the F-1 eviction mitigation.
- Per-method weighting on RPC. Finding F-3 of the prose proof's §6.2 acknowledged as Option 1b deferred to a follow-on (per-method token-multiplier table; ~50 LOC + 1 day of weight tuning + a regression test).

Companion analytic proof: `docs/proofs/S014RateLimiterSoundness.md` (the FA-RateLimiter proof; T-1 + T-2 + T-3 + T-4 + T-5 + T-6 + L-1..L-7). This TLA+ spec formalizes the state-machine layer of that proof's §6.2 "Closure (shipped)" F-1 mitigation subsection: INV-1 lifts the §6.2 point-6 memory bound (a bucket survives at most `eviction_threshold + sweep_interval` seconds); INV-2 captures the audit-trail soundness of the cumulative `evicted_count`; INV-3 lifts §6.2 point-4 (semantic safety — evicted bucket re-creates as full-capacity, observationally indistinguishable from the un-evicted bucket having refilled); INV-4 captures the erase-or-skip loop body's idempotence at rate_limiter.hpp:134-141; INV-5 lifts the configure-zero-disables config option at rate_limiter.hpp:56 + 129; INV-6 captures the amortization argument (the cadence bounds residual stale-key count). The pre-F-1 theorems T-1..T-6 remain valid under the F-1 mitigation and are out of scope here — the prose proof's §1 + §4 + §5 cover them.

### BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla → FA-StateIntegrity (S-021 + S-033 + S-038 + apply-time gate composition)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `chains` (Nodes → Seq(Block) where Block = [index, prev_hash, state_root, txs]), `local_state` (Nodes → [height, txs: SUBSET TxUniverse]), `chain_at_rest` (Nodes → SerializedChain ∪ {NoSerialization}), `pending_inbox` (Nodes → Seq(Block)), `apply_throws` / `load_throws` (Nodes → BOOLEAN), `tampered_at` (Nodes → 0..MaxHeight ∪ {"none"}) |
| `INV_LoadDetectsTampering` | T-1: if `chain_at_rest[n]` has been tampered (`tampered_at[n] /= "none"`), the wrapped chain blob fails one of two integrity checks — either `validate_chain` returns FALSE (case (a): interior-block tamper, caught by the `prev_hash` chain consistency at `src/chain/chain.cpp:54-58`) OR `head_hash` recompute differs from `cr.head_hash` (case (b): head-block tamper, caught by the wrap check at `src/chain/chain.cpp:2046-2050`). Case (c) "adversary forges committee signatures to mask the tamper" reduces to A1 (Ed25519 EUF-CMA per Preliminaries §2.2) and is FA-track territory (out of scope for the state-machine layer; cf. FrostVerify.tla / FB23 for the abstract EUF-CMA model) |
| `INV_ApplyGateFiresOnMismatch` | T-2: across every reachable state, every block in `chains[n]` has either `state_root = ZeroRoot` (pre-S-038 backward-compat zero-skip — `WireFormatBackwardCompat.md` T-1) OR `state_root = state_root_of(head_state(prefix))` where `prefix` is the chain up to that block. The standing-invariant form of "the S-033 gate at chain.cpp:1432-1444 always fires on divergent blocks before they reach `blocks_.push_back`" — a divergent block would violate the disjunction but the gate's throw prevents installation. The DivergentTxPropose adversarial action exercises the gate-firing path by depositing a block with a fabricated `state_root` into `pending_inbox`; the next `ApplyBlockOnReceive` latches `apply_throws[n] = TRUE` and refuses to advance |
| `INV_SelfApplyConsistent` | T-3: across every reachable state, every block in `chains[n]` produced by node n (i.e., installed via `ProduceBlock(n)`) has `state_root` in `{ZeroRoot, state_root_of(head_state(prefix))}`. The structural witness that the producer's tentative-chain dry-run pattern at `src/node/node.cpp:1024-1117` guarantees gate-pass on self-apply: the tentative chain's `compute_state_root()` equals the live chain's `compute_state_root()` after the same body is applied to both, by FA-Apply-1 (AccountState.tla / FB5). Self-apply NEVER triggers the gate's loud-fail path because the producer feeds the gate with a value it itself computed via the same deterministic operator |
| `INV_CrossNodeConsistency` | T-4: for any two honest nodes n1, n2, if `chains[n1] = chains[n2]` (byte-identical chain sequences), then `state_root_of(local_state[n1]) = state_root_of(local_state[n2])`. The FA-Apply-1 byproduct lifted to the spec layer: equal block sequences applied from equal starting states reach byte-identical post-apply states by apply determinism. The non-trivial coverage point is the antecedent — when chains differ (e.g., one node has applied a fork the other hasn't), the invariant degenerates to vacuous; the fork-choice layer (FA1 / S-029) handles fork pruning in production. This spec asserts the cleaner FA-Apply-1 consequence: equal prefixes ⇒ equal roots |
| `INV_NoSilentDivergence` | T-5: the headline composition claim. If two honest nodes n1, n2 have `local_state[n1].height = local_state[n2].height` AND `state_root_of(local_state[n1]) /= state_root_of(local_state[n2])` (i.e., the same height with different state_roots — a divergence), then at least one of `apply_throws[n1]`, `apply_throws[n2]`, `load_throws[n1]`, `load_throws[n2]` is TRUE. The structural witness that every state divergence is loud-failed at the appropriate boundary — either at receive (apply_throws via T-2) or at load (load_throws via T-1). The composition is total over the state-integrity surface: there is no reachable state where two honest nodes silently diverge |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-three specs above). The recommended `BlockchainStateIntegrity.cfg` (Nodes = {n1, n2, n3}, MaxHeight = 3, TxUniverse = {t1, t2}) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under a minute on a single core. The six-action state machine (ProduceBlock, ApplyBlockOnReceive, SerializeChain, LoadChain, TamperAtRest, DivergentTxPropose) exercises every reachable interleaving of producer-side state_root population, receiver-side gate firing, at-rest serialize/load round-trips, and the two adversary surfaces (disk-level tamper + Byzantine producer). Variables modeled: `chains` (function `NodeId → Seq(Block)` where Block has [index, prev_hash, state_root, txs] — matches the C++ `std::vector<Block> blocks_` at `include/determ/chain/chain.hpp` with the per-block field structure collapsed to the four state-integrity-relevant fields), `local_state` (function `NodeId → [height, txs: SUBSET TxUniverse]` — the canonical state projection abstracted to (height, accumulated_tx_set) per FA-Apply-1's apply-determinism contract), `chain_at_rest` (function `NodeId → SerializedChain ∪ {NoSerialization}` where SerializedChain has [head_hash, blocks] — matches the S-021 wrapped JSON form `{head_hash, blocks}` at chain.cpp:1944-1985), `pending_inbox` (function `NodeId → Seq(Block)` — the gossip-ratified inbound queue; abstracts the wire-level V1..V20 admission gates), `apply_throws` / `load_throws` (function `NodeId → BOOLEAN` — latching sentinels for "an integrity gate has fired at this node"; lifts the C++ exception propagation into observable state-machine markers), `tampered_at` (function `NodeId → 0..MaxHeight ∪ {"none"}` — spec-only audit field tracking the height-index of the most recent TamperAtRest mutation; lets INV_LoadDetectsTampering observe the post-tamper state). Actions modeled: `ProduceBlock(n)` (the C++ Node::try_finalize_round at node.cpp:1024-1117 — six steps collapsed into a single atomic action: build_body, tentative-chain dry-run for state_root computation, populate body.state_root, apply on live chain, broadcast to other nodes' inboxes), `ApplyBlockOnReceive(n)` (the receiver-side path — drains head of pending_inbox; on prev_hash continuity + state_root match advances the chain, on mismatch latches apply_throws and refuses to advance per the A9 atomic-apply rollback), `SerializeChain(n)` (Chain::save at chain.cpp:1944-1985 — writes the wrapped JSON blob; resets tampered_at to "none"), `LoadChain(n)` (Chain::load at chain.cpp:1987-2054 — replays the blob with prev_hash continuity + head_hash recompute; on mismatch latches load_throws), `TamperAtRest(n)` (the disk-level adversary surface — mutates one block's txs field at an arbitrary target_height; the wrap header's stored head_hash is NOT patched, so the next LoadChain MUST detect either via interior prev_hash mismatch or via head head_hash mismatch), `DivergentTxPropose(n, dest)` (the Byzantine-producer adversary — node n deposits a block with a fabricated state_root into dest's inbox; the next ApplyBlockOnReceive MUST latch apply_throws on the gate's mismatch fire).

This spec captures the just-shipped composition theorem of `docs/proofs/BlockchainStateIntegrity.md` at the state-machine layer. The analytic proof (T-1..T-5) establishes that four independently-shipped mechanisms (S-021 chain.json wrap, S-033 state_root Merkle commitment, S-038 producer-side population, the apply-time gate at chain.cpp:1421-1446) together exhaust the state-mutation surface across three operational boundaries (at-rest / produce / receive). The TLA+ state-machine layer abstracts these into six actions + five invariants:

1. **Surface decomposition** is captured by the action set — ProduceBlock covers the producer boundary, ApplyBlockOnReceive covers the receiver boundary, SerializeChain + LoadChain cover the at-rest boundary, TamperAtRest + DivergentTxPropose are the two adversary surfaces.
2. **The five theorem statements** are each lifted to a standing invariant — T-1 → INV_LoadDetectsTampering (disjunction over case (a) interior tamper and case (b) head tamper; case (c) forge-sigs is A1 / FA-track), T-2 → INV_ApplyGateFiresOnMismatch (every installed block satisfies state_root = computed root by construction), T-3 → INV_SelfApplyConsistent (every self-produced block has the tentative-dry-run-computed state_root), T-4 → INV_CrossNodeConsistency (FA-Apply-1 lifted), T-5 → INV_NoSilentDivergence (the composition's end-state property).
3. **The composition is total over the state-integrity surface** — the spec's TLC enumeration of every reachable interleaving witnesses that every divergent block introduction (via DivergentTxPropose) is loud-failed at receive (apply_throws latches before chain advances), and every divergent chain at rest (via TamperAtRest) is loud-failed at load (load_throws latches before chains[n] is installed). No silent divergence is reachable under the bounded model; the proof's structural argument (four mechanisms × four surfaces = total coverage) is the unbounded counterpart.

The abstract-hash model (compute_hash and state_root_of as pure functions returning tagged tuples) is the standard TLA+ projection of A2 (SHA-256 collision resistance) — distinct pre-images map to distinct outputs by tuple inequality. The cryptographic tightness is FA-track territory (Preliminaries.md §2.1); the FB-track here checks the state-machine consistency of the surface composition under the abstract-hash discipline.

**Out of scope** (consistent with `BlockchainStateIntegrity.md` §6):
- Pre-S-038 historical blocks bypass T-2 (intentional backward-compat). The spec captures this via the `b.state_root = ZeroRoot` disjunct in INV_ApplyGateFiresOnMismatch and INV_SelfApplyConsistent. Post-S-038 every produced block has non-zero state_root (modeled by ProduceBlock's step-4 population at `body.state_root = state_root_of(post_state)`).
- Out-of-namespace state divergence (any future state field NOT threaded into `Chain::compute_state_root` would land outside the commitment). The spec models compute_state_root as a pure function of (height, txs) which is fully covered; the namespace-coverage lock-in is `tools/test_state_root_namespaces.sh` (12 assertions).
- Consensus-layer divergence prevention (S-030 D2 closure). That is FB22 `F2ViewReconciliation.tla` / `F2-SPEC.md` territory — the apply-time gate is the receiver-side safety net, but the producer-side reconciliation that prevents divergent blocks from being assembled in the first place is the parallel mechanism.
- Snapshot pathway (covered by FA-Apply-2 / FB6 `Snapshot.tla`). The snapshot tail-head's stored `state_root` is checked against the freshly-restored `compute_state_root()` at chain.cpp:1778-1783; that surface is the parallel composition this spec doesn't model.
- Non-Byzantine bugs in `compute_state_root` itself. T-2 assumes `compute_state_root()` correctly hashes the actual `Chain` state. A bug that omits a state field from `build_state_leaves` would leave that field out of the commitment; T-2 would fail to detect divergence in it. The namespace-coverage regressions (§7 of the prose proof) are the mitigation.
- The Ed25519 EUF-CMA / SHA-256 collision resistance bounds — the spec lifts these to deterministic predicates ("distinct pre-images map to distinct hashes") via the abstract-hash model; the cryptographic tightness is FA-track territory.

Companion analytic proof: `docs/proofs/BlockchainStateIntegrity.md` (the composition theorem shipped Round 21; T-1 + T-2 + T-3 + T-4 + T-5 with the per-surface adversary model in §5 and the test-suite citation table in §7). This TLA+ spec formalizes the state-machine layer of that proof: the six actions cover the producer / receiver / at-rest / adversary surfaces enumerated in §5; the five invariants cover the five theorems in §1; the composition's structural totality (four mechanisms × four surfaces) is witnessed by TLC's enumeration of every reachable schedule under the bounded universe.

Cross-reference triangle. FB5 `AccountState.tla` (FA-Apply-1 — apply determinism, the load-bearing input to T-3 + T-4 of this spec). FB6 `Snapshot.tla` (FA-Apply-2 — the snapshot-pathway sibling surface; the S-021 wrap check has a parallel head_hash recompute at `restore_from_snapshot`). FB26 (this spec — the load / apply / produce surface composition). Together, the three specs cover the full state-integrity surface at the state-machine layer.

### JsonValidation.tla → FA-S018 (S-018 clear-diagnostic + defense-in-depth state machine)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `input_objects` (function Surfaces → SUBSET JsonObjects), `validation_log` (Seq of LogEntry where LogEntry has [surface, field_name, outcome, has_diagnostic]), `fired_surfaces` (SUBSET Surfaces); `Len(validation_log) <= MaxValidations` enforces the bounded-work cap |
| `INV_ClearDiagnostic` | T-1: every exception emitted by `RequireField` has a `field_name` attribute equal to the key being required. State-form witness: every entry in `validation_log` whose outcome is a failure (MissingField or WrongType) has its `field_name` field set to a key in `FieldNames` AND has `has_diagnostic = TRUE`. Structural argument: every LogEntry constructed via `MakeLogEntry` has its `field_name` slot set to the schema entry's key — and the helper sets `has_diagnostic = TRUE` unconditionally. The C++ correspondent is the `"S-018: missing required JSON field 'FIELD'"` and `"S-018: JSON field 'FIELD' has wrong type: ..."` exception strings at `include/determ/util/json_validate.hpp:39-48`; the structural witness for "every helper-emitted exception carries the field name in single quotes" |
| `INV_NoInternalLeakage` | T-2: no exception is emitted without the field-name context (e.g., a raw `nlohmann::detail::type_error`). State-form witness: every entry in `validation_log` (regardless of outcome) has `has_diagnostic = TRUE`. Structural argument: the `MakeLogEntry` helper sets `has_diagnostic = TRUE` unconditionally — by construction every logged entry inherits the field-name context. The pre-S-018 leaky path (where a `nlohmann::detail::*` exception escapes without field-name context) would correspond to a LogEntry with `has_diagnostic = FALSE`, which is structurally unreachable in this spec because no action produces such an entry. The C++ correspondent is the `catch (const std::exception& e)` clause at `json_validate.hpp:44-48` that intercepts every nlohmann-internal exception and re-throws with `"S-018: JSON field 'FIELD' has wrong type: <inner>"` |
| `INV_DefenseInDepth` | T-3: any of the 5 surface entry points (Wire / RPC / Snapshot / Keyfile / Genesis) that calls `ValidateMessage` produces only field-name-tagged exceptions. State-form witness: every entry in `validation_log` has its `surface` field in `Surfaces` AND has `has_diagnostic = TRUE`. Structural argument: `ValidateAtSurface` is the only action that appends to `validation_log`, and its body restricts `s` to `Surfaces` by construction. Every entry in the log is therefore tagged with one of the five surfaces AND inherits the helper-emitted field-name context. No parallel bypass at any surface skips the helper contract. The C++ correspondents are the five entry points enumerated in §3.3 of the prose proof: `net::Message::deserialize` (Wire), `RpcServer::dispatch` structured-payload args (RPC), `Chain::restore_from_snapshot` collection wrappers (Snapshot), `crypto::load_node_key` (Keyfile), `GenesisConfig::from_json` (Genesis) |
| `INV_BoundedWork` | T-4: `ValidateMessage(obj, schema)` takes O(\|schema\|) time. State-form witness: `Len(validation_log) <= MaxValidations`. Structural argument: there is no action in the spec that iterates recursively or appends an unbounded number of entries. `ValidateAtSurface` appends exactly `Len(schema)` entries (a finite sequence-walk), and `Len(schema)` is bounded by `MaxSchemaLen` by construction of `BoundedSchemas`. The total log length is therefore bounded by `MaxValidations`.
