The C++ correspondents are the helpers' bodies at `json_validate.hpp:37-49` + `60-72` + `87-102`: one `contains()` + one `at()` + one `get<T>()` per call, all O(1) over the extracted value's already-bounded size; `json_require_array` adds an `is_array()` check; no loops, no recursion, no allocation beyond the failure-path exception string |
| `INV_OptionalBackwardCompat` | T-5: `OptionalField` returns the default value without emitting an exception when the key is absent. State-form witness: no entry in `validation_log` has outcome `"OptionalAbsent"` — by construction `ExtractOptional` does NOT append to the log. Structural argument: `ExtractOptional`'s action body leaves `validation_log` UNCHANGED. The only outcomes that ever appear in the log are Pass / MissingField / WrongType (from the required-field path), and none of these are emitted by the `OptionalField` operator. The C++ correspondents are the `j.value(field, default)` pattern (e.g., `ContribMsg::aborts_gen` at `producer.cpp` reading `j.value("aborts_gen", uint64_t{0})`) and the `if (j.contains(field)) { ... }` guard pattern (e.g., `Block::tx_root` / `delay_seed` / `delay_output` / `consensus_mode` / `bft_proposer` / `partner_subset_hash` / `state_root` at `Block::from_json`); both patterns silently take the default on absence, never emitting an exception |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-four specs above). The recommended `JsonValidation.cfg` (FieldNames = {amount, prev_hash, transactions}, MaxSchemaLen = 2, MaxValidations = 5) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The three-action state machine (ValidateAtSurface, ExtractOptional, SaturateSurface) exercises every reachable interleaving of surface entries × input JsonObjects × schema instances within the bounded universe. Variables modeled: `input_objects` (function `Surfaces → SUBSET JsonObjects` — the per-surface accumulator of admitted JSON inputs; abstracts the 5 surfaces' per-entry-point admission paths into a single tracking surface for INV-3's surface-tag invariant), `validation_log` (Seq of LogEntry where LogEntry = [surface, field_name, outcome, has_diagnostic] — the headline observable for INV-1/INV-2/INV-3/INV-4; every `ValidateAtSurface` invocation appends one entry per schema entry, capturing the C++ helper's per-required-field exception emission), `fired_surfaces` (SUBSET Surfaces — tracks which surfaces have fired at least one validation; drives the SaturateSurface stutter once every surface has been exercised). Actions modeled: `ValidateAtSurface(s)` (the headline action — pick a surface s, an input JsonObject, a schema; invoke ValidateMessage; append one LogEntry per schema entry; gated by the `Len(validation_log) + MaxSchemaLen <= MaxValidations` bound — the structural T-4 enforcement), `ExtractOptional(s)` (the optional-field extraction — pick a surface, an input, a key, a default; return either the present value or the default; never append to validation_log — the structural T-5 enforcement), `SaturateSurface` (stutter once every surface has fired AND the log bound is reached).

This spec captures the just-shipped S-018 closure of `JsonValidationSoundness.md` at the state-machine layer. The analytic proof (T-1..T-5) establishes that the three helpers in `include/determ/util/json_validate.hpp` (`json_require<T>`, `json_require_hex`, `json_require_array`) together provide a clear-diagnostic + defense-in-depth contract across every attack-relevant wire-format consumer. The TLA+ state-machine layer abstracts these into three actions + five invariants:

1. **The five-surface entry-point inventory** is captured by the `Surfaces` constant = {Wire, RPC, Snapshot, Keyfile, Genesis}. Each surface corresponds to one of the five entry points enumerated in §4.3 of the prose proof: wire (gossip envelope + per-message-type from_json), RPC (structured-payload args via the same S-018-hardened from_json), snapshot (`Chain::restore_from_snapshot` collection wrappers), keyfile (`crypto::load_node_key`), genesis (`GenesisConfig::from_json`). No parallel bypass at any surface skips the helper contract — `ValidateAtSurface` restricts s to `Surfaces` by construction.
2. **The clear-diagnostic contract** is captured by the `MakeLogEntry` helper's invariant: every LogEntry has `has_diagnostic = TRUE` AND its `field_name` slot bound to the schema entry's key. Pre-S-018 the leaky path would produce LogEntries with `has_diagnostic = FALSE` (the raw nlohmann-internal exception escaping without field-name context), which is structurally unreachable in this spec because no action produces such an entry. The C++ side's catch-`std::exception` clause at `json_validate.hpp:44-48` is the structural witness for "every nlohmann-internal exception gets re-thrown with the field-name context."
3. **The bounded-work contract** is captured by the `Len(validation_log) + MaxSchemaLen <= MaxValidations` guard on `ValidateAtSurface` and the `BoundedSchemas` constraint on schemas. No action in the spec iterates recursively or appends an unbounded number of entries — each ValidateMessage call walks a finite schema once.
4. **The optional-field backward-compat contract** is captured by `ExtractOptional`'s UNCHANGED clause on `validation_log`. The OptionalField operator never emits to the log; the C++ side's `j.value(field, default)` and `if (j.contains(field)) { ... }` patterns silently take the default on absence.

The abstract-diagnostic model (`has_diagnostic` as a BOOLEAN tag derived from the outcome rather than a byte-level exception message string) is the spec-layer projection of "the exception's `what()` contains the field name in single quotes" — the byte-level diagnostic substring matching is the regression test's job (`tools/test_s018_json_validation.sh`, 10/10 PASS). The cryptographic / size-cap / rate-limit gating layers that sit above the helpers (S-022, S-014, S-033 + S-038) are out of scope; S-018's role is field-level diagnostic clarity, NOT security-relevant rejection.

**Out of scope** (consistent with `JsonValidationSoundness.md` §6):
- The byte-level exception message text. The spec uses a BOOLEAN `has_diagnostic` tag to model "the exception's `what()` contains the field name in single quotes"; the byte-level diagnostic substring matching is the regression test's job (`tools/test_s018_json_validation.sh`).
- The catch-`std::exception` vs catch-`nlohmann::json::exception` choice. §4.2 of the prose proof argues catching `std::exception` is robust under RTTI-symbol-visibility variations; the spec collapses both branches into a single WrongType outcome with `has_diagnostic = TRUE`.
- The intentionally-non-converted residual sites enumerated in §6 of the prose proof (inner-loop array elements where the iterating container is already validated, CLI output formatters, client-side RPC response parser, `BlockSigMsg::dh_secret` optional-residual at `producer.cpp:212`). These are not exposed to peer-supplied JSON; the spec's five surfaces cover the attack surface that the helpers protect.
- The cryptographic / size-cap / rate-limit gating layers above the helpers (S-022 size caps, S-014 rate limiting, S-033 / S-038 state-root verification). S-018's role is field-level diagnostic clarity, NOT security-relevant rejection; the spec models only the diagnostic-clarity surface.
- The Ed25519 EUF-CMA / SHA-256 collision resistance bounds — the spec lifts these to deterministic predicates ("distinct pre-images map to distinct hashes") via the abstract-hash discipline (used in sibling specs FB23 / FB24 / FB25 / FB26); not invoked directly here because S-018 is below the cryptographic verification layer.

Companion analytic proof: `docs/proofs/JsonValidationSoundness.md` (the FA-S018 proof shipped Round 22; T-1 + T-2 + T-3 + T-4 + T-5 with the per-helper conversion inventory in §3.3 + adversary model in §5 + test-suite citation in §7). This TLA+ spec formalizes the state-machine layer of that proof: INV-1 lifts T-1's per-helper field-name-context emission; INV-2 lifts T-2's catch-`std::exception` clause; INV-3 lifts T-3's five-surface defense-in-depth; INV-4 lifts T-4's bounded-work / no-recursion / no-loop helper-body inspection; INV-5 lifts T-5's REQUIRED-vs-OPTIONAL distinction. The byte-level diagnostic-substring assertion is the regression test (`tools/test_s018_json_validation.sh`, 10/10 PASS) — the FB-track state-machine layer and the runtime regression together cover both the structural-soundness and the byte-precision-string assertions.

Cross-reference. FB22 `F2ViewReconciliation.tla` (v2.7 F2 view-reconciliation primitives), FB23 `FrostVerify.tla` (Ed25519 EUF-CMA model), FB24 `MakeContribCommitment.tla` (S-030 D2 commit-binding model), FB25 `RateLimiterEviction.tla` (S-014 F-1 lifetime-bound model), FB26 `BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla` (S-021 + S-033 + S-038 composition). FB27 (this spec — the S-018 clear-diagnostic + defense-in-depth state machine, sitting below the cryptographic / size-cap / rate-limit gating layers and providing the field-level diagnostic-clarity contract that operator triage relies on).

### S006ContribMsgEquivocation.tla → FA-S006 (Phase-1 same-generation ContribMsg equivocation detection state machine)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `pending_contribs` (Seq(ContribMsg) with "at most one entry per signer" structural constraint enforced by the ReceiveContribSameGen guard — the sequence proxy is the TLC-initialization vehicle for the partial-fn-keyed-by-signer C++ `std::map<std::string, ContribMsg> pending_contribs_` at `include/determ/node/node.hpp`), `pending_equivocation_evidence` (SUBSET EquivocationEvent), `drained_events` (SUBSET EquivocationEvent), `valid_sigs` (SUBSET of [signer, commit_hash] tuples — the spec-layer projection of `crypto::verify` acceptance), `event_origins` (SUBSET SourceGen — the per-event audit-tag tracking the generation at which the event was constructed), `current_gen` (AbortGenerations — the receiver's `current_aborts_.size()`), `received_contribs` (SUBSET ContribMsg — audit set of every ContribMsg admitted by the receive path) |
| `INV_SameGenDetection` | T-1 (Same-Generation Duplicate Detection): for every pair of distinct ContribMsgs `cm1, cm2` in `received_contribs` with the same signer / block_index / aborts_gen but distinct commit_hashes, an EquivocationEvent against that signer at that block_index exists somewhere in the system — either in `pending_equivocation_evidence` (not yet drained) or in `drained_events` (already baked into a block and routed through the apply pipeline). The structural witness: ReceiveContribSameGen's B4 branch (commit-mismatch on existing entry) constructs an event when the duplicate-detect predicate fires; the pool-dedup scan ensures at most one event per (equivocator, block_index) survives across the union pending ++ drained, but at least one always does (B4 always appends OR a prior B4 fired and produced the same-key event already). The C++ correspondent is the receive-path branch at `src/node/node.cpp:2122..2163` — the `auto existing = pending_contribs_.find(msg.signer)` + `if (existing_commit != commit)` + EquivocationEvent construction sequence |
| `INV_CrossGenNoFalsePositive` | T-2 (Different-Generation Drop, No False Positive): no EquivocationEvent in pending_equivocation_evidence \cup drained_events has cross-generation sources. State-form witness: every event in the union has a corresponding entry in `event_origins` recording a single shared gen (the gen of its two ContribMsg sources, which by INV-1's preconditions are equal). The structural argument: ReceiveContribSameGen's pre-condition requires `aborts_gen = current_gen` for both the existing entry (admitted under a prior B2 at current_gen) and the incoming message (B4 entry guard); ReceiveContribDifferentGen short-circuits to UNCHANGED before reaching the duplicate-detect branch, modeling the C++ gen-gate at `node.cpp:2068` (`if (msg.aborts_gen != current_aborts_.size()) return;`). AdvanceGeneration clears pending_contribs on reset (modeling `reset_round`), so an honest signer's legitimate retry at a higher gen finds no existing entry to false-trigger against |
| `INV_EvidencePoolMonotone` | T-3 composition (FA-Apply-10 consume-side compatibility): the union `pending_equivocation_evidence \cup drained_events` only ever grows across every `[Next]_vars` step. Action-form invariant `(pending' \cup drained') \supseteq (pending \cup drained)`. The structural argument: SignAndSend / ReceiveContribDifferentGen / AdvanceGeneration / Stutter all preserve both sets; ReceiveContribSameGen B4 either extends pending or preserves it (on pool-dedup hit); ApplyBlockDrainsPool moves entries from pending to drained (the union grows by 0). Composed with FB15 EquivocationApply.tla's pending_events / drained semantics — the same pool the apply-side consumes. The C++ correspondent is the `Node::pending_equivocation_evidence_` vector + the producer's `build_body` consume site at `producer.cpp:452` + the FA-Apply-10 slash-on-apply at `chain.cpp:1344..1356` |
| `INV_TwoSigsValid` | T-4 (Two-Sig Proof Soundness): every entry in pending_equivocation_evidence \cup drained_events has its sig_a and sig_b in `valid_sigs` (the spec-layer projection of `crypto::verify` acceptance), AND those sigs are bound to the correct (signer, commit_hash) tuples via the structural equality `sig_a = [signer |-> equivocator, commit_hash |-> digest_a]` and `sig_b = [signer |-> equivocator, commit_hash |-> digest_b]`. The structural witness: ReceiveContribSameGen B4 constructs the event using the existing entry's sig (which was admitted via a prior B2 / B3 that required the incoming sig in valid_sigs) AND the incoming message's sig (also pre-checked at the B4 entry guard). The downstream V11 re-verification at `validator.cpp:307..322` is the corresponding apply-time witness; INV-4 captures the receive-time half of the two-layer check. EUF-CMA forgery resistance is FB23 FrostVerify.tla territory; the spec abstracts via the valid_sigs membership predicate |
| `INV_ReplaySafe` | T-5 (Replay-Safety): no two events in pending_equivocation_evidence \cup drained_events share a PoolDedupKey (equivocator, block_index). The structural witness: ReceiveContribSameGen B4's pool-dedup scan (the `dup_in_pool \/ dup_in_drained` guard) rejects any incoming event whose key already exists in the union, AND ApplyBlockDrainsPool moves entries to drained without duplication (the union does not gain a duplicate by the move). The C++ correspondent is the pool-dedup loop at `node.cpp:2147..2153` (the `for (auto& e : pending_equivocation_evidence_)` scan that skips events with matching `(equivocator, block_index)`). Composed with FB15 EquivocationApply.tla's `Inv_NoDoubleSlash`, this gives the cross-spec end-to-end claim: the same (equivocator, block_index) pair contributes at most one slash across the full detect → bake → apply pipeline |
| `INV_ChannelReuse` | T-3 sub-claim (no new wire format): every entry in pending_equivocation_evidence \cup drained_events satisfies `EquivocationEventShape` — the same six-field shape produced by the rev.8 BlockSigMsg-level detector. The structural witness: ReceiveContribSameGen B4 uses the constructor pattern of the EquivocationEvent record type, with the same six fields the rev.8 BlockSigMsg detector populates (equivocator, block_index, digest_a, sig_a, digest_b, sig_b). No alternate struct, no additional fields, no parallel ContribMsg-equivocation subtype. The C++ correspondent is the `chain::EquivocationEvent` struct at `include/determ/chain/block.hpp:256..279` (unchanged from rev.8); the S-006 closure reuses it verbatim per the digest-agnostic argument in §2.2 of the prose proof. Implicit corollary: the unused legacy `contrib_equivocations_` field declared in `node.hpp` was removed (per `SECURITY.md` §S-006 "Cleanup"), and the spec doesn't model the deleted dead code |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-five specs above). The recommended `S006ContribMsgEquivocation.cfg` (Signers = {a, b}, BlockIndices = {0, 1}, AbortGenerations = {0, 1}, Hashes = {h1, h2, h3}) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The five-action state machine (SignAndSend, ReceiveContribSameGen, ReceiveContribDifferentGen, AdvanceGeneration, ApplyBlockDrainsPool) exercises every reachable interleaving of honest / Byzantine signing, same-gen / cross-gen arrivals, abort-quorum boundaries, and block-apply consume. Variables modeled: `pending_contribs` (Seq(ContribMsg) used as a partial-fn proxy — the spec enforces "at most one entry per signer" structurally via the ReceiveContribSameGen guard; matches the C++ `std::map<std::string, ContribMsg> pending_contribs_` at `include/determ/node/node.hpp`), `pending_equivocation_evidence` (SUBSET EquivocationEvent — the receive-time pool, matching `Node::pending_equivocation_evidence_`; SET semantics so the (equivocator, block_index) pool-dedup at `node.cpp:2147..2153` collapses duplicates), `drained_events` (SUBSET EquivocationEvent — spec-layer audit of events consumed by block-apply; tracks cross-block / cross-spec replay safety), `valid_sigs` (SUBSET of [signer, commit_hash] tuples — the set of Ed25519 sig pairs that have passed `crypto::verify`; populated by SignAndSend), `event_origins` (SUBSET SourceGen — per-event audit tag tracking the gen at which the event was constructed; INV-2's structural witness for no-cross-gen-sources), `current_gen` (AbortGenerations — the receiver's `current_aborts_.size()`), `received_contribs` (SUBSET ContribMsg — audit set of every ContribMsg admitted; INV-1's coverage check predicate). Actions modeled: `SignAndSend(s, h, g, c)` (the adversarial / honest signer surface — admits a `[signer, commit_hash]` pair to valid_sigs; Byzantine signers may sign multiple distinct commits over the same (block_index, aborts_gen) tuple, honest signers obey H2 of Preliminaries §4 but the spec doesn't enforce this — the detector at ReceiveContrib catches the equivocation regardless), `ReceiveContribSameGen(s, h, c)` (the headline action — the C++ receive path's four branches: B1 cross-gen short-circuits via the disabled-action equivalence, B2 first-arrival admits to pending_contribs, B3 byte-identical retry drops silently, B4 commit-mismatch on existing entry constructs the EquivocationEvent and routes via the pool-dedup scan), `ReceiveContribDifferentGen(s, h, g)` (the cross-generation drop branch — disabled when `g = current_gen`, no-op otherwise, modeling the C++ gen-gate at line 2068), `AdvanceGeneration` (abort-quorum boundary — increments current_gen to any greater value in AbortGenerations and clears pending_contribs, modeling `reset_round`), `ApplyBlockDrainsPool` (block-finalize consume — moves the entire pending_equivocation_evidence pool into drained_events; the per-event FA-Apply-10 slash mechanics are FB15 territory). The four ReceiveContribSameGen branches are mutually exclusive on their inner-IF guards and together cover the full receive-path branching at `node.cpp:2056..2170`.

This spec captures the just-shipped S-006 closure of `S006ContribMsgEquivocation.md` at the state-machine layer. The analytic proof (T-1..T-5) establishes that the receive-time Phase-1 detector at `Node::on_contrib` adds a second equivocation-detection surface — at the Phase-1 commit layer — without introducing a new wire format, new validator predicate, or new apply-side branch. The TLA+ state-machine layer abstracts these into five actions + six invariants:

1. **Same-generation duplicate detection (T-1)** is captured by INV_SameGenDetection — every distinct-commit same-gen pair in received_contribs is matched by an EquivocationEvent in pending ++ drained. The C++ correspondent is the B4 branch at `node.cpp:2122..2163` which constructs the event when the duplicate-detect predicate `existing_commit != commit` fires. The pool-dedup at `node.cpp:2147..2153` ensures at most one event per (equivocator, block_index) survives, captured by INV_ReplaySafe.

2. **Cross-generation drop without false positive (T-2)** is captured by INV_CrossGenNoFalsePositive — every event's origin record has a single gen. The C++ correspondent is the gen-gate at `node.cpp:2068` which short-circuits before the duplicate-detect branch; the spec models this via ReceiveContribDifferentGen's no-op body. AdvanceGeneration clears pending_contribs on reset, modeling the `reset_round` machinery — an honest signer's legitimate retry at a higher gen finds no existing entry to false-trigger against.

3. **Composition with FA6 + FA-Apply-10 (T-3)** is captured by INV_EvidencePoolMonotone (the pool is the same pool the apply-side consumes) and INV_ChannelReuse (no new wire format). FB15 EquivocationApply.tla covers the apply-side mechanics; the two specs share the EquivocationEvent struct shape exactly. The C++ correspondent is the rev.8 EquivocationEvent struct at `include/determ/chain/block.hpp:256..279` — reused verbatim by S-006 per the digest-agnostic argument in §2.2 of the prose proof.

4. **Two-sig proof soundness (T-4)** is captured by INV_TwoSigsValid — every event has both sigs in valid_sigs and bound to the correct (signer, commit_hash) tuples. The C++ correspondent is the sig-verify gate at `node.cpp:2089` (`crypto::verify(entry->pubkey, commit.data(), commit.size(), msg.ed_sig)`); the corresponding gate fired on the existing entry's admission ensures both halves of the constructed event are pre-validated. The downstream V11 re-verification at `validator.cpp:307..322` is the belt-and-suspenders apply-time witness; INV-4 captures the receive-time half of the two-layer check.

5. **Replay-safety (T-5)** is captured by INV_ReplaySafe — no two events share a PoolDedupKey across pending + drained. The C++ correspondent is the pool-dedup loop at `node.cpp:2147..2153` (the `for (auto& e : pending_equivocation_evidence_)` scan that skips events with matching `(equivocator, block_index)`). Composed with FB15 EquivocationApply.tla's `Inv_NoDoubleSlash`, this gives the cross-spec end-to-end claim: the same (equivocator, block_index) pair contributes at most one slash across the full detect → bake → apply pipeline.

The abstract-sig model (`valid_sigs` as a SUBSET of [signer, commit_hash] tuples populated only by SignAndSend) is the standard TLA+ projection of A1 (Ed25519 EUF-CMA) — the cryptographic tightness is FA-track territory (FB23 FrostVerify.tla). The abstract-hash model (Hashes as a finite universe with distinct ContribMsg content producing distinct commit_hash) is the standard TLA+ projection of A2 (SHA-256 collision resistance) — the cryptographic tightness is FA-track territory (FB24 MakeContribCommitment.tla). The FB-track here checks the state-machine consistency of the detection surface under the abstract-sig + abstract-hash discipline.

**Out of scope** (consistent with `S006ContribMsgEquivocation.md` §6):
- Apply-side slash mechanics (T-E1 / T-E2 / T-E3 / T-E5 / T-E7 of FA-Apply-10). The `drained_events` set is the spec-layer audit of "events that have been consumed by the apply pipeline"; the per-event stake-forfeit + registry-deactivation + accumulated-slashed update happens in FB15 EquivocationApply.tla, which this spec composes with via INV_EvidencePoolMonotone + INV_ReplaySafe (shared pool semantics + replay-safety).
- The V11 validator predicate re-verification at block-validate time. INV_TwoSigsValid captures the receive-time sig-verify; V11's re-verification at `validator.cpp:307..322` is FA6 territory. The two-layer check is documented in §4.4 of the prose proof.
- Cross-shard equivocation routing (the `shard_id` / `beacon_anchor_height` fields of the C++ EquivocationEvent). FA6 T-6.1 covers this; the spec abstracts cross-shard handling.
- The forensic-audit coarseness at pool-dedup time (§6.3 of the prose proof). The (equivocator, block_index) key collapses multiple distinct same-(d, h) incidents into one observable event; this is intentional and matches the C++ behavior. INV_ReplaySafe captures the dedup contract; the multi-incident forensic audit is out of scope.
- The byte-identical retry case (§6.1 of the prose proof). The spec's ReceiveContribSameGen B3 branch (existing_commit = c) short-circuits to "no event, drop silently" — captured by the IF-branch in the action body that leaves pending_equivocation_evidence UNCHANGED on equal-commit retries.
- The F2 view-root binding contract (§6.4 of the prose proof). The spec's `commit_hash` field is the equivalence-class output of `make_contrib_commitment` per FB24 MakeContribCommitment.tla; the distinct-pre-image lemmas L-2 / L-3 of FB24 are the cryptographic backing.
- The deleted `contrib_equivocations_` field (§6.5 of the prose proof). The post-S-006 source has no such field; the spec doesn't model the deleted dead code.
- Cryptographic forgery resistance. SignAndSend admits any (signer, commit_hash) pair into valid_sigs without enforcing EUF-CMA at the spec layer; FB23 FrostVerify.tla covers the cryptographic side. The composition is via INV_TwoSigsValid's valid_sigs membership predicate.

Companion analytic proof: `docs/proofs/S006ContribMsgEquivocation.md` (the FA-S006 proof shipped R23A7; T-1 + T-2 + T-3 + T-4 + T-5 with the receive-path source citation in §3, per-theorem proofs in §4, adversary model in §5, identified gaps in §6, test-suite citation in §7). This TLA+ spec formalizes the state-machine layer of that proof: INV_SameGenDetection lifts T-1's same-gen duplicate-detect coverage; INV_CrossGenNoFalsePositive lifts T-2's cross-gen no-false-positive; INV_EvidencePoolMonotone + INV_ChannelReuse lift T-3's composition + no-new-wire-format; INV_TwoSigsValid lifts T-4's two-sig soundness; INV_ReplaySafe lifts T-5's replay-safety pool-dedup contract.

Cross-reference. FB22 `F2ViewReconciliation.tla` (v2.7 F2 view-reconciliation primitives — the post-S-006 contrib commit binds via the DTM-F2-v1 path), FB23 `FrostVerify.tla` (Ed25519 EUF-CMA model — the abstract-sig discipline INV_TwoSigsValid relies on), FB24 `MakeContribCommitment.tla` (S-030 D2 commit-binding model — the distinct-pre-image property INV_SameGenDetection relies on), FB25 `RateLimiterEviction.tla` (S-014 F-1 lifetime-bound model), FB26 `BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla` (S-021 + S-033 + S-038 composition), FB27 `JsonValidation.tla` (S-018 clear-diagnostic + defense-in-depth). ### BlockTimestampMonotonic.tla → R24A5 (Block.timestamp monotonicity + digest-exclusion contract)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `chains` (Nodes → Seq(Block) — each block carries the four invariant-relevant fields index/timestamp/prev_hash/txs), `pending_inbox` (Nodes → Seq(Block) — gossip queue), `tampered_at` (Nodes → 0..MaxChainLength ∪ {"none"} — interior tamper site, latches across actions), `load_throws` (Nodes → BOOLEAN — reload reject latch) |
| `INV_TimestampMonotonic` | T-1 (forward-looking S-035 path-1 contract): when `monotonic_gate` is TRUE, every adjacent pair in every chain satisfies `chain[i].timestamp >= chain[i-1].timestamp`. When `monotonic_gate` is FALSE (the R24A5-pinned current behavior), the invariant is vacuously satisfied. The structural witness: ApplyBlock's `ts_ok` predicate gates on `b.timestamp >= head.timestamp` only when `monotonic_gate = TRUE`; rejects otherwise. ProduceBlock samples timestamps only in `[head.timestamp, head.timestamp + MaxTimestampSkew]`, so producer-side blocks always satisfy T-1 regardless of the gate setting — the gate's role is to reject adversarial / tampered inbound blocks at apply time. The C++ correspondent is the documented absence of an inter-block timestamp gate in `Chain::append` at `src/chain/chain.cpp:54` — the test-pinned current behavior under SECURITY.md §S-035 path 1 |
| `INV_DigestExcludesTimestamp` | T-2 (digest invariance under timestamp): for every pair of conceptual blocks `b1, b2` identical in every field except timestamp, `compute_block_digest(b1) = compute_block_digest(b2)`. The structural witness: `compute_block_digest`'s pre-image tuple omits the timestamp field (see the operator definition in §1 of the .tla); pure-function equality + abstract-hash discipline makes the equality automatic. The K-of-K Phase-2 digest deliberately excludes consensus-time metadata so committee members converge on the same digest despite local clock skew within the ±30s validator window. The C++ correspondent is the `compute_block_digest` implementation at `src/node/producer.cpp` (~line 577) — the timestamp field is omitted from the digest's pre-image. Lifted from R24A5 test scenario 7; the analytic source is `docs/proofs/S030-D2-Analysis.md` (D2 selective-abort resistance) |
| `INV_SigningBytesIncludesTimestamp` | T-3 (signing_bytes timestamp binding): for every pair of blocks `b1, b2` identical in every field except timestamp where `b1.timestamp /= b2.timestamp`, `compute_signing_bytes(b1) /= compute_signing_bytes(b2)`. The structural witness: `compute_signing_bytes`'s pre-image tuple INCLUDES timestamp; by abstract-hash injectivity (distinct pre-images map to distinct outputs), distinct timestamps produce distinct signing_bytes. The producer's full block hash IS timestamp-bound for chain-history integrity; a committee member's signature cannot replay across blocks differing in timestamp. The C++ correspondent is the `Block::signing_bytes` implementation at `include/determ/chain/block.hpp` — the timestamp field is included via the leading tuple, alongside index/prev_hash/txs (plus the conditional partner_subset_hash + state_root tails per PROTOCOL.md §4.1). Lifted from R24A5 test scenario 6 |
| `INV_HistoricalTamperCascades` | T-4 (cascade via prev_hash): tampering `chain[i].timestamp` for an interior block invalidates the `compute_hash` cascade for `chain[i+1..head]` via the prev_hash chain. The structural witness: `compute_hash` of the tampered block /= prev_hash of the next block (because `compute_hash` INCLUDES timestamp, so a single-field mutation breaks the cascade); `validate_chain` returns FALSE; ReloadChain's failure path latches `load_throws[n] = TRUE`. State-form invariant: at every reachable state, if `tampered_at[n] /= "none"` AND the tampered block has at least one successor, then `validate_chain(chains[n])` is FALSE. The C++ correspondent is the `Chain::append` prev_hash check at `src/chain/chain.cpp:54-58` (the spec's `validate_chain` helper mirrors it) + the `Chain::load` head_hash recompute at `src/chain/chain.cpp:1987-2054` (composes with FB26's INV_LoadDetectsTampering via the shared `validate_chain` discipline). Lifted from R24A5 test scenarios 5 + 8 + S-021 closure |
| `INV_EqualTimestampAccepted` | T-5 (non-strict monotonicity): adjacent equal timestamps (`chain[i].timestamp = chain[i-1].timestamp`) are admissible — block production within the same UTC second is legal. The structural witness: ProduceBlock samples timestamps from `[head.timestamp, head.timestamp + MaxTimestampSkew]` inclusive of the lower bound, so `head.timestamp` is a reachable sample; ApplyBlock's `ts_ok` predicate uses non-strict `>=`, so equal-timestamp adjacent blocks are admissible under both gate-OFF and gate-ON disciplines. The C++ correspondent is R24A5 test scenario 2: `Chain::append` accepts equal adjacent timestamps verbatim |
| `PROP_EventualBlockProduction` | Liveness: under fairness on ProduceBlock, chain length grows over time — eventually some chain reaches MaxChainLength. The structural witness: ProduceBlock's pre-condition `Len(chains[n]) <= MaxChainLength` is enabled until saturation; weak fairness on the action set guarantees it fires until disabled. The dual of FB26's "no silent divergence" liveness track |
| `PROP_NoSilentDivergence` | Temporal composition of T-4 + S-021: tampered chain at any node fires the load-time recompute reject before any downstream apply extends the tampered chain. State-form witness: for every reachable state where `tampered_at[n] /= "none"` AND `chain[n]` has a successor block past the tamper site, eventually ReloadChain fires and latches `load_throws[n] = TRUE`. Composes with FB26's `INV_LoadDetectsTampering` via the shared `validate_chain` helper + the shared prev_hash continuity discipline. T-4 (HistoricalTamperCascades) is the structural source; this temporal property asserts the cascade is observable via the `load_throws` gate within the bounded reachable schedule |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-six specs above). The recommended `BlockTimestampMonotonic.cfg` (Nodes = {n1, n2}, MaxChainLength = 3, MaxTimestamp = 3, MaxTimestampSkew = 1, TxUniverse = {t1}, monotonic_gate = FALSE) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The four-action state machine (ProduceBlock, ApplyBlock, TamperHistoricalTimestamp, ReloadChain) exercises every reachable interleaving of legitimate block production, cross-node gossip, adversarial tampering, and load-time reload. Variables modeled: `chains` (Nodes → Seq(Block) — each chain seeded with the GenesisBlock pinned at index=0 / timestamp=0 / prev_hash=GenesisHash per `make_genesis_block` at `src/chain/genesis.cpp:301`), `pending_inbox` (Nodes → Seq(Block) — the gossip queue between nodes; ProduceBlock at one node appends to other nodes' inboxes, ApplyBlock drains the head subject to prev_hash + optional ts_ok gate), `tampered_at` (Nodes → 0..MaxChainLength ∪ {"none"} — interior tamper site logged by TamperHistoricalTimestamp), `load_throws` (Nodes → BOOLEAN — latches TRUE the moment ReloadChain detects a cascade-broken prev_hash). Actions modeled: `ProduceBlock(n)` (samples timestamp from `[head.timestamp, head.timestamp + MaxTimestampSkew]` inclusive on both ends — lower bound makes T-5 EqualTimestampAccepted reachable, upper bound makes T-1 monotonic samples reachable; broadcasts to other-node inboxes), `ApplyBlock(n)` (drains pending_inbox head; validates prev_hash continuity + the optional `monotonic_gate` strict-monotonic gate; appends on success, silently drops on reject — the exception-surface invariants are FB26 / FB27 territory), `TamperHistoricalTimestamp(n)` (adversary mutates an interior block's timestamp; the post-tamper `compute_hash` differs because the pre-image INCLUDES timestamp, breaking the prev_hash cascade at the next block), `ReloadChain(n)` (the spec-layer projection of `Chain::load`; walks `validate_chain`; latches `load_throws` on prev_hash mismatch — the T-4 boundary catch).

This spec captures the just-shipped R24A5 `test-time-monotonicity` unit test at the state-machine layer. The analytic source (`src/main.cpp::test-time-monotonicity` at lines 28776..29049 + `tools/test_time_monotonicity.sh`) pins 17 assertions across 9 scenarios; the TLA+ state-machine layer abstracts the four cryptographic surfaces (chain identity, signing_bytes, digest, optional apply-time gate) into four actions + six invariants + two temporal properties:

1. **Strict-monotonic gate (T-1)** is captured by `INV_TimestampMonotonic` conditional on the `monotonic_gate` CONSTANT. The default cfg leaves the gate DISABLED to match the current `Chain::append` behavior pinned by R24A5 scenarios 1, 2, 3, 8 (backward / equal / far-future / negative timestamps all admitted at the chain layer). Flipping the gate to TRUE exercises the forward-looking S-035 path-1 contract for spec-coverage purposes ahead of the actual code change.

2. **Digest excludes timestamp (T-2)** is captured by `INV_DigestExcludesTimestamp`. The K-of-K Phase-2 digest deliberately omits consensus-time metadata so committee members converge on the same digest despite local clock skew within the ±30s validator window. The C++ correspondent is `compute_block_digest` at `src/node/producer.cpp` ~line 577; the analytic backing is the D2 selective-abort resistance argument in `docs/proofs/S030-D2-Analysis.md`.

3. **Signing_bytes includes timestamp (T-3)** is captured by `INV_SigningBytesIncludesTimestamp`. The producer's full block hash IS timestamp-bound for chain-history integrity; a committee member's signature cannot replay across blocks differing in timestamp. The C++ correspondent is `Block::signing_bytes` at `include/determ/chain/block.hpp` (the timestamp field is included via the leading tuple, alongside the conditional partner_subset_hash + state_root tails per PROTOCOL.md §4.1).

4. **Historical tamper cascades (T-4)** is captured by `INV_HistoricalTamperCascades`. Tampering an interior block's timestamp breaks `compute_hash` at that block (since `compute_hash` INCLUDES timestamp), which breaks `prev_hash` at the next block, which makes `validate_chain` return FALSE at load time, which latches `load_throws`. Composes with FB26 BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla's `INV_LoadDetectsTampering` via the shared `validate_chain` helper.

5. **Equal-timestamp acceptance (T-5)** is captured by `INV_EqualTimestampAccepted`. Block production within the same UTC second is admissible (non-strict monotonicity); ProduceBlock's sample range includes `head.timestamp` as the lower bound, and ApplyBlock's `ts_ok` predicate uses non-strict `>=`.

The two temporal properties (PROP_EventualBlockProduction + PROP_NoSilentDivergence) lift the live-progress + cascade-observability claims to the temporal layer. PROP_NoSilentDivergence is the headline composition: any tamper at any node fires the load-time reject before downstream apply extends the tampered chain — the dual liveness of FB26's safety track.

**Out of scope** (consistent with the R24A5 test's documented scope):
- The validator's wall-clock window check (`|B.timestamp - now()| <= 30s` at `src/node/validator.cpp::check_timestamp`). This is a validator-time gate (Preliminaries V14) orthogonal to the chain-layer monotonicity contract; the spec abstracts `now()` and the ±30s window into the `MaxTimestampSkew` constant at ProduceBlock time.
- The partner_subset_hash + state_root threading in signing_bytes (PROTOCOL.md §4.1, R4 Phase 3 conditional + S-033 conditional). The spec's `compute_signing_bytes` is a timestamp-focused projection; the full signing_bytes specification is FB26 (BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla) territory.
- The genesis-trust pin (validator.cpp:19 short-circuit at index 0). The chain init seeds with `GenesisBlock`; the spec never re-applies genesis.
- Cryptographic soundness of SHA-256 (A2) and Ed25519 EUF-CMA (A1). The abstract-hash discipline + abstract-sig pattern is FA-track territory (FB23 FrostVerify.tla).
- The ±30s validator window's interaction with operator-side clock skew. The spec's `MaxTimestampSkew` abstracts this; the wall-clock skew model is documented in §V14 of Preliminaries + the S-003 validator-window analysis.

Companion analytic source: `src/main.cpp::test-time-monotonicity` (R24A5, 17 assertions across 9 scenarios at lines 28776..29049) + `tools/test_time_monotonicity.sh` (the shell wrapper). This TLA+ spec formalizes the state-machine layer of those assertions: INV_TimestampMonotonic lifts T-1's forward-looking strict-monotonic gate (current code has the gate DISABLED per S-035 path 1); INV_DigestExcludesTimestamp lifts T-2's digest-omission (R24A5 scenario 7); INV_SigningBytesIncludesTimestamp lifts T-3's signing_bytes inclusion (R24A5 scenario 6); INV_HistoricalTamperCascades lifts T-4's prev_hash cascade (R24A5 scenarios 5 + 8 + S-021 composition); INV_EqualTimestampAccepted lifts T-5's non-strict monotonicity (R24A5 scenario 2).

### ChainPrevHashLink.tla → R25 (prev_hash chain-link contract + cascade-detection invariants)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `chains` (Nodes → Seq(Block) — each block carries the four invariant-relevant fields index/prev_hash/body_hash/compute_hash), `pending_inbox` (Nodes → Seq(Block) — gossip queue between nodes), `tampered_at` (Nodes → 0..MaxChainLength ∪ {"none"} — interior tamper site, latches across actions), `load_throws` (Nodes → BOOLEAN — reload reject latch), `rejected_by` (Nodes → {"none", "chain", "validator", "both"} — latches WHICH gate fired on the most recent reject; "both" indicates the two-layer defense fired in concert), `ghost_chain_history` (Nodes → Seq(Block) — append-only legitimate-history record that TamperHistorical does NOT mutate; the INV_AppendOnly witness) |
| `INV_PrevHashLinkValid` | T-1 (happy path): for every non-genesis block in every chain, `block[i].prev_hash = block[i-1].compute_hash`. The structural witness: the chain only grows via ProduceBlock + ApplyBlock, both of which construct/validate blocks with `prev_hash = head_hash(chains[n])` before appending. The invariant is asserted on the SUBCHAIN preceding the tamper site (`tampered_at[n] = "none" \/ i <= tampered_at[n]`) so TamperHistorical doesn't spuriously invalidate INV_1 (the cascade past the tamper site is captured by INV_HistoricalTamperCascades). The C++ correspondent is the per-block link discipline enforced by `Chain::append` at `src/chain/chain.cpp:54-58` (every append checks `b.prev_hash == head_hash()`). Lifted from R25 test scenario 1 |
| `INV_GenesisPrevHashZero` | T-2 (chain-anchor convention): the genesis block (chain[1] in 1-indexed TLA) has `prev_hash = ZeroHash`. The structural witness: Init seeds with `GenesisBlock` whose `prev_hash = ZeroHash`; TamperHistorical's quantifier is `i \in 2..Len(chains[n])` so genesis is skipped. The C++ correspondent is `make_genesis_block` at `src/chain/genesis.cpp` leaving `prev_hash` at its default-constructed all-zero `Hash{}` (the chain-identity anchor for the empty-chain bootstrap path). Lifted from R25 test scenario 2 |
| `INV_WrongPrevHashRejected` | T-3 (two-layer defense): for every reachable state, every block that has ever been appended to `chains[n]` satisfied `prev_hash_ok(b, chains[n])` at append time. The state-form witness: ApplyBlock's success branch is the ONLY path that drains an inbox block into the chain, and it's gated on the shared `prev_hash_ok` predicate; the reject branch silently drops from inbox without extending the chain, latching `rejected_by[n] = "both"` to record the two-layer defense (chain-layer + validator-layer both gate on the same condition). The C++ correspondents are `Chain::append` at `src/chain/chain.cpp:54-58` (chain-layer gate; throws `"Block prev_hash mismatch"`) AND `BlockValidator::check_prev_hash` at `src/node/validator.cpp:43-48` (validator-layer gate; returns `{false, "prev_hash mismatch"}`). The two-layer defense ensures any regression weakening one gate is caught by the other. Lifted from R25 test scenarios 3a (all-zero prev_hash at height 2), 3b (0xFF... prev_hash at height 2), and 6 (empty prev_hash at height 1) |
| `INV_ReloadPreservesLinks` | T-4 (round-trip identity): for every reachable state where the chain is untampered (`tampered_at[n] = "none"`), `load_throws[n]` is FALSE AND every per-block link in `chains[n]` holds. The structural witness: the abstract-hash discipline is purely structural (no serialization noise), so the in-memory chain and a hypothetical reloaded copy have byte-identical prev_hash linkage. The C++ correspondent is `Chain::save` + `Chain::load` round-trip — the S-021 chain-integrity gate enforces head_hash globally; T-4 additionally pins the per-block link discipline so a regression that bypassed the head_hash check OR changed compute_hash inputs would still trip on a per-block link recompute. Lifted from R25 test scenario 4 |
| `INV_HistoricalTamperCascades` | T-5 (cascade via prev_hash): tampering ANY compute_hash-contributing field at `chain[i]` invalidates the downstream prev_hash linkage at `chain[i+1]` — because `chain[i+1].prev_hash` was bound to the PRE-tamper compute_hash of `chain[i]`. The structural witness: compute_hash is injective over its full pre-image tuple (abstract-hash discipline); any single-field mutation changes compute_hash; `validate_chain` returns FALSE at load time; ReloadChain's failure path latches `load_throws[n] = TRUE`. State-form invariant: at every reachable state, if `tampered_at[n] = k` with `k \in 2..Len(chains[n])` AND `k < Len(chains[n])`, then `validate_chain(chains[n])` is FALSE. The C++ correspondent is the load-time recompute discipline at `src/chain/chain.cpp::Chain::load` (the per-block prev_hash continuity walk inside the S-021 wrap). Lifted from R25 test scenario 5 |
| `INV_AppendOnly` | T-7 (no retroactive rewrite): for every reachable state with no tamper, `chains[n]` and `ghost_chain_history[n]` are byte-identical sequences. The structural witness: `ghost_chain_history` is updated only by ProduceBlock + ApplyBlock (the legitimate extension actions); TamperHistorical does NOT touch the ghost. Equality between `chains[n]` and `ghost_chain_history[n]` in the no-tamper branch proves legitimate chain extension never rewrites earlier blocks — the append-only contract on which fork-resolution and snapshot consistency depend. The C++ correspondent is `Chain::append`'s vector-push-back semantics at `src/chain/chain.cpp` (the chain's `blocks_` vector grows via `push_back`; existing entries are not rewritten). Lifted from R25 test scenario 7 |
| `PROP_EventualBlockProduction` | Liveness: under fairness on ProduceBlock, chain length grows over time — eventually some chain reaches MaxChainLength. The structural witness: ProduceBlock's pre-condition `Len(chains[n]) <= MaxChainLength` is enabled until saturation; weak fairness on the action set guarantees it fires until disabled. The dual of FB26's + FB29's "no silent divergence" liveness track |
| `PROP_TamperEventuallyDetected` | Temporal composition of T-5 + S-021: if `tampered_at[n] /= "none"` AND `chains[n]` has at least one successor block past the tamper site, then eventually ReloadChain fires and latches `load_throws[n] = TRUE`. State-form witness: ReloadChain's failure path is enabled whenever `validate_chain(chains[n])` is FALSE; INV_HistoricalTamperCascades pins that the tamper structurally invalidates validate_chain; weak fairness on ReloadChain guarantees the load_throws latch within the bounded reachable schedule. Composes with FB26's `INV_LoadDetectsTampering` + FB29's `PROP_NoSilentDivergence` via the shared `validate_chain` helper + the shared prev_hash continuity discipline |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-seven specs above). The recommended `ChainPrevHashLink.cfg` (Nodes = {n1, n2}, MaxChainLength = 3, BodyHashes = {bh1, bh2, bh3}) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The four-action state machine (ProduceBlock, ApplyBlock, TamperHistorical, ReloadChain) exercises every reachable interleaving of legitimate block production, cross-node gossip, adversarial body-hash tampering, and load-time reload. Variables modeled: `chains` (Nodes → Seq(Block) — each chain seeded with the GenesisBlock pinned at index=0 / prev_hash=ZeroHash / body_hash=GenesisBodyHash per `make_genesis_block` at `src/chain/genesis.cpp`), `pending_inbox` (Nodes → Seq(Block) — the gossip queue between nodes; ProduceBlock at one node appends to other nodes' inboxes, ApplyBlock drains the head subject to the shared `prev_hash_ok` predicate), `tampered_at` (Nodes → 0..MaxChainLength ∪ {"none"} — interior tamper site logged by TamperHistorical), `load_throws` (Nodes → BOOLEAN — latches TRUE the moment ReloadChain detects a cascade-broken prev_hash), `rejected_by` (Nodes → {"none", "chain", "validator", "both"} — latches "both" on every wrong-link reject to record the two-layer defense), `ghost_chain_history` (Nodes → Seq(Block) — append-only legitimate-history record that TamperHistorical does NOT mutate; the INV_AppendOnly witness). Actions modeled: `ProduceBlock(n)` (constructs a block with `prev_hash = head_hash(chains[n])` and a fresh `body_hash` from BodyHashes; appends to chains[n] AND ghost_chain_history[n]; broadcasts to other-node inboxes), `ApplyBlock(n)` (drains pending_inbox head; validates via `prev_hash_ok`; appends on success AND mirrors into ghost_chain_history, drops + latches `rejected_by = "both"` on reject), `TamperHistorical(n)` (adversary mutates an interior block's body_hash; the post-tamper `compute_hash` differs because the pre-image INCLUDES body_hash, breaking the prev_hash cascade at the next block; `ghost_chain_history` is UNCHANGED), `ReloadChain(n)` (the spec-layer projection of `Chain::load`; walks `validate_chain`; latches `load_throws` on prev_hash mismatch — the T-5 boundary catch).

This spec captures the just-shipped R25 `test-chain-prev-hash-link` unit test at the state-machine layer. The analytic source (`src/main.cpp::test-chain-prev-hash-link` at lines 29088..29395 + `tools/test_chain_prev_hash_link.sh`) pins ~22 assertions across 7 scenarios; the TLA+ state-machine layer abstracts the five operational surfaces (chain-layer apply, validator-layer apply, hash injectivity, reload integrity, adversarial tamper cascade) into four actions + seven invariants + two temporal properties:

1. **Happy path (T-1)** is captured by `INV_PrevHashLinkValid`. The chain only grows via ProduceBlock + ApplyBlock, both of which require `prev_hash = head_hash(chains[n])` before appending; the post-condition is the per-block link `chain[i].prev_hash = chain[i-1].compute_hash` on every legitimately-extended chain.

2. **Genesis anchor (T-2)** is captured by `INV_GenesisPrevHashZero`. The chain init seeds with `GenesisBlock` whose `prev_hash = ZeroHash` (the all-zero sentinel — no predecessor). TamperHistorical's quantifier is `i \in 2..Len(chains[n])`, so the genesis block is structurally excluded from tampering.

3. **Two-layer defense (T-3)** is captured by `INV_WrongPrevHashRejected`. The shared `prev_hash_ok` predicate models both the chain-layer (`Chain::append` at `src/chain/chain.cpp:54-58`) and the validator-layer (`BlockValidator::check_prev_hash` at `src/node/validator.cpp:43-48`) gates; ApplyBlock's reject branch latches `rejected_by = "both"` to observe the two-layer defense firing in concert. The defense ensures any regression weakening one gate is caught by the other.

4. **Reload integrity (T-4)** is captured by `INV_ReloadPreservesLinks`. The abstract-hash discipline is purely structural; the in-memory chain and a hypothetical reloaded copy have byte-identical prev_hash linkage. T-4 composes with S-021 (the chain.json wrapping object's head_hash recompute at load time) — INV_4 pins the per-block link discipline so a regression bypassing the head_hash check OR changing compute_hash inputs would still trip.

5. **Cascade detection (T-5)** is captured by `INV_HistoricalTamperCascades` + `PROP_TamperEventuallyDetected`. TamperHistorical's body_hash mutation changes compute_hash (abstract-hash injectivity); `chain[i+1].prev_hash` no longer matches the post-tamper compute_hash; `validate_chain` returns FALSE; ReloadChain latches `load_throws`. The temporal property pins that the cascade is eventually observable.

6. **Empty-prev-hash at height 1 (T-6)** is captured by `INV_WrongPrevHashRejected`. A height-1 block with `prev_hash = ZeroHash` differs from `head_hash(genesis-only-chain) = GenesisBlock.compute_hash` (which is NOT zero — genesis hashes its own index/body_hash/etc. via the BLOCK-tagged tuple); the shared `prev_hash_ok` predicate rejects, and `rejected_by = "both"` records the two-layer defense firing.

7. **Append-only (T-7)** is captured by `INV_AppendOnly` via the ghost-history snapshot. `ghost_chain_history` is updated only by ProduceBlock + ApplyBlock (legitimate extension); TamperHistorical does NOT touch the ghost. In the no-tamper branch, `chains[n] = ghost_chain_history[n]` proves legitimate extension never rewrites earlier blocks — the contract on which fork-resolution and snapshot consistency depend.

**Out of scope** (consistent with the R25 test's documented scope):
- Cryptographic soundness of SHA-256 (A2). The abstract-hash discipline + pre-image injectivity is the spec-layer abstraction; FB23 FrostVerify.tla covers the cryptographic side.
- The C++-side throw-exception semantics. The spec models the chain-state outcome (block dropped from inbox without extending `chains[n]`); the exception-surface invariants live in FB27 JsonValidation.tla (S-018 clear-diagnostic).
- The wrap-on-disk byte format (chain.json head_hash + blocks). The spec abstracts serialization into the pure-function `validate_chain` helper; S-021's chain.json wrapping is FB26 territory.
- Fork-resolution semantics (S-029). The spec is single-chain; `resolve_fork`'s heaviest-sig-set + fewer-aborts + smallest-hash tie-breaker is FA-track territory.
- The specific identity of the field being tampered. FB30's body_hash abstraction collapses ALL compute_hash-contributing fields (timestamp, creators, txs, etc.) into a single opaque body-hash universe; FB29 BlockTimestampMonotonic.tla covers the timestamp-specific cascade as a sibling specialization.

Companion analytic source: `src/main.cpp::test-chain-prev-hash-link` (R25, ~22 assertions across 7 scenarios at lines 29088..29395) + `tools/test_chain_prev_hash_link.sh` (the shell wrapper). This TLA+ spec formalizes the state-machine layer of those assertions: INV_PrevHashLinkValid lifts T-1's happy-path linkage; INV_GenesisPrevHashZero lifts T-2's chain-anchor convention; INV_WrongPrevHashRejected lifts T-3 + T-6's two-layer defense; INV_ReloadPreservesLinks lifts T-4's round-trip identity; INV_HistoricalTamperCascades + PROP_TamperEventuallyDetected lift T-5's cascade; INV_AppendOnly lifts T-7's no-retroactive-rewrite contract.

Cross-reference. FB22 `F2ViewReconciliation.tla` (v2.7 F2 view-reconciliation primitives), FB23 `FrostVerify.tla` (Ed25519 EUF-CMA model — the abstract-sig discipline), FB24 `MakeContribCommitment.tla` (S-030 D2 commit-binding — the distinct-pre-image property this spec's abstract-hash discipline mirrors), FB25 `RateLimiterEviction.tla` (S-014 F-1 lifetime-bound model), FB26 `BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla` (S-021 + S-033 + S-038 composition — sibling state-integrity surface; this spec's INV_HistoricalTamperCascades + PROP_TamperEventuallyDetected compose with FB26's INV_LoadDetectsTampering via the shared prev_hash continuity discipline + the shared `validate_chain` helper), FB27 `JsonValidation.tla` (S-018 clear-diagnostic + defense-in-depth), FB28 `S006ContribMsgEquivocation.tla` (S-006 Phase-1 same-gen detection), FB29 `BlockTimestampMonotonic.tla` (R24A5 timestamp monotonicity + digest-exclusion — closely related sibling; FB29 pins the cascade for the timestamp field specifically, while FB30 generalizes to any compute_hash-contributing field via the body_hash abstraction). FB30 (this spec — the prev_hash chain-link state machine + cascade-detection invariants). Together FB26 + FB29 + FB30 witness the chain-identity surface end-to-end: FB26 covers the state_root + apply-time + load-time integrity gates; FB29 covers the timestamp threading across compute_hash / signing_bytes / compute_block_digest plus the forward-looking strict-monotonic gate; FB30 covers the prev_hash chain-link contract at both the chain-layer and validator-layer gates plus the append-only + reload-preserve + tamper-cascade properties.
### SnapshotIntegrity.tla → FA-Snapshot (S-012 + S-037 + S-038 composition)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `live_chain` (Nodes → Seq(Block) where Block = [index, prev_hash, state_root, txs]), `live_state` (Nodes → [accounts, stakes, registrants, dapp_registry] each a SUBSET of Slots — the four mutable maps that survive across snapshot boundaries and contribute to the a:/s:/r:/d: state_root namespaces), `snapshot_blob` (Nodes → Snapshot ∪ {NoSnapshot} where Snapshot has [tail_chain, serialized_state, head_state_root]), `apply_throws` / `restore_throws` (Nodes → BOOLEAN), `tampered_at` (Nodes → TamperSite where TamperSite = {"none", "chain", "state", "dapp_registry"}) |
| `INV_SnapshotRoundTripPreservesAllNamespaces` | T-S1 composed with T-S2 (10-namespace round-trip + S-037 dapp_registry inclusion). For every node-pair (n, n2) where n2 has successfully restored from n's snapshot (no `restore_throws` latch + `live_chain[n2] = snapshot_blob[n].tail_chain`), the restored `live_state[n2]` equals `snapshot_blob[n].serialized_state` across all four namespaces AND `state_root_of(live_state[n2]) = snapshot_blob[n].head_state_root`. The headline composition: dapp_registry round-trips under the `d:` namespace AND the state_root over all namespaces matches byte-for-byte. The structural witness for "the S-037 closure threads dapp_registry through serialize_state + restore_from_snapshot symmetrically; the post-restore gate at chain.cpp:1893-1911 verifies the recomputed state_root equals the snapshot's stored head_state_root byte-for-byte" — without S-037 the recompute would fail on any DApp-active chain |
| `INV_StateRootGateFiresOnRestoreTamper` | T-S4 (Tamper Detection at Snapshot Boundary). If a node's snapshot has been tampered at state or dapp_registry layer AND another node has installed live_state from the tampered snapshot, then `restore_throws` MUST be TRUE — the contrapositive: if `restore_throws[n2] = FALSE` after installing live_state from a tampered snapshot, then `state_root_of(serialized_state) = head_state_root`, contradicting the tamper. The structural witness for the post-restore recompute-vs-stored gate at chain.cpp:1893-1911 catching any state-modifying tamper that did NOT also re-sign the head_state_root |
| `INV_ProducerSelfApplyConsistentPostS038` | T-S3 (Producer-Side State_Root Wiring / S-038 closure). Across every reachable state, every block in `live_chain[n]` has `state_root` in `{ZeroRoot, state_root_of(head_state(prefix))}` where prefix is the chain up to that block. The post-S-038 invariant: the producer's tentative-chain dry-run at node.cpp:1024-1117 (steps 1-5) guarantees `body.state_root` is populated with the canonical post-apply Merkle root, NOT empty. The pre-S-038 dormant-gate case (where `body.state_root = Hash{}` and the apply-time gate's `if (b.state_root != zero)` short-circuit meant the gate never actually fired on production blocks) is captured by the `ZeroRoot` disjunct; post-S-038 every produced block satisfies the second disjunct |
| `INV_DAppRegistryRoundtrips` | T-S2 standalone (S-037 closure isolated). For every node-pair (n, n2) where n2 has successfully restored n's snapshot AND no tampering was observed, `live_state[n2].dapp_registry = snapshot_blob[n].serialized_state.dapp_registry`. Standalone sub-claim of INV_SnapshotRoundTripPreservesAllNamespaces — called out so a regression that re-removes the `d:` namespace from `Chain::serialize_state` at chain.cpp:1653-1669 would surface as a single-invariant failure in TLC traces (instant regression diagnosis). The structural witness for the S-037 closure: dapp_registry is emitted at serialize AND consumed at restore symmetrically; without the symmetry the recompute gate fires |
| `INV_RestoreDeterminism` | T-S5 (Restore Determinism). For every node-pair (n1, n2): if `snapshot_blob[n1] = snapshot_blob[n2]` AND `live_chain[n1] = live_chain[n2]` AND both have completed restore without throwing, then `live_state[n1] = live_state[n2]`. The structural witness for "restore is a pure function of (snapshot, current_chain) — the C++ `Chain::restore_from_snapshot` has no fresh-randomness inputs". The state-machine projection of byte-determinism: two nodes consuming byte-identical snapshots reach byte-identical post-restore states |
| `INV_NoSilentDivergence` | T-S4 cross-node form (the snapshot-pathway mirror of FB26 BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla's same-named invariant). If two nodes have the same restored chain but different state_roots, at least one of `apply_throws` or `restore_throws` MUST be TRUE — the integrity gates fire before the divergent state can survive at apply time. Restricted to the snapshot pathway via the antecedent's requirement that both nodes have non-empty `live_chain` (i.e., either produced or restored). Composed with FB26's INV_NoSilentDivergence (the chain.json wrap + apply-time pathway), the two invariants together exhaust the state-divergence surface across both at-rest pathways (chain.json save/load AND snapshot serialize/restore) |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-seven specs above). The recommended `SnapshotIntegrity.cfg` (Nodes = {n1, n2}, MaxHeight = 3, Slots = {sl1, sl2}) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under a minute on a single core. The seven-action state machine (ProduceBlock, SerializeSnapshot, RestoreFromSnapshot, ApplyBlockAfterRestore, TamperSnapshot, TamperLiveState, Stutter) exercises every reachable interleaving of producer-side state_root population (S-038 wiring), snapshot emission, cross-node restore with post-restore gate firing, post-restore apply with the S-033 gate firing, and the four adversary surfaces (chain-tamper / state-tamper / dapp_registry-tamper / live-state tamper). Variables modeled: `live_chain` (function `NodeId → Seq(Block)` where Block has [index, prev_hash, state_root, txs] — matches the C++ `std::vector<Block> blocks_` at `include/determ/chain/chain.hpp`), `live_state` (function `NodeId → [accounts, stakes, registrants, dapp_registry]` each a SUBSET of Slots — the four mutable maps that survive across snapshot boundaries and contribute to the a:/s:/r:/d: state_root namespaces; the spec's collapse of the C++ `std::map<std::string, AccountState> accounts_`, `std::map<std::string, StakeEntry> stakes_`, `std::map<std::string, RegistryEntry> registrants_`, `std::map<std::string, DAppEntry> dapp_registry_` into the SUBSET-of-Slots abstraction is the standard FB-track tractability move — distinct contents per namespace produce distinct state_roots by the abstract-hash discriminator), `snapshot_blob` (function `NodeId → Snapshot ∪ {NoSnapshot}` where Snapshot has [tail_chain, serialized_state, head_state_root] — matches the JSON form at chain.cpp:1541-1701; the `head_state_root` field corresponds to the tail-head's `state_root` field stored in the snapshot's tail-header bundle and consumed by the post-restore gate at chain.cpp:1893-1911), `apply_throws` / `restore_throws` (function `NodeId → BOOLEAN` — latching sentinels for the two integrity gates: `apply_throws` for the S-033 apply-time gate at chain.cpp:1421-1446; `restore_throws` for the post-restore state_root recompute gate at chain.cpp:1893-1911), `tampered_at` (function `NodeId → TamperSite` where TamperSite = {"none", "chain", "state", "dapp_registry"} — spec-only audit field tracking the most-recent adversary site; the dapp_registry branch is called out separately so a regression that re-removes the `d:` namespace from `Chain::serialize_state` surfaces as a tamper-detection failure on this specific site). Actions modeled: `ProduceBlock(n)` (the C++ Node::try_finalize_round at node.cpp:1024-1117 — five steps collapsed into a single atomic action: build_body with state_root=Hash{}, tentative-chain dry-run, populate `body.state_root` via the tentative chain's `compute_state_root()` (the S-038 wiring), apply on live chain, advance. INV_ProducerSelfApplyConsistentPostS038 is the structural witness that step 4 always fires — every produced block carries a non-zero `state_root`), `SerializeSnapshot(n)` (Chain::serialize_state at chain.cpp:1541-1701 — emits the four-map state shape verbatim plus tail_chain and head_state_root; pre-S-037 the `dapp_registry` field was absent, the spec models the post-S-037 form with all four maps emitted; INV_DAppRegistryRoundtrips locks in the S-037 closure), `RestoreFromSnapshot(n2)` (Chain::restore_from_snapshot at chain.cpp:1703-1932 — replays tail_chain, rehydrates serialized_state, recomputes state_root_of(restored) and compares to head_state_root via the post-restore gate at chain.cpp:1893-1911; on mismatch latches `restore_throws[n2]` and leaves the chain uninstalled), `ApplyBlockAfterRestore(n2)` (Chain::apply_transactions S-033 gate at chain.cpp:1421-1446 — the post-restore apply path; declared state_root must match computed post-apply state_root or `apply_throws` latches), `TamperSnapshot(n)` (three-disjunct adversary surface: (a) interior tail-chain block, (b) state-namespace contents, (c) dapp_registry specifically — the S-037 closure surface; the wrap header's `head_state_root` is NOT patched, so the next RestoreFromSnapshot MUST detect by recompute-vs-stored mismatch), `TamperLiveState(n)` (at-rest tamper of live state between serialize and restore — mutates live_state.accounts; exercises the cross-node INV_NoSilentDivergence: producer's drift relative to a previously-emitted snapshot is observable at the state-root layer).

This spec captures the post-S-037 / post-S-038 snapshot-pathway state-integrity surface at the state-machine layer. The analytic proof (T-S1..T-S5 in `S033StateRootNamespaceCoverage.md` §1 / §4.5 + the FA-Apply-12 sub-theorem in `AppliedReceiptRestore.md`) establishes that three independently-shipped mechanisms compose:

1. **S-033 (state_root commitment)**: `Block::signing_bytes` binds `state_root` under the zero-skip backward-compat shim. The apply-time gate at chain.cpp:1421-1446 recomputes the state root post-apply and compares to the block's declared `state_root`, throwing on mismatch.

2. **S-037 (dapp_registry + applied_inbound_receipts snapshot coverage)**: the `d:` and `i:` namespaces contribute leaves to the state_root Merkle commitment. Pre-S-037 the snapshot serializer omitted these; a DApp-active chain's snapshot would carry the tail head's correct state_root in JSON, but `restore_from_snapshot` would rehydrate a chain whose recomputed state_root differed — the post-restore gate at chain.cpp:1893-1911 would loud-fail. S-037 added both namespaces to `serialize_state` + `restore_from_snapshot` with the full set of fields needed to reproduce the value-hash byte-for-byte.

3. **S-038 (producer-side state_root population)**: pre-S-038 every produced block had `body.state_root = Hash{}`; the apply-time gate's `if (b.state_root != zero)` short-circuit meant the receiver-side check was DORMANT on production blocks. S-038 added the tentative-chain dry-run pattern at node.cpp:1024-1117 so every produced block carries a non-zero `state_root`.

The TLA+ state-machine layer abstracts these into seven actions + six invariants:

- **Ten-namespace round-trip** is captured by `INV_SnapshotRoundTripPreservesAllNamespaces`. The four-map state shape `[accounts, stakes, registrants, dapp_registry]` is the post-S-037 mutable-state surface that contributes to the state_root commitment via the a:/s:/r:/d: namespaces; the remaining six namespaces (i:/b:/m:/p:/k:/c:) collapse cleanly into the same SUBSET-of-Slots abstraction under `state_root_of`'s tuple discriminator (the abstract-hash discipline used by FB26 BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla).

- **DApp registry round-trip (S-037 closure)** is captured by `INV_DAppRegistryRoundtrips`, called out as a standalone sub-claim so a regression that re-removes the `d:` namespace from `Chain::serialize_state` surfaces as a single-invariant failure in TLC traces.

- **Producer-side state_root wiring (S-038 closure)** is captured by `INV_ProducerSelfApplyConsistentPostS038`. The post-S-038 contract: every produced block carries a non-zero `state_root` populated via the tentative-chain dry-run.

- **Tamper detection at snapshot boundary** is captured by `INV_StateRootGateFiresOnRestoreTamper` (post-restore recompute fires on any state-modifying tamper) + `INV_NoSilentDivergence` (cross-node form — divergent state_roots imply at least one throw-gate latched).

- **Restore determinism** is captured by `INV_RestoreDeterminism`. Restore is a pure function of (snapshot, current_chain).

The abstract-hash model (`state_root_of` as a pure function returning a tagged tuple over the four namespace contents) is the standard TLA+ projection of A2 (SHA-256 collision resistance) — distinct pre-images map to distinct outputs by tuple inequality. The cryptographic tightness is FA-track territory (Preliminaries.md §2.1).

**Out of scope** (consistent with `S033StateRootNamespaceCoverage.md` §6 + this spec's §11 header comment):

- The basic apply-determinism invariant (covered by FA-Apply-1 / FB5 AccountState.tla). FB31's `apply` operator is the spec-layer projection; the underlying determinism property is FB5 territory.
- The cross-shard receipt dedup invariant (covered by FB17 AppliedReceiptRestore.tla / FA-Apply-12). FB31 composes this via INV_SnapshotRoundTripPreservesAllNamespaces' `i:` namespace coverage (collapsed into the SUBSET-of-Slots abstraction).
- The chain.json wrap (FB26 BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla territory). FB31's RestoreFromSnapshot models the in-memory snapshot restore path; the disk-level chain.json wrap + head_hash check is the parallel state-integrity boundary covered by FB26.
- The byte-level codec round-trip (the JSON encoding / decoding fidelity). The `serialized_state` field is modeled as a TLA+ record; the codec is FA-track territory (`tools/test_state_root_namespaces.sh`, 12 assertions).
- Pre-S-038 historical blocks bypass the apply-time gate (intentional backward-compat via the zero-skip shim). INV_ProducerSelfApplyConsistentPostS038 captures this via the `b.state_root = ZeroRoot` disjunct; post-S-038 every produced block has non-zero state_root by construction.
- Ed25519 EUF-CMA / SHA-256 collision resistance bounds (the cryptographic tightness is FA-track territory).

Companion analytic proofs: `docs/proofs/S033StateRootNamespaceCoverage.md` (the ten-namespace coverage theorem T-1..T-5; FB31 lifts T-5 Snapshot Round-Trip Soundness to the state-machine layer with the cross-node restore + adversarial tamper enumeration), `docs/proofs/AppliedReceiptRestore.md` (FA-Apply-12 — the receipt dedup-set restore correctness sub-theorem; FB17 AppliedReceiptRestore.tla covers the receipt-set's standalone state machine; FB31 unifies this with the broader 10-namespace surface via INV_SnapshotRoundTripPreservesAllNamespaces' `i:` namespace coverage), `docs/proofs/BlockchainStateIntegrity.md` (the composition theorem T-1..T-5; FB26 BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla covers the chain.json wrap + apply-time gate composition; FB31 is the snapshot-pathway sibling), `docs/proofs/AccountStateInvariants.md` (FA-Apply-1 — apply determinism, the prerequisite for restore equivalence).

Cross-reference. FB5 `AccountState.tla` (FA-Apply-1 — apply determinism, the load-bearing input to INV_RestoreDeterminism and the ApplyBlockAfterRestore action's determinism contract), FB6 `Snapshot.tla` (FA-Apply-2 — the basic snapshot/restore state machine; FB31's foundation. FB6 collapses the 10 state_root namespaces to two — `a:` balances+nonces and `b:` accumulated counters — per its file header; FB31 extends to the full four-map surface that contributes to the a:/s:/r:/d: namespaces plus the SUBSET-of-Slots projection for the remaining six namespaces, the dapp_registry round-trip via INV_DAppRegistryRoundtrips, and the producer-side state_root wiring via INV_ProducerSelfApplyConsistentPostS038), FB17 `AppliedReceiptRestore.tla` (FA-Apply-12 — the `i:` namespace's standalone snapshot lifecycle, the S-037 closure witness for the receipt dedup-set; FB31 composes this with the nine other namespaces via the SUBSET-of-Slots abstraction), FB26 `BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla` (chain.json wrap + apply-time gate — S-021 + S-033 + S-038 composition; FB31 is the snapshot-pathway sibling; FB26's INV_NoSilentDivergence and FB31's INV_NoSilentDivergence together exhaust the state-divergence surface across both at-rest pathways). FB31 (this spec — the post-S-037 / post-S-038 snapshot integrity surface). Together FB6 + FB17 + FB26 + FB31 witness the full state-integrity surface at the state-machine layer: FB6 is the basic snapshot/restore foundation; FB17 is the cross-shard receipt-set sub-claim; FB26 covers the chain.json + apply-time gates; FB31 closes the snapshot-pathway gap to the post-S-037 + post-S-038 closure.
### CrossShardReceiptRoundtrip.tla → FA-CrossShard (composition of FA-Apply-9 + FA-Apply-12 + FA-Apply-13)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `INV_TypeOK` | shape of `live_state_src` (SrcState = [balance: Domains → Nat, outbound_emitted_count: Nat, height: Nat]), `live_state_dst` (DstState = [balance: Domains → Nat, applied_inbound_receipts: SUBSET DedupKey, inbound_first_seen: DedupKey → Nat, height: Nat]), `gossip_inflight` / `inbound_pool_dst` / `eligible_for_apply` (Seq(Receipt) — the three transit queues), `snapshot_blob_src` / `snapshot_blob_dst` (per-shard snapshot or NoSnapshot sentinel), `apply_throws` (BOOLEAN — latches on dedup violation or apply-time invariant breach) |
| `INV_NoDoubleCredit` | T-RT4 (apply-side dedup, composition of FA-Apply-9 / T-R1 + T-R2 from FB14). For every receipt R applied at destination, R.dedup_key is in `applied_inbound_receipts` AND no two `ApplyEligibleReceiptOnDst` steps for the same dedup_key both fire the first-credit branch. The structural witness is the if/then/else split in `ApplyEligibleReceiptOnDst`: the fresh branch requires `k \notin applied_inbound_receipts`, so a second apply for the same key MUST route to the duplicate branch. Matches `chain.cpp:1363-1381` + the dedup check helper at `chain.cpp:204-206` |
| `INV_TimeOrderedAdmission` | T-RT3 (CROSS_SHARD_RECEIPT_LATENCY=3 wait, S-016 Option 2 partial closure). For every receipt in `eligible_for_apply`, `first_seen[k] + LATENCY <= dst.height`. The admission wait is enforced; receipts cannot short-circuit the latency gate. Matches `node.cpp:1577-1597` (`Node::inbound_receipts_eligible_for_inclusion`) and the production constant `CROSS_SHARD_RECEIPT_LATENCY = 3` at `node.cpp:1574`. v2.7 F2 (Option 1) closes fully via the Phase-1 intersection rule — composition with FB22 F2ViewReconciliation.tla is future-work |
| `INV_OutboundDebitPrecedesInboundCredit` | T-RT1 (FA7 Lemma L-7.3 state-form witness). `outbound_emitted_count >= |applied_inbound_receipts|` — every applied receipt corresponds to an emitted-on-source step, and the source-side debit is an atomic part of `EmitOutboundReceipt`. The strict-precedence claim is structural: `EmitOutboundReceipt` atomically increments `outbound_emitted_count` AND applies the source-side debit; the corresponding destination credit is at least one Gossip + Admit + Apply step later. The state-form witness for the temporal-precedence theorem |
| `INV_A1SourceDstComposition` | T-RT2 (cross-shard A1 supply identity). `Sum(src balances) + Sum(dst balances) + Sum(in-flight receipt amounts) <= InitialTotalSupply`. The receipt-as-conserved-quantity contract spanning source debit, transit, time-order admission queue, and destination credit. The strict-inequality form accommodates the fee component (fee stays on source for creator distribution per FB10; the receipt amount is the cross-shard supply movement). Matches the A1 algebra at `chain.cpp:1397-1404` lifted to the cross-shard composition |
| `INV_DedupSetSurvivesSnapshot` | T-RT5 (FA-Apply-12 / T-AR3 lifted, S-037 closure). For every snapshot taken at destination, the post-restore `applied_inbound_receipts` set is a superset of the snapshot's saved set. Pre-S-037 the snapshot lacked the `i:` namespace; `restore_from_snapshot` would silently drop the dedup-set and allow a re-injected receipt to credit a second time. Post-S-037 the live set is always a superset — `RestoreFromSnapshot` preserves verbatim. Matches `chain.cpp:330-344` (`i:` namespace emission in `serialize_state`) + `chain.cpp:1778-1783` (consumer in `restore_from_snapshot`) |
| `INV_ReplayDetected` | T-RT6 (replay catches at apply, composed adversary). For every receipt-dedup_key k in `applied_inbound_receipts`, no spurious balance increment is reachable from any transit queue's apply path. The `AttemptReplayReceipt` adversary's state-form witness: re-injecting an already-applied receipt into `gossip_inflight` flows through the normal pipeline and the eventual `ApplyEligibleReceiptOnDst` fires the duplicate branch — no balance mutation, no throw, no orphaned receipt. The structural impossibility of double-credit under replay |
| `INV_NoSilentDivergence` | T-RT7 (composition no-stuck-receipt). `outbound_emitted_count >= |applied_inbound_receipts|` (every applied receipt came from an emission) AND every emitted receipt is accounted for as either applied OR in one of the three transit queues. The cross-shard composition's no-receipt-lost claim — every emission has a trackable destination (apply OR dedup-skip) and no receipt is silently dropped between source debit and destination credit |
| `INV_SourceA1OutboundApply` | T-RT8 (FA-Apply-13 / T-O1 + T-O3 state-form witness). Per-domain balance non-negativity across both shards: `\A d : src.balance[d] >= 0 AND dst.balance[d] >= 0`. The action-level T-O1 + T-O3 form is structurally enforced by `EmitOutboundReceipt`'s EXCEPT clause (which mutates only `balance[from]`; the to-domain on source is UNCHANGED — the destination credit lives on the OTHER shard via the receipt path); the state-level invariant is the standing claim that no domain's balance ever wraps or goes negative |
| `PROP_EventualReceiptApply` (temporal) | under fairness on `GossipReceiptArrival` + `AdmitTimeOrderedEligibleReceipts` + `ApplyEligibleReceiptOnDst`, every emitted receipt is eventually applied (fresh-credit branch) OR rejected for dedup (duplicate-skip branch). State-form: a non-empty `gossip_inflight` queue leads to either an empty queue (drained) OR the apply path firing. The no-receipt-stuck-forever liveness contract |
| `PROP_NoLossOfFunds` (temporal) | under fairness, the A1 cross-shard supply identity is eventually re-established after every `EmitOutboundReceipt`: the receipt is either applied (in-flight term → destination balance) OR silently dropped per the dedup gate. The refund path for stuck receipts is v2.X future-work (per S-016 partial closure narrative — out of scope for this spec); `INV_A1SourceDstComposition`'s in-flight component captures the transient state |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-five specs above). The recommended `CrossShardReceiptRoundtrip.cfg` (`Domains = {d_src, d_dst}`, `Hashes = {h1, h2}`, `Shards = {sh_src, sh_dst}`, `MaxAmount = 3`, `MaxFee = 0`, `InitialBalance = 10`, `MaxHeight = 4`, `LATENCY = 1`) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under a minute on a single core. `LATENCY = 1` (relaxed from production `CROSS_SHARD_RECEIPT_LATENCY = 3` at `node.cpp:1574`) keeps the TLC state space tractable while preserving the time-order-gate semantics; production-equivalent runs with `LATENCY = 3` are feasible at MaxHeight=6+ on multi-core TLC. Seven actions cover the cross-shard cycle: `EmitOutboundReceipt(from, to, amount, fee, tx_h)` (source-side cross-shard TRANSFER apply at chain.cpp:752-766), `GossipReceiptArrival` (head of gossip_inflight → inbound_pool_dst with first_seen latched), `AdmitTimeOrderedEligibleReceipts` (head of inbound_pool_dst → eligible_for_apply if `first_seen + LATENCY <= dst.height` — mirrors `Node::inbound_receipts_eligible_for_inclusion`), `ApplyEligibleReceiptOnDst` (the if/then/else dedup-on-apply branch — fresh: credit + insert; duplicate: silent skip — chain.cpp:1363-1381), `SerializeSnapshotSrc` / `SerializeSnapshotDst` (per-shard snapshot emission; dst snapshot binds `applied_inbound_receipts` + `inbound_first_seen` — the S-037 `i:` namespace), `RestoreFromSnapshotSrc` / `RestoreFromSnapshotDst` (per-shard restore), `AttemptReplayReceipt(r)` (adversary re-injects an already-applied or in-transit receipt into gossip_inflight).
