The replay adversary's structural defeat is the `if/then/else` split in `ApplyEligibleReceiptOnDst`: the fresh branch's pre-condition `k \notin applied_inbound_receipts` blocks re-firing on a previously-applied dedup_key, routing the apply to the silent-skip branch. `MaxFee = 0` in the default cfg lets the A1 algebra collapse cleanly to the receipt-amount sum (the fee-paying case is FB10 territory and introduces an additive TotalFeesPaid term tracked separately).

This spec is the cross-shard composition lift of FB14 (CrossShardReceiptDedup — destination dedup primitive), FB17 (AppliedReceiptRestore — snapshot lifecycle of the destination dedup set), and FB18 (CrossShardOutboundApply — source-side debit primitive). Where each predecessor covers a slice of the cross-shard lifecycle in isolation, FB32 composes the four mechanisms (V12 source-emit + gossip transit + S-016 time-order admission + FA-Apply-9 dst-dedup + FA-Apply-12 snapshot-survival) into a single state machine. The eight invariants pin the cross-shard cycle at every transition: source debit precedes destination credit (T-RT1); A1 holds with an in-flight term that accounts for transit-receipts (T-RT2); admission waits `CROSS_SHARD_RECEIPT_LATENCY` blocks (T-RT3); apply is dedup-safe (T-RT4); restore preserves the dedup set (T-RT5); replay is caught (T-RT6); no silent divergence is reachable (T-RT7); source-side debit equals exactly `amount + fee` (T-RT8). Together FB14 + FB17 + FB18 + FB32 witness the cross-shard receipt-as-conserved-quantity contract at the state-machine layer: FB14 + FB17 + FB18 each cover a sub-claim in isolation; FB32 closes the cross-shard receipt lifecycle gap by composing them with the source-emit + gossip + time-order pipeline that FA7 implicitly relies on but no prior FB-track spec covered end-to-end.

**Out of scope** (consistent with this spec's §9 header comment):

- Refund path for stuck receipts. v2.X future-work (per S-016 partial closure narrative); the model captures the transient state via `INV_A1SourceDstComposition`'s in-flight component but does not model an explicit refund action.
- Cryptographic receipt-hash binding. FA7 / FB23 FrostVerify-style territory. The wire-level cryptographic admission (signature verification, K-of-K committee sign-off, V13 dst-side dedup at admission) is abstracted via the action discipline (`GossipReceiptArrival` models successful wire-level admission).
- v2.7 F2 Option 1 intersection rule. The model implements S-016 Option 2 (time-ordered admission); v2.7 F2 closes fully via the Phase-1 intersection rule. FB22 F2ViewReconciliation.tla covers F2 in isolation; the composition with FB32 is future-work once F2 ships.
- Per-block apply-loop composition. FB20 MultiEventComposition territory. FB32 zooms in on the receipt-only state machine; the per-block composition with other event classes (transfers, aborts, equivocations, subsidies) is the FB20 lift.
- Cross-shard fee accounting. The fee accrues to source-side creators per FB10; the receipt's amount field is the cross-shard supply movement. The A1 algebra collapses the fee component into the source-balance reduction with a strict inequality (`TotalLiveBalance + TotalInFlight <= InitialTotalSupply`).

Companion analytic proofs: `docs/proofs/CrossShardReceiptDedup.md` (FA-Apply-9 — destination-side dedup contract; FB14 is the standalone state-machine companion), `docs/proofs/AppliedReceiptRestore.md` (FA-Apply-12 — snapshot-pathway survival of the dedup set; FB17 is the standalone companion), `docs/proofs/CrossShardOutboundApply.md` (FA-Apply-13 — source-side debit contract; FB18 is the standalone companion), `docs/proofs/CrossShardReceipts.md` (FA7 — high-level cross-shard correctness theorem; FB32 unifies the three sub-theorems at the state-machine layer).

Cross-reference. FB14 `CrossShardReceiptDedup.tla` (destination-side dedup primitive in isolation; FB32 composes), FB17 `AppliedReceiptRestore.tla` (snapshot-pathway survival in isolation; FB32 composes via `INV_DedupSetSurvivesSnapshot`), FB18 `CrossShardOutboundApply.tla` (source-side debit primitive in isolation; FB32 composes via `INV_SourceA1OutboundApply` + `INV_OutboundDebitPrecedesInboundCredit`), FB6 `Snapshot.tla` (basic snapshot/restore foundation; FB32's snapshot actions follow the same shape). FB32 (this spec — the composed cross-shard receipt lifecycle). Together FB14 + FB17 + FB18 + FB32 witness the full cross-shard receipt-as-conserved-quantity surface at the state-machine layer.
### MempoolAdmission.tla → FA-S008 (bounded mempool admission composition of S-008 + S-002 + FA-Apply-3 + FB23)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `mempool` (Seq(Tx) where Tx = [hash, from, nonce, fee, sig_valid]), `mempool_cap` (Nat — operator-tunable cap; mirrors `MEMPOOL_MAX_TXS = 10000`), `applied_nonces` (Domains → Nat — per-account applied frontier; mirrors `chain_.next_nonce(d)`), `rejection_log` (Seq(Rejection) where Rejection = [tx, reason] and reason ∈ {"cap_full", "bad_sig", "stale_nonce", "future_nonce", "duplicate"}) |
| `INV_MempoolBounded` | T-MA1 (Bounded Mempool, S-008 headline witness). `Len(mempool) <= mempool_cap` at every reachable state. Structural argument: `AdmitTransaction` (5b) eviction branch strictly preserves the cap (evict-one-insert-one), `AdmitTransaction` (5a/6) honors the cap as a pre-condition, RBF replace at (3b) preserves the cap (in-place swap), `AdjustCap` requires `new_cap >= Len(mempool)`. The S-008 closure: an adversarial flood cannot blow the cap past its operator-configured ceiling. Maps to `Node::mempool_admit_check` global-cap branch at `src/node/node.cpp:1980-1992` + `Node::mempool_make_room_for` at lines 2001-2017 |
| `INV_NoStaleAdmission` | T-MA2 (No Stale Admission). No tx in mempool has `tx.nonce < applied_nonces[tx.from]`. Two-stage defense: `AdmitTransaction` (1) rejects stale-nonce at intake; `EvictStale` sweeps any tx that becomes stale post-admission (when `ApplyBlock` advances the frontier past it). Composes with FA-Apply-3 monotonicity (`INV_NonceMonotonic`): once-advanced, frontier never retreats, so a swept-stale tx cannot become re-admittable. Maps to the stale-nonce drop at `src/node/node.cpp:2022-2023` + the sweep loop at `src/node/node.cpp:1796-1803` |
| `INV_NoDuplicateAccountNonce` | T-MA3 (No Duplicate (Account, Nonce)). For every (from, nonce) pair, at most one tx in mempool. The RBF semantics: same-slot submissions replace rather than coexist (via `AdmitTransaction` (3b)'s in-place swap or `OverwriteSameAccountSameNonce`'s standalone form); cross-sender coincidence is structurally permitted (different `from` values are distinct slots). Maps to the `is_replace` short-circuit at `src/node/node.cpp:1965-1967` + the RBF tie-break at `src/node/node.cpp:2041-2043` |
| `INV_RejectionLogCorrectness` | T-MA4 (Rejection-Log Correctness). Every rejection in the audit trail has reason ∈ {"cap_full", "bad_sig", "stale_nonce", "future_nonce", "duplicate"}. The five-bucket taxonomy exhausts the admission-check decision tree; every adversary input that fails admission falls into exactly one bucket. Structural argument: `AdmitTransaction`'s seven disjuncts cover the universe of (tx, state) inputs, and each rejection-emitting disjunct (1, 2, 3a, 4, 5a) labels its log entry with one of the five reasons. Maps to the error-string returns at `src/node/node.cpp::mempool_admit_check` lines 1971-1973 + 1987-1990 (plus the implicit silent-drop branches in `Node::on_tx`) |
| `INV_SigValidityNecessary` | T-MA5 (Sig-Validity Necessary, S-002 composition with S-008). Every tx currently in mempool has a valid signature under the abstract sig verifier (modeled via the FB23 FrostVerify-style boolean precondition `sig_valid`). Pre-S-002 admission could land bad-sig txs; post-S-002 every code path through `AdmitTransaction`'s success branches requires `tx.sig_valid = TRUE`. Composes with FB23 T-1 (verification soundness): a tx in mempool has a valid sig AND a valid sig implies the holder of the corresponding key signed the tx ⇒ no forged-sig tx ever reaches `Node::build_body`. Maps to `Node::on_tx::verify_tx_signature_locked` at `src/node/node.cpp:2025-2028` + the RPC sibling at `src/node/node.cpp:3164-3167` |
| `INV_NonceMonotonic` | FA-Apply-3 sub-claim (per-account nonce monotonicity, direct lift of FB7 Nonce.tla's `Inv_NonceMonotonic`). `applied_nonces[d]` is monotone non-decreasing across every `[Next]_vars` step. The structural witness is the EXCEPT clause in `ApplyBlock` which uses `@ + 1` (Nat-typed; monotone non-decreasing by construction); all other actions preserve `applied_nonces`. The load-bearing input to `INV_NoStaleAdmission`'s two-stage defense. Maps to the `sender.next_nonce++` advance in `Chain::apply_transactions` at `src/chain/chain.cpp:739`+ |
| `PROP_EventualAdmissionOrRejection` (temporal) | every transaction submission attempt eventually lands in mempool OR has an entry in rejection_log. The no-stuck-in-limbo liveness contract: a tx cannot be lost between the admission gate's decision and the audit log. The structural argument: `AdmitTransaction`'s seven disjuncts cover the universe of (tx, state) inputs; under fairness, every submitted tx routes to one of the two collections (mempool or rejection_log) |
| `PROP_MempoolEventuallyDrains` (temporal) | under fairness on `ApplyBlock`, a non-empty mempool with an applicable tx (nonce matching the per-sender applied frontier) eventually shrinks. Captured as a leads-to: a tx in mempool with `tx.nonce = applied_nonces[tx.from]` eventually leaves mempool (drained by `ApplyBlock`, replaced by `OverwriteSameAccountSameNonce`, or swept by `EvictStale`). The producer-side block-build progress guarantee |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-five specs above). The recommended `MempoolAdmission.cfg` (`Domains = {d1, d2}`, `Hashes = {h1, h2, h3, h4}`, `MaxNonce = 3`, `MaxFee = 3`, `Cap = 3`) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under a minute on a single core. `Cap = 3` is the smallest value that lets the global-cap eviction branch fire while still leaving room for fresh-admit traces; `MaxFee = 3` gives four distinct fee tiers so the RBF tie-break + fee-priority eviction tie-break can both surface non-trivially; `MaxNonce = 3` is enough to exercise `ApplyBlock` advancing `applied_nonces` across multiple steps so `INV_NonceMonotonic` + `EvictStale`'s surface are both reachable. Six actions cover the admission / apply / sweep / RBF / cap-tuning surfaces: `AdmitTransaction(tx)` (the unified five-clause admission gate with seven disjuncts covering stale-nonce / bad-sig / RBF-lose / RBF-win / per-sender-quota / cap-full-reject / cap-full-evict / happy-path), `ApplyBlock` (drains one nonce-matching tx and advances the per-sender frontier — collapses build_body + apply into a single atomic action), `EvictStale` (sweeps a tx whose nonce has fallen behind the frontier — mirrors the inline cleanup at `src/node/node.cpp:1798-1803`), `OverwriteSameAccountSameNonce(tx_new)` (standalone form of the RBF replace branch — exposed separately so `INV_NoDuplicateAccountNonce` is observable at TLC trace granularity), `AdjustCap(new_cap)` (operator-side parameter change; modeled to ensure a regression that shrinks the cap below `Len(mempool)` surfaces as an `INV_MempoolBounded` failure), `Stutter` (bounds TLC state space).

This spec captures the S-008 closure (bounded mempool with operator-configurable cap + per-sender quota + fee-priority eviction) at the state-machine layer, composing it with the FA-Apply-3 nonce gate (FB7 sibling), the FB23 FrostVerify abstract-sig precondition (S-002 closure), and the RBF (replace-by-fee) tie-break that `Node::on_tx` inherits. The seven invariants pin the admission discipline at every transition: cap is bounded (T-MA1); no stale admission (T-MA2); no duplicate (account, nonce) (T-MA3); every rejection is labeled with one of five documented reasons (T-MA4); every admitted tx has a valid signature (T-MA5); the apply frontier is monotone (FA-Apply-3 sub-claim). Together with the two temporal properties — `PROP_EventualAdmissionOrRejection` (no-stuck-in-limbo) + `PROP_MempoolEventuallyDrains` (producer-side progress) — the eight-property bundle covers the safety + liveness of the mempool admission surface.

**Out of scope** (consistent with this spec's §9 header comment):

- Per-tx-type apply semantics (TRANSFER / REGISTER / STAKE / etc.). FB5 AccountState.tla + FB8 StakeLifecycle.tla + FB9 DAppRegistry.tla territory. FB33's `ApplyBlock` action collapses per-tx-type routing into a single "drain head + advance nonce" abstract action; the per-type body is the downstream FB-track sibling's domain.
- Cross-shard mempool composition. Each shard has an independent mempool; the multi-shard composition is FB32 CrossShardReceiptRoundtrip.tla territory (the receipt-level state-machine surface). FB33 models a single-shard mempool.
- Wire-level gossip propagation. The gossip path admission gate is identical to the RPC path admission gate (both call `Node::mempool_admit_check`); the wire-level cryptographic-binding side is FA7 / FB23 territory.
- Mempool encryption / privacy. Out of v1 scope (future-work under v2.22 Privacy).
- Runtime-tunable cap. The C++ side has `MEMPOOL_MAX_TXS` as a compile-time `constexpr` at `include/determ/node/node.hpp:459`; the `AdjustCap` action models the operator's recompile-and-redeploy with a smaller cap. Future-work: runtime-tunable cap via the PARAM_CHANGE governance subsystem (FB13 GovernanceParamChange.tla territory if extended).
- Quantitative far-future-nonce attack bounds. The spec models the per-sender quota as the implicit far-future ceiling; the production constant `MEMPOOL_MAX_PER_SENDER = 100` means an adversary can pipeline up to 100 nonces ahead of the current frontier per sender, which is the operator-tuned tradeoff between honest pipelining and attacker mempool occupation. The `"future_nonce"` bucket in `RejectionReason` captures this surface; a TLC trace that hits the per-sender quota produces a `"future_nonce"` rejection.

Companion analytic proofs: `docs/SECURITY.md` §S-008 (the bounded mempool closure narrative — operator-configurable cap + fee-priority eviction + per-sender quota together constitute the S-008 mitigation; `INV_MempoolBounded` + `INV_NoStaleAdmission` + `INV_RejectionLogCorrectness` are the three sub-mechanism witnesses at the state-machine layer), `docs/proofs/NonceMonotonicity.md` (FA-Apply-3 — the per-account nonce monotonicity theorem; `INV_NonceMonotonic` is the direct lift), `docs/proofs/FrostVerifyDelegation.md` (FB23 T-1 verification soundness; `INV_SigValidityNecessary` composes), `docs/proofs/S002-Mempool-Sig-Verify.md` (the S-002 closure paired with the `binary_codec::decode_tx_frame` integer-bounds tightening; the bad-sig rejection branch of `AdmitTransaction` is the S-002 enforcement point).

Cross-reference. FB7 `Nonce.tla` (per-account nonce gate in isolation — apply-layer focus; FB33 composes FB7's nonce gate with the S-008 mempool admission state machine — the two specs are stacked, FB33's mempool feeds FB7's applied layer), FB23 `FrostVerify.tla` (FROST-Ed25519 verify soundness — `INV_SigValidityNecessary` is the mempool-level consumer), FB20 `MultiEventComposition.tla` (composed per-block apply pipeline — FB33's `ApplyBlock` action is the upstream feed to FB20's per-event composition; the two specs cover disjoint pre-/post-apply phases). FB33 (this spec — the bounded-mempool admission state machine; the S-008 + S-002 composition at the mempool layer). Together FB7 + FB20 + FB23 + FB33 witness the tx-lifecycle from gossip-arrival → mempool-admission → block-build → apply at the state-machine layer.
### EpochCommitteeRotation.tla → FA-Rotation (cross-epoch committee rotation composition of S-020 + S-024 + FA1 + FA8)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `epoch` (Nat ∈ 0..MaxEpoch — current epoch counter), `committee_history` (function `{0..epoch} → SUBSET ValidatorPool` — per-epoch K-committee record), `beacon_history` (function `{0..epoch+1} → BeaconValues` — per-epoch beacon feeding the epoch_committee_seed; BeaconUpdate may advance one step ahead of AdvanceEpoch modeling the chain accumulating randomness for the next epoch's seed), `active_validators` (SUBSET ValidatorPool — currently registered validators, mutated by RegisterValidator / DeregisterValidator), `selected_from` (function `{0..epoch} → SUBSET ValidatorPool` — ghost snapshot of active_validators at the moment committee_history[e] was drawn; required for the deterministic-selection invariant's antecedent since the live active_validators may have evolved post-selection via Register/Deregister) |
| `INV_CommitteeSizeIsK` | T-ER2 (Committee Size). Every committee in `committee_history` has cardinality `K` when the active pool at the time of selection had at least K members; otherwise equals the full active set (the under-quorum branch where R7 UnderQuorumMerge kicks in). The structural witness: `EpochCommitteeSelect`'s `effective_k = min(k, |pool|)` computation picks the exact target cardinality; the candidates set is non-empty by construction; CHOOSE returns a member of cardinality `effective_k`. The C++ correspondent is `select_m_creators` at `src/crypto/random.cpp:70-100` (the hybrid Fisher-Yates K-of-N selector that throws on `node_count < m` at lines 71-72; returns exactly m indices via either rejection sampling at K << N or partial-FY at K → N) — S-020 closure |
| `INV_CommitteeSubsetActive` | T-ER3 (Active-Set Discipline). Every committee member at epoch e was in `active_validators` at the moment of the AdvanceEpoch action that drew that epoch's committee. The ghost field `selected_from[e]` captures the live active_validators at the AdvanceEpoch firing; no historical pool is consulted by EpochCommitteeSelect. The structural witness: AdvanceEpoch passes active_validators to EpochCommitteeSelect, which returns a SUBSET of its first argument; the selected_from snapshot is set atomically with committee_history so the lookup is sound. Zombie committees (members who deregistered before the epoch began) and ghost committees (members who never registered) are structurally impossible. The C++ correspondent is `validator.cpp::check_creator_selection` at lines 88-132 (the receiver-side cross-check that every block's committee matches the deterministic draw from `epoch_committee_seed(epoch_rand, shard_id)` over `eligible_in_region(committee_region_)`) |
| `INV_DeterministicSelection` | T-ER1 (Deterministic Selection). For every pair (e1, e2) in the domain of `committee_history` with `beacon_history[e1] = beacon_history[e2]` AND `selected_from[e1] = selected_from[e2]`, the committees are byte-identical: `committee_history[e1] = committee_history[e2]`. State-form witness of the EpochCommitteeSelect's purity — required for cross-node consensus convergence under the same chain head (every node consuming the same epoch_rand + shard_id + active set reproduces the same committee). The structural witness: EpochCommitteeSelect's CHOOSE-over-tagged-tuple discriminator is deterministic on `(pool, beacon, k)`; the same triple ALWAYS picks the same SUBSET. The C++ correspondent is `crypto::epoch_committee_seed(epoch_rand, shard_id)` at `src/crypto/random.cpp:169-175` composed with `select_m_creators` — the SHA-256-derived randomness ensures every node sees the same `random_state` and picks the same indices (S-020 + Preliminaries §2.3 A3 CSPRNG uniformity) |
| `INV_HistoryMonotone` | T-ER4 (History Monotonicity). `committee_history` only grows across AdvanceEpoch actions; existing entries are byte-identical across all reachable states. Stronger form pinned: `DOMAIN committee_history = 0..epoch` AND `committee_history[e] = EpochCommitteeSelect(selected_from[e], beacon_history[e], K)` for every e in the domain (the per-epoch committee is the function-value of the selection on the captured snapshot — no retroactive rewrites). The structural witness: AdvanceEpoch's `(epoch + 1 :> new_committee) @@ committee_history` clause PREPENDS a new key; the `@@` operator preserves existing keys' values verbatim; no other action mutates committee_history. The rotation-history analog of FB30 ChainPrevHashLink.tla's `INV_AppendOnly` — legitimate rotation never rewrites past committees, on which fork-resolution and snapshot consistency depend |
| `PROP_EventualRotation` (temporal) | T-ER5 (Eventual Rotation). Under fairness on AdvanceEpoch + on either BeaconUpdate or Register/Deregister, the committee changes infinitely often when `|active_validators| > K` (so multiple distinct K-committees exist within the pool). The forward-progress contract: the rotation rationale (defeating long-run committee capture by adversarial sticky-membership) requires actual rotation in the limit. State-form witness: eventually some pair of consecutive epochs has different committees (`<>(\E e: committee_history[e] # committee_history[e + 1])`). The bounded-MaxEpoch form is what TLC validates; the unbounded generalization is a temporal-induction argument anchored at the same state-form witness |
| `PROP_NoCommitteeFreeze` (temporal) | No-stuck-committee discipline: if `|active_validators| >= K + 1`, the same committee cannot persist for more than `MaxEpoch / 2` consecutive epochs without a beacon change OR a pool change. State-machine witness for the no-stuck-committee contract: even under adversarial beacon + pool stability, the bounded-epoch enumeration shows the committee changes within a bounded window. The TLA+ liveness body asserts that eventually for some e, `beacon_history[e+1] /= beacon_history[e]` OR `selected_from[e+1] /= selected_from[e]` OR `committee_history[e+1] /= committee_history[e]` — the rotation-freeze anti-condition fails under fairness |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-eight specs above). The recommended `EpochCommitteeRotation.cfg` (`ValidatorPool = {v1, v2, v3, v4, v5}`, `K = 3`, `MaxEpoch = 4`, `BeaconValues = {b1, b2, b3}`) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The four-action state machine (AdvanceEpoch, RegisterValidator, DeregisterValidator, BeaconUpdate) exercises every reachable interleaving of cross-epoch committee rotation, active-set evolution, and beacon-randomness updates. Variables modeled: `epoch` (Nat — current epoch counter, monotone non-decreasing across AdvanceEpoch), `committee_history` (function `{0..epoch} → SUBSET ValidatorPool` — per-epoch K-committee record, only grown by AdvanceEpoch), `beacon_history` (function `{0..epoch+1} → BeaconValues` — per-epoch beacon feeding the seed; BeaconUpdate may advance one step ahead of AdvanceEpoch modeling the chain accumulating randomness for the next epoch's seed), `active_validators` (SUBSET ValidatorPool — currently registered validators), `selected_from` (function `{0..epoch} → SUBSET ValidatorPool` — ghost snapshot of active_validators at the moment committee_history[e] was drawn; required for the deterministic-selection invariant's antecedent). Actions modeled: `AdvanceEpoch` (epoch → epoch+1; draws the new committee via `EpochCommitteeSelect(active_validators, beacon_history[epoch+1], K)`; stores in committee_history[epoch+1]; snapshots active_validators into selected_from[epoch+1]; mirrors `Node::current_epoch_index` + `Node::current_epoch_rand` at `src/node/node.cpp:909-934`), `RegisterValidator(v)` (v ∈ ValidatorPool \ active_validators → add; mirrors REGISTER tx apply path at `src/chain/chain.cpp::apply_transactions` REGISTER branch with the active_from delay collapsed), `DeregisterValidator(v)` (v ∈ active_validators → remove with `Cardinality > 1` guard; mirrors DEREGISTER tx apply path), `BeaconUpdate(b)` (updates the beacon for the NEXT epoch; models the chain accumulating randomness through the current epoch_blocks and producing the seed for the next epoch). The abstract operator `EpochCommitteeSelect(pool, beacon, k)` is the spec-layer projection of `crypto::select_m_creators(crypto::epoch_committee_seed(epoch_rand, shard_id), avail_domains.size(), m)`; returns a SUBSET of `pool` of cardinality `min(k, |pool|)` that is a deterministic function of its three inputs.

This spec captures the cross-epoch committee rotation contract that governs Determ's per-epoch K-member committee selection at the state-machine layer. The committee is redrawn at every epoch boundary via `crypto::select_m_creators` keyed on the per-epoch seed `crypto::epoch_committee_seed(epoch_rand, shard_id)`; each epoch carries a fresh draw, so the committee rotates as the beacon-sourced randomness evolves and as the active validator pool grows/shrinks via REGISTER/DEREGISTER transactions. The TLA+ state-machine layer abstracts the three rotation sub-claims (deterministic per-epoch selection, cross-epoch rotation, active-set discipline) plus the history-monotonicity property into four actions + five invariants + two temporal properties:

1. **Deterministic per-epoch selection (T-ER1)** is captured by `INV_DeterministicSelection`. Same `(pool, beacon, k)` triple produces same committee output — required for cross-node consensus convergence under the same chain head. The structural witness is `select_m_creators`'s SHA-256-derived randomness: every node consuming the same `random_state` reproduces the same hybrid Fisher-Yates output per S-020.

2. **Committee size discipline (T-ER2)** is captured by `INV_CommitteeSizeIsK`. The per-epoch committee has cardinality K when the active pool has at least K members; otherwise equals the full pool (the under-quorum branch where R7 UnderQuorumMerge kicks in). The structural witness is `select_m_creators`'s `node_count >= m` precondition + the exact-m-indices return contract.

3. **Active-set discipline (T-ER3)** is captured by `INV_CommitteeSubsetActive`. Every committee member at epoch e was in active_validators at the moment of selection — zombie / ghost committees are structurally impossible. The ghost field `selected_from[e]` captures the live active_validators at the AdvanceEpoch firing.

4. **History monotonicity (T-ER4)** is captured by `INV_HistoryMonotone`. committee_history only grows across AdvanceEpoch; existing entries are byte-identical. The rotation-history analog of FB30 ChainPrevHashLink.tla's `INV_AppendOnly` — legitimate rotation never rewrites past committees, on which fork-resolution and snapshot consistency depend.

5. **Eventual rotation (T-ER5)** is captured by `PROP_EventualRotation` + `PROP_NoCommitteeFreeze`. Under fairness on AdvanceEpoch + a beacon change OR a non-trivial pool mutation between consecutive epochs, the committee changes infinitely often when multiple distinct K-committees exist within the pool — the forward-progress contract that defeats long-run committee capture by adversarial sticky-membership.

**Out of scope** (consistent with this spec's §7 header comment):

- Cryptographic uniformity of the SHA-256-derived index stream feeding `select_m_creators`. FB23 FrostVerify.tla + Preliminaries §2.3 (A3 CSPRNG uniformity) territory. The spec asserts the determinism side (purity); the uniformity side is the analytic-cryptography side.
- Quantitative bias bounds on the K/N ratio. S-020 closure narrative — the spec asserts the structural form; the bias-bound is the analytic side.
- The chain-layer apply discipline that gates REGISTER / DEREGISTER. FB5 AccountState.tla + FB8 StakeLifecycle.tla territory. The spec models the post-active-from / post-inactive-from state, abstracting the activation / deactivation delays.
- R4 region-aware overlay and R7 under-quorum merge. The spec covers the BASE rotation contract; R4 layers `eligible_in_region` filtering on top of `active_validators`; R7 widens the pool with refugees when under-quorum. These are sibling FB-track surfaces (Sharding.tla + future UnderQuorumMerge.tla territory).
- The within-epoch consensus surface (K-of-K block-sig phase, proposer rotation under aborts, equivocation slashing). FB1 Consensus.tla + FB22 F2ViewReconciliation.tla territory. This spec covers across-epoch rotation only.
- Snapshot / restore round-trip of the registry state. FB31 SnapshotIntegrity.tla covers the `s:` namespace's snapshot lifecycle that this spec's active_validators abstracts.

Companion analytic proofs: `docs/SECURITY.md` §S-020 (hybrid Fisher-Yates closure — the selection-function determinism + bias bound that `EpochCommitteeSelect`'s purity abstracts), `docs/SECURITY.md` §S-024 (formally-accepted epoch_blocks parameter + its bias bound — the epoch parameter the spec's MaxEpoch constant abstracts), `docs/proofs/RegionalSharding.md` (R4 — the region-aware overlay on top of this base rotation), `docs/proofs/UnderQuorumMerge.md` (R7 — the under-quorum branch when |active_validators| < K), `docs/proofs/Preliminaries.md` §2.1 (A2 SHA-256 collision resistance) + §2.3 (A3 CSPRNG uniformity) (the cryptographic assumptions underlying EpochCommitteeSelect's determinism + uniformity).

Cross-reference. FB1 `Consensus.tla` (FA1 K-of-K committee safety — the within-epoch consensus surface that this spec's per-epoch committee draw feeds; FB1 covers within-epoch; FB34 covers across-epoch), FB2 `Sharding.tla` (FA7 cross-shard surface — the per-shard committee derivation uses the same `epoch_committee_seed` but with the `shard_id` parameter; FB34 abstracts the shard dimension into the EpochCommitteeSelect's beacon input), FB22 `F2ViewReconciliation.tla` (v2.7 F2 within-round committee view reconciliation; closely related sibling — F2 handles within-round, FB34 handles across-epoch), FB23 `FrostVerify.tla` (Ed25519 EUF-CMA model + abstract-sig discipline; the cryptographic uniformity side that this spec's determinism complements), FB30 `ChainPrevHashLink.tla` (R25 prev_hash chain-link state machine — `INV_AppendOnly`'s append-only ghost-history pattern is the structural template that `INV_HistoryMonotone` mirrors). FB34 (this spec — the cross-epoch committee rotation state machine). Together FB1 + FB22 + FB34 witness the committee-membership surface end-to-end: FB1 covers within-epoch K-of-K safety; FB22 covers within-round F2 view reconciliation; FB34 covers across-epoch rotation discipline + active-set tracking + selection determinism.

### RegionalShardingCommittee.tla → FA-Regional (R4 region-aware committee selection composition of FA1 + FA8 + S-020 + R4 region-filter + R7 under-quorum merge + FB34 base rotation)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `block_height` (Nat ∈ 0..MaxBlock — current block height counter), `current_region` (Regions ∪ {"NONE"} — the active region for THIS block; "NONE" is the pre-genesis sentinel), `current_committee` (SUBSET of validator domain IDs — the committee drawn for the current block; Init is empty; AdvanceBlock populates), `region_history` (function `{0..block_height} → Regions` — per-block region record, only grown by AdvanceBlock), `committee_history` (function `{0..block_height} → SUBSET validator domain IDs` — per-block committee record, only grown by AdvanceBlock), `active_validators` (SUBSET DOMAIN Validators — currently registered validators, mutated by RegisterValidator / RegionPoolShrink), `merge_state` (function `Region → SUBSET Region` — per-region merge: `merge_state[R]` is the set of regions whose validators are admitted as refugees when R is the active region; set by ForceMerge), `beacon` (Nat — per-block beacon counter; abstracts the chain's cumulative_rand evolution at the abstract-randomness layer) |
| `INV_CommitteeFromActiveRegion` | T-RC1 (Committee From Active Region). For every block h in the domain of `region_history`, every member of `committee_history[h]` is in `EligibleInRegion(region_history[h], active_validators)` OR in the refugees from a merged-from region (when merge_state is active for that region). Composes R4 region-filter with R7 under-quorum merge by admitting refugees from sibling regions. The structural witness: `AdvanceBlock` draws the committee from `EffectivePool(R, active_validators, merge_state)` which is `EligibleInRegion(R) ∪ refugees-from-merged-regions`. The C++ correspondent is `Node::start_block_sig_phase` at `src/node/node.cpp:731` (the `registry_.eligible_in_region(cfg_.committee_region)` call) + lines 732-748 (the R4-Phase-4 under-quorum refugee-pool extension via `chain_.shards_absorbed_by`) |
| `INV_CommitteeSizeIsK` | T-RC2 (Committee Size). Every committee in `committee_history` has cardinality K (when the effective pool at the time of selection had at least K members) OR equals the full effective pool (under-quorum branch where R7 fires). The structural witness: `SelectMCreators`'s `effective_k = min(k, |pool|)` computation picks the exact target cardinality; the candidates set is non-empty by construction; CHOOSE returns a member of cardinality `effective_k`. Same shape as FB34 T-ER2 but lifted to the region-filtered + refugee-extended pool. The C++ correspondent is `select_m_creators` at `src/crypto/random.cpp:70-100` (S-020 closure — the hybrid Fisher-Yates K-of-N selector that throws on `node_count < m`) |
| `INV_RegionFilterDeterministic` | T-RC3 (Region Filter Determinism). `EligibleInRegion(region, active_validators)` is a deterministic SUBSET of `active_validators` for every region; pure linear-scan equivalent at the spec layer. State-form witness: the SUBSET-comprehension is a pure function of `(region, active_validators)`; TLA+ set semantics is purely extensional — same elements imply same set. Bidirectional purity is asserted: for any two regions R1, R2 ∈ Regions, `EligibleInRegion(R1) ∩ EligibleInRegion(R2) = {}` when `R1 # R2` (because a validator's region is single-valued in `Validators[v].region`). The C++ correspondent is `NodeRegistry::eligible_in_region` at `src/node/registry.cpp:86-95` (a pure linear scan over the sorted pool with strict equality on the region tag — deterministic by construction) |
| `INV_NoCrossRegionLeak` | T-RC4 (No Cross-Region Leak). At block h with region R AND no merge in effect for R, every validator in `committee_history[h]` has `Validators[v].region = R` — no cross-region leak. When a merge IS in effect, the looser predicate holds: every validator's region is in `{R} ∪ merge_state[R]` (the effective region set). Structural witness: the committee comes from `EligibleInRegion(R) ∪ refugees` where refugees are filtered by `merge_state[R]`; merge_state is monotone non-decreasing (ForceMerge only ADDS, never removes), so the current merge_state's region set is a SUPER-set of any past selection's region set — the invariant holds in the wider direction too. The C++ correspondent is the same `start_block_sig_phase` lines 731-748 region-filter + refugee-extension that drives the committee draw |
| `PROP_EventualCommitteeRotation` (temporal) | T-RC5a (Eventual Committee Rotation). Under fairness on AdvanceBlock + a region change OR an active-set mutation between consecutive blocks, the committee changes infinitely often when `|EligibleInRegion(R)| > K` (so multiple distinct K-committees exist within the region's pool). The forward-progress contract: the per-block region rotation paired with the per-block beacon advance ensures the committee rotates non-trivially across blocks; under fairness on the AdvanceBlock action, the committee at some block differs from the committee at the prior block. State-form witness: eventually some pair of consecutive blocks has different committees (`<>(\E h: committee_history[h] # committee_history[h + 1])`). Analog of FB34 T-ER5 lifted to the per-block regional surface |
| `PROP_UnderQuorumMerge` (temporal) | T-RC5b (Under-Quorum Merge composition with R7). If `|EligibleInRegion(R)| < K` for the current region R, eventually a merge to a sibling region fires (ForceMerge enables) — the R7 forward-progress contract that prevents the chain from stalling on an under-quorum region. Structural witness: ForceMerge's pre-condition is `Cardinality(EligibleInRegion(current_region, active_validators)) < K`; under weak fairness on the ForceMerge action, the merge fires when enabled and a sibling region has at least one active validator. The C++ correspondent is the MERGE_EVENT apply branch at `src/chain/chain.cpp:1018-1025` that populates `merge_state_` with `refugee_region`; the spec's `merge_state` variable mirrors this. Composes with R7 `UnderQuorumMerge.md`'s analytic narrative on the merge mechanism |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other twenty-nine specs above). The recommended `RegionalShardingCommittee.cfg` (`Validators = (v1, v2 in r1; v3, v4 in r2)`, `Regions = {"r1", "r2"}`, `K = 2`, `MaxBlock = 4`) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The four-action state machine (AdvanceBlock, RegisterValidator, RegionPoolShrink, ForceMerge) exercises every reachable interleaving of per-block region rotation, validator pool evolution, and R7 under-quorum merge composition. Variables modeled: `block_height` (Nat — current block height counter, monotone non-decreasing across AdvanceBlock), `current_region` (Regions ∪ {"NONE"} — the active region for THIS block), `current_committee` (SUBSET of validator domain IDs — the committee drawn for the current block), `region_history` (function `{0..block_height} → Regions` — per-block region record, only grown by AdvanceBlock), `committee_history` (function `{0..block_height} → SUBSET validator domain IDs` — per-block committee record, only grown by AdvanceBlock), `active_validators` (SUBSET DOMAIN Validators — currently registered validators), `merge_state` (function `Region → SUBSET Region` — per-region merge state set by ForceMerge), `beacon` (Nat — per-block beacon counter). Actions modeled: `AdvanceBlock` (block_height → block_height + 1; rotates the active region per protocol; draws a fresh committee via `SelectMCreators(EffectivePool(new_region, active_validators, merge_state), new_beacon, K)`; mirrors `Node::start_block_sig_phase` at `src/node/node.cpp:731`), `RegisterValidator(v, region)` (v ∈ DOMAIN Validators \ active_validators with `region = Validators[v].region` → add; mirrors REGISTER tx apply path at `src/chain/chain.cpp::apply_transactions` REGISTER branch with the activation delay collapsed), `RegionPoolShrink` (narrows the active validator pool by deregistering a validator; mirrors DEREGISTER tx apply path; composes with R7 by exposing the under-quorum branch reachably), `ForceMerge` (when `|EligibleInRegion(current_region)| < K`, activates the under-quorum merge by widening the effective pool with refugees from a sibling region; mirrors MERGE_EVENT tx + `chain.cpp::shards_absorbed_by` lookup). The abstract operators `EligibleInRegion(region, active_validators)` (pure SUBSET-comprehension; deterministic on inputs) and `SelectMCreators(pool, beacon, k)` (delegated to FB34; deterministic on inputs) compose to give the per-block committee draw discipline.

This spec captures the R4 region-aware committee selection contract that governs Determ's per-block K-member committee selection under regional sharding, plus the R7 under-quorum merge composition at the state-machine layer. The committee for block h is drawn from `NodeRegistry::eligible_in_region(committee_region)` keyed on the per-block beacon; under R7 the eligible pool is widened with refugees from sibling regions when `|EligibleInRegion(region)| < K`. The TLA+ state-machine layer abstracts the five sub-claims (region-filtered selection, no cross-region leak, region filter determinism, under-quorum merge composition, committee size discipline under merge) into four actions + five invariants + two temporal properties:

1. **Region-filtered selection (T-RC1)** is captured by `INV_CommitteeFromActiveRegion`. Every per-block committee member is in the active region's eligible pool OR in the refugees from a merged-from region — composes R4 region-filter with R7 under-quorum merge.

2. **Committee size discipline (T-RC2)** is captured by `INV_CommitteeSizeIsK`. The per-block committee has cardinality K when the effective (region-filtered + refugee-extended) pool has at least K members; otherwise equals the full effective pool. Same shape as FB34 T-ER2 lifted to the regional surface.

3. **Region filter determinism (T-RC3)** is captured by `INV_RegionFilterDeterministic`. The `EligibleInRegion` filter is a deterministic SUBSET of `active_validators` — required for cross-node consensus convergence on the same chain head's region-filtered pool. The bidirectional purity (disjoint filters across distinct regions) is the structural witness for "no cross-region leak at the FILTER layer".

4. **No cross-region leak (T-RC4)** is captured by `INV_NoCrossRegionLeak`. At block h with region R AND no merge in effect, every committee member has `Validators[v].region = R` — no cross-region leak. Under merge, the looser predicate `Validators[v].region ∈ {R} ∪ merge_state[R]` holds — still satisfying region-membership for the EFFECTIVE pool.

5. **Eventual rotation + under-quorum merge composition (T-RC5)** is captured by `PROP_EventualCommitteeRotation` + `PROP_UnderQuorumMerge`. Under fairness on AdvanceBlock + ForceMerge, the per-block committee rotates non-trivially across blocks AND an under-quorum region eventually receives a sibling merge — the R7 forward-progress contract that prevents the chain from stalling on a single region's pool collapse.

**Out of scope** (consistent with this spec's §7 header comment):

- Cryptographic uniformity of the SHA-256-derived index stream feeding `select_m_creators`. FB23 FrostVerify.tla + Preliminaries §2.3 (A3 CSPRNG uniformity) territory. The spec asserts the determinism side (purity); the uniformity side is the analytic-cryptography side.
- Quantitative bias bounds on the K/N ratio. S-020 closure narrative — the spec asserts the structural form; the bias-bound is the analytic side.
- MERGE_EVENT gossip + validation determinism (FA9 territory). The spec abstracts the MERGE_EVENT mechanism as `ForceMerge`; the wire-level gossip surface is a separate FB-track concern.
- Per-shard region assignment from the genesis manifest. The per-shard `shard_committee_regions_` map is a config-layer artifact; this spec models the post-config rotation directly via the abstract `RotateRegion` helper.
- Snapshot / restore round-trip of the `merge_state` field. FB31 SnapshotIntegrity.tla covers the snapshot lifecycle that this spec's `merge_state` abstracts.
- The within-block consensus surface (K-of-K block-sig phase, proposer rotation under aborts, equivocation slashing). FB1 Consensus.tla + FB22 F2ViewReconciliation.tla territory. This spec covers per-block committee SELECTION; the within-block surface is the sibling FB-track domain.

Companion analytic proofs: `docs/proofs/RegionalSharding.md` (R4 — the region-aware overlay analytic narrative; this spec is the state-machine witness), `docs/proofs/UnderQuorumMerge.md` (R7 — the under-quorum merge mechanism; this spec is the state-machine witness composed via `PROP_UnderQuorumMerge`), `docs/SECURITY.md` §S-020 (hybrid Fisher-Yates closure — the selection-function determinism + bias bound that `SelectMCreators` abstracts, delegated to FB34), `docs/proofs/Preliminaries.md` §2.1 (A2 SHA-256 collision resistance) + §2.3 (A3 CSPRNG uniformity) (the cryptographic assumptions underlying `SelectMCreators`'s determinism + uniformity).

Cross-reference. FB1 `Consensus.tla` (FA1 K-of-K committee safety — the within-block consensus surface that this spec's per-block committee draw feeds; FB1 covers within-block; FB35 covers the region-filtered per-block committee membership), FB2 `Sharding.tla` (FA7 cross-shard surface — the per-shard committee derivation uses the same `epoch_committee_seed` but with the `shard_id` parameter; FB35 lifts the regional dimension explicitly), FB22 `F2ViewReconciliation.tla` (FA8 BFT escalation surface — within-round view reconciliation under aborts; the BFT escalation gate composes with this spec's region-filtered pool via the same `eligible_in_region` precondition), FB23 `FrostVerify.tla` (Ed25519 EUF-CMA model + abstract-sig discipline; the cryptographic uniformity side that this spec's determinism complements), FB30 `ChainPrevHashLink.tla` (R25 prev_hash chain-link state machine — `INV_AppendOnly`'s append-only ghost-history pattern is the structural template for this spec's `region_history` + `committee_history` monotonicity), FB34 `EpochCommitteeRotation.tla` (parent rotation spec — FB35 specializes by adding R4 region-filter + R7 under-quorum merge on top of the base rotation; `SelectMCreators` is the same shape as FB34's `EpochCommitteeSelect`, delegated). FB35 (this spec — the R4 region-aware committee selection state machine + R7 under-quorum merge composition). Together FB1 + FB22 + FB34 + FB35 witness the committee-membership surface end-to-end across the rotational + regional dimensions: FB1 covers within-block K-of-K safety; FB22 covers within-round F2 view reconciliation; FB34 covers across-epoch base rotation; FB35 specializes to per-block region-filtered committee selection with the under-quorum merge composition.

### RpcHmacAuth.tla → FA-RPC-Auth (S-001 closure, cross-tenant arm — HMAC-SHA-256 RPC authentication state machine)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `server_secret` (RpcSecrets ∪ {"NONE"} — the server's currently-configured HMAC secret; "NONE" is the pre-configure sentinel matching the auth-disabled branch at `src/rpc/rpc.cpp:113`), `auth_log` (Seq of [secret, body, auth_header, result] — the audit log of every ProcessRequest invocation; the secret field captures the server_secret AT THE TIME OF PROCESSING, which may differ from the secret the legitimate caller used pre-rotation), `pending_requests` (Seq of [body, auth_header] — the incoming-request queue grown by IssueAuthorizedRequest / IssueForgedRequest, shrunk by ProcessRequest in FIFO order). Length bounds: `Len(auth_log) <= MaxRequests` and `Len(pending_requests) <= MaxRequests` |
| `INV_NoForgedAccepted` | T-1 (Authentication Soundness). Every entry in `auth_log` with `result = "ACCEPT"` has `auth_header = Hmac(secret, body)` — i.e., the constant-time compare at ProcessRequest succeeded iff the canonical Hmac matched. State-form witness of T-1's HMAC-PRF unforgeability claim lifted to the state-machine layer. The analytic side (`RpcAuthHmacSoundness.md` L-1, L-5) bounds the adversary's probability of producing a valid forged_header at `2^-256 + q²/2^256`; the spec layer enforces the structural non-collision (forged headers are in `ForgedHeaders = {"FORGED"}`, which is disjoint from `HmacOutputs = {<<"HMAC", s, b>> : s ∈ RpcSecrets, b ∈ Messages}` by construction). The C++ correspondent is `RpcServer::verify_auth` at `src/rpc/rpc.cpp:112-129` — specifically the constant-time XOR-OR compare at lines 122-128 |
| `INV_ConstantTimeCompare` | T-3 (Constant-Time Comparison). Documentary invariant citing the C++ source at `src/rpc/rpc.cpp:122-128`: the XOR-OR loop iterates a fixed 64 bytes with no early exit; the per-iteration body is `diff |= (expected[i] ^ got[i])` which has no branch dependence on individual byte values; the final ternary `(diff == 0) ? "" : "auth_failed"` is the only conditional whose information content is "all 64 bytes matched vs ≥ 1 mismatch" — a single aggregate bit, useless for per-byte probing. TLA+'s semantic model is discrete state transitions, not real-time execution, so the spec layer cannot meaningfully model byte-level timing channels. The C++ side's constant-time guarantee is a precondition that the spec layer assumes; the audit at L-3 of `RpcAuthHmacSoundness.md` verifies the precondition. INV_ConstantTimeCompare is asserted as TRUE at the spec layer, serving as a documentation anchor for the C++-side audit |
| `INV_SecretConfidentiality` | T-4 (Secret Confidentiality at the Implementation Surface). `server_secret` never appears as a field of any element of `pending_requests` — the wire-layer payload contains only the Hmac output (which is one-way per A_HMAC), never the secret bytes. The structural witness: `PendingEntry` has only `[body, auth_header]` fields — no `secret` field. So no `pending_requests` element CAN carry the secret. The invariant body asserts this structurally over the field-existence predicate: for every entry e ∈ `pending_requests`, `DOMAIN e = {"body", "auth_header"}`. The C++ correspondents are the startup log at `src/rpc/rpc.cpp:92-104` (emits only `auth_secret_.size()`, never the value), the `verify_auth` error returns at lines 115 + 128 (fixed string constants with no dependence on K), and the `rpc_call` client at lines 276-321 (reads the secret from `DETERM_RPC_AUTH_SECRET`, computes the HMAC, embeds the Hmac output in the request — secret bytes never written to the wire). The auth_log's `secret` field records WHICH secret was used at processing time (server-side state, not wire-exposed) which is consistent with confidentiality at the wire surface |
| `INV_NoAuthBypass` | T-2 (No Auth Bypass). No entry in `auth_log` has `result = "ACCEPT"` where the recorded `auth_header` differs from `Hmac(secret, body)`. Captures the "every accepted request was either issued legitimately OR the adversary broke HMAC" claim. Under A_outside (the adversary has no access to the secret), the only requests that pass the verify gate are those where the auth_header equals the canonical Hmac. By construction of ForgedHeaders (disjoint from HmacOutputs), no IssueForgedRequest produces an entry that can pass the verify gate. Structural witness in `ProcessRequest`'s action body: `outcome := IF head.auth_header = Hmac(server_secret, head.body) THEN "ACCEPT" ELSE "REJECT"`. INV_NoAuthBypass and INV_NoForgedAccepted are equivalent under the action's deterministic outcome computation but stated separately to document both contracts (backward: every ACCEPT has matching canonical Hmac; forward: no non-matching header gets ACCEPT). The C++ correspondent is the same `verify_auth` flow at `src/rpc/rpc.cpp:112-129` |
| `PROP_EventualReject` (temporal) | T-5 (Eventual Rejection of Forgery). Under fairness on `ProcessRequest`, every forged request (where the queued auth_header is NOT the canonical Hmac for the current server_secret) is eventually rejected and logged with `result = "REJECT"`. The forward-progress contract: every queued request reaches the verify gate; the verify gate is deterministic; forged requests are always rejected. So eventually the auth_log contains a "REJECT" entry for every forged request that was ever enqueued (modulo the MaxRequests bound). State-form witness: `<>(\E i: i > Len(pending_requests) \/ Head(pending_requests).auth_header \in HmacOutputs)` — every forged request at some queue position eventually gets popped and processed (rejected) |
| `PROP_NoForgeryWithoutSecret` (temporal) | The adversary cannot produce a valid auth_header without learning the secret — modeled via the abstract Hmac() function's pre-image resistance. The structural argument: `IssueForgedRequest`'s `forged_header` parameter is constrained to `ForgedHeaders = {"FORGED"}`, which is disjoint from `HmacOutputs` by construction. So no `forged_header` can equal `Hmac(secret, body)` for any (secret, body) pair — the adversary CANNOT produce a valid auth_header by structural construction. The analytic side: under A_HMAC, the probability that a randomly-chosen forged_header collides with `Hmac(secret, body)` is bounded by `2^-256` per attempt (L-5 of `RpcAuthHmacSoundness.md`); the spec layer collapses the probabilistic non-collision into a structural non-collision via the `ForgedHeaders ∩ HmacOutputs = {}` disjointness. State-form witness: `[](\A i: auth_log[i].auth_header \in ForgedHeaders => auth_log[i].result = "REJECT")` — invariantly, every forged-origin log entry is REJECTed |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other thirty specs above). The recommended `RpcHmacAuth.cfg` (`RpcSecrets = {"s1", "s2"}`, `Messages = {"body1", "body2"}`, `MaxRequests = 4`) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The four-action state machine (ConfigureSecret / IssueAuthorizedRequest / IssueForgedRequest / ProcessRequest) exercises every reachable interleaving of secret-rotation, legitimate-request issuance, adversarial-forge attempts, and pipeline-dequeue ordering. Variables modeled: `server_secret` (`RpcSecrets ∪ {"NONE"}` — the server's currently-configured HMAC secret; "NONE" is the pre-configure sentinel mirroring the auth-disabled default at `src/rpc/rpc.cpp:113`), `auth_log` (Seq of `[secret, body, auth_header, result]` — the audit log of every ProcessRequest invocation, only grown by ProcessRequest), `pending_requests` (Seq of `[body, auth_header]` — the incoming-request queue, grown by IssueAuthorizedRequest / IssueForgedRequest and shrunk by ProcessRequest in FIFO order). Actions modeled: `ConfigureSecret(s)` (server's secret is set or rotated to s ∈ RpcSecrets; mirrors `RpcServer::RpcServer` construction at `src/rpc/rpc.cpp:79-90` and the operational rotation path via DETERM_RPC_AUTH_SECRET env-var re-read), `IssueAuthorizedRequest(body)` (legitimate caller computes `auth_header := Hmac(server_secret, body)` and enqueues `[body, auth_header]` to pending_requests; mirrors `rpc_call` at `src/rpc/rpc.cpp:276-321` — the secret bytes themselves are NEVER written to the request body or the wire, only the HMAC output), `IssueForgedRequest(body, forged_header)` (adversarial caller enqueues `[body, forged_header]` where forged_header is constrained to ForgedHeaders, structurally disjoint from HmacOutputs; models the A_outside adversary from `S001RpcAuthSoundness.md` §2.3), `ProcessRequest` (dequeue head of pending_requests; recompute `expected := Hmac(server_secret, head.body)`; accept iff `head.auth_header = expected`; log result to auth_log; mirrors `verify_auth` at `src/rpc/rpc.cpp:112-129`). The abstract `Hmac(secret, body)` operator is modeled as a tagged tuple `<<"HMAC", secret, body>>` — distinct (secret, body) pairs produce distinct outputs by TLA+ extensional equality on tuples; same (secret, body) pair always produces the same output (purity / determinism). The cryptographic strength of HMAC-SHA-256 (A_HMAC PRF security per L-5 of `RpcAuthHmacSoundness.md`) is asserted at the analytic layer; the spec layer enforces only the determinism + distinctness contract.

This spec captures the S-001 closure contract (cross-tenant arm: HMAC RPC authentication) that governs Determ's `RpcServer::verify_auth` at the state-machine layer. Every state-mutating RPC request must carry an `auth` header containing `hex(HMAC-SHA-256(server_secret, canonical(method, body)))`; the server recomputes the expected HMAC under its locally-stored secret and accepts iff the constant-time compare returns `diff == 0`. The TLA+ state-machine layer abstracts the five sub-claims (HMAC-PRF unforgeability, no auth bypass, constant-time compare, secret confidentiality, eventual reject of forgeries) into four actions + five invariants + two temporal properties:

1. **HMAC-PRF unforgeability (T-1)** is captured by `INV_NoForgedAccepted`. Every entry in `auth_log` with `result = "ACCEPT"` has `auth_header = Hmac(secret, body)` — the structural witness that no adversary without the secret can produce a valid auth_header. The analytic side (RpcAuthHmacSoundness.md L-1, L-5) bounds the per-attempt forgery probability at `2^-256 + q²/2^256`; the spec layer enforces structural non-collision via the ForgedHeaders ∩ HmacOutputs = {} disjointness.

2. **No auth bypass (T-2)** is captured by `INV_NoAuthBypass`. No entry in `auth_log` has `result = "ACCEPT"` where the recorded `auth_header` differs from `Hmac(secret, body)`. Captures the "every accepted request was either issued legitimately OR the adversary broke HMAC" claim. Equivalent to INV_NoForgedAccepted under the action's deterministic outcome computation; stated separately to document both backward (every ACCEPT has matching Hmac) and forward (no non-matching header gets ACCEPT) directions.

3. **Constant-time compare (T-3)** is captured by `INV_ConstantTimeCompare`. Documentary invariant citing the C++ source at `src/rpc/rpc.cpp:122-128`. TLA+'s discrete-state semantic model cannot meaningfully model byte-level timing channels; the C++ side's constant-time guarantee is a precondition the spec layer assumes, with the L-3 audit in `RpcAuthHmacSoundness.md` verifying the precondition holds.

4. **Secret confidentiality (T-4)** is captured by `INV_SecretConfidentiality`. `server_secret` never appears as a field of any element of `pending_requests` — the wire-layer payload contains only the Hmac output, never the secret bytes. Structural witness: `PendingEntry` has only `[body, auth_header]` fields — no `secret` field. The C++ correspondents are the startup log emitting only `auth_secret_.size()` (`src/rpc/rpc.cpp:92-104`), the fixed-string error returns (`:115`, `:128`), and the `rpc_call` client embedding only the Hmac output in the request (`:276-321`).

5. **Eventual rejection of forgery (T-5)** is captured by `PROP_EventualReject` + `PROP_NoForgeryWithoutSecret`. Under fairness on `ProcessRequest`, every forged request reaches the verify gate; the verify gate is deterministic; forged requests are always rejected. The standing temporal claim that the adversary cannot accumulate accepted forgeries even with unbounded attempts (modulo the MaxRequests model bound).

**Out of scope** (consistent with this spec's §7 header comment):

- Cryptographic strength of HMAC-SHA-256. The spec assumes A_HMAC (PRF security per RFC 2104 + Bellare-Canetti-Krawczyk 1996 / Bellare 2006) + A2/H1 (SHA-256 collision resistance per Preliminaries §2.1) hold; the analytic side at L-1, L-5 of `RpcAuthHmacSoundness.md` verifies. The spec layer enforces only the structural determinism + distinctness contract on the abstract Hmac() operator.
- Byte-level constant-time guarantee at `src/rpc/rpc.cpp:122-128`. The spec uses an atomic equality predicate; the byte-level audit is L-3 of `RpcAuthHmacSoundness.md` territory. TLA+'s discrete-state model is fundamentally incapable of expressing per-byte timing properties.
- Replay surface (T-2 limitation of `RpcAuthHmacSoundness.md`). HMAC alone does not bind a nonce — an attacker who eavesdrops a legitimate (body, auth_header) pair can replay it indefinitely; the spec's ProcessRequest would correctly ACCEPT a replayed pair. The apply-layer nonce gate (FA-Apply-3, FB7 Nonce.tla) is the second-line replay defense; the composition is at `S001RpcAuthSoundness.md` T-2 territory.
- Configuration-surface plaintext persistence of the secret at `Config::to_json` (F-1 of `RpcAuthHmacSoundness.md`). The spec models only the RPC-runtime surface; the config-lifecycle surface is a separate concern (operator filesystem hygiene + v2.17 passphrase encryption pattern).
- The localhost-only / external-bind binding mode (Option 1 of S-001's closure at `src/rpc/rpc.cpp:79-89`). The spec models the post-bind state; the network-layer binding mode is the operator-policy side of S-001.
- Rate limiter (S-014 / FB25 RateLimiterEviction.tla) that gates the RPC verify rate. The spec models the unbounded-rate baseline; the per-peer-IP rate-limit composition is FB25 territory.
- The input-validation arm of S-001's composition (S-018 JSON validation, per-method semantic gates). The spec covers the HMAC layer only; the input-validation arm is FB27 `JsonValidation.tla` territory. The full composition theorem is at `S001RpcAuthSoundness.md` T-1.

Companion analytic proofs: `docs/proofs/RpcAuthHmacSoundness.md` (the HMAC-PRF cryptographic layer — T-1 auth soundness, T-2 replay analysis, T-3 constant-time compare audit, T-4 secret confidentiality at RPC surface, T-5 HMAC PRF q²/2^256 q-query bound; this spec is the state-machine witness lifting T-1 + T-2 + T-4 + T-5 to discrete-state assertions and T-3 to a documentary precondition), `docs/proofs/S001RpcAuthSoundness.md` (the composition theorem covering HMAC auth + input-validation defense; §3 T-1..T-5 enumerate the composition claims; this spec covers the HMAC arm only), `docs/SECURITY.md` §S-001 (closure narrative for the HMAC RPC auth scheme; this spec is the state-machine witness of Option 3's "attacker without secret cannot forge requests" claim), `docs/proofs/Preliminaries.md` §2.1 (A2 SHA-256 collision resistance) + §2.2 (A1 Ed25519 EUF-CMA, cited by analogy for the EUF-CMA-style game in T-1).

Cross-reference. FB7 `Nonce.tla` (FA-Apply-3 nonce-gate — apply-layer replay defense; the second-line backstop to T-2's HMAC replay limitation that this spec does NOT model; together FB7 + FB36 close the end-to-end replay surface per `S001RpcAuthSoundness.md` T-2), FB23 `FrostVerify.tla` (Ed25519 EUF-CMA model + abstract-sig discipline; the structural analog at the consensus-signature layer — FB36 uses the abstract-Hmac discipline mirroring FrostVerify's abstract-sig discipline), FB25 `RateLimiterEviction.tla` (S-014 F-1 rate-limiter; the pre-gate that bounds the adversary's verify-attempt rate; composes with this spec via the rate-limiter-as-pre-gate discipline documented in the threat-model matrix of `S001RpcAuthSoundness.md` §5), FB27 `JsonValidation.tla` (S-018 closure; the structural-validation arm of the composition theorem at `S001RpcAuthSoundness.md` T-1; sibling spec covering the input-validation layer that FB36 deliberately omits). FB36 (this spec — the RPC HMAC-SHA-256 authentication state machine for S-001 closure, cross-tenant arm). Together FB7 + FB25 + FB27 + FB36 witness the end-to-end RPC defense posture: FB36 covers the HMAC cryptographic gate; FB27 covers the structural JSON validation layer; FB25 covers the rate-limiter pre-gate that bounds the adversary's verify-attempt rate; FB7 covers the apply-layer nonce gate that backstops the replay surface. The composition theorem at `S001RpcAuthSoundness.md` T-1 enumerates the joint soundness statement across all four arms.

### HelloHandshake.tla → R32A5 (test-hello-handshake-determinism) + S-022 (per-message-type caps) + S-021 (chain identity) — HELLO peer-handshake state machine

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `peer_handshakes` (Seq of [from, to, wire_version, chain_id, node_id, status] — one entry per InitiateHandshake invocation; status is one of {"PENDING", "ACCEPT", "REJECT"}; ProcessHandshake / RejectMismatchedChain / RejectIncompatibleWireVersion mutate the status field at index idx) and `accepted_peers` (SUBSET of NodeIds — the set of peer node_ids that have successfully completed handshake; grows monotonically — ACCEPT entries add from.node_id; InitiateHandshake / REJECT entries do not). Length bound: `Len(peer_handshakes) <= MaxHandshakes` |
| `INV_ChainIdAgreement` | T-1 (Chain-ID Agreement). Every accepted handshake (status = "ACCEPT") has its chain_id equal to the receiver's chain_id — the structural witness of the "no cross-chain peer admission" contract at the handshake boundary. ProcessHandshake's `cid_match := entry.chain_id = receiver_cid` is a pre-condition for the ACCEPT branch; the alternative RejectMismatchedChain action handles the mismatch path with REJECT. Together they discharge the cross-chain isolation contract. The invariant body asserts as a per-entry predicate over peer_handshakes: every ACCEPT entry has a well-formed chain_id in ChainIds (the structural witness; the receiver-side equality is implicit in the action's IF-THEN-ELSE). The C++ correspondent is the implicit chain-identity gate threaded through `set_chain_identity` at `src/net/gossip.cpp:17-23` plus the per-message validation pipeline; the spec's chain_id discriminator is the spec-layer projection of the production (genesis_hash, region) identity tuple |
| `INV_WireVersionCompat` | T-2 (Wire-Version Compatibility). Every accepted handshake has `wire_version <= kWireVersionMax`. The build can only speak versions in {kWireVersionLegacy = 0, kWireVersionBinary = 1} per `include/determ/net/messages.hpp:90-92`; admitting a higher version would break the post-handshake codec negotiation. Structural witness in ProcessHandshake's action body: `wv_compat := entry.wire_version <= kWireVersionMax; new_status := IF cid_match /\ wv_compat THEN "ACCEPT" ELSE "REJECT"`. RejectIncompatibleWireVersion covers the wv > kWireVersionMax case with REJECT. The C++ correspondent is the wire_version negotiation at `src/net/gossip.cpp:180-184` (`negotiated = their_v < kWireVersionMax ? their_v : kWireVersionMax`); the spec collapses the negotiation into the binary admission gate |
| `INV_HelloIsJsonAlways` | T-3 (HELLO-Always-JSON). HELLO never gets binary-codec'd. The spec models HELLO as always-JSON; the action set has no Encode-HELLO-as-binary disjunct. The HandshakeRecord shape has fields {from, to, wire_version, chain_id, node_id, status} — no `encoded_binary` flag. By TypeOK, every entry in peer_handshakes conforms to HandshakeRecord; so no entry can carry a "this was binary-codec'd" marker. The invariant body asserts the field-existence predicate structurally: DOMAIN e = {"from", "to", "wire_version", "chain_id", "node_id", "status"} for every entry. The C++ correspondent is the unconditional throw at `src/net/binary_codec.cpp:330-331` (`if (m.type == MsgType::HELLO) throw std::runtime_error("binary_codec: HELLO must be sent as JSON");`). The spec layer collapses the runtime throw-on-binary-encode contract into the structural absence of a binary-encoding flag |
| `INV_AcceptedPeersSubsetHandshakes` | Every member of `accepted_peers` has a corresponding ACCEPT entry in `peer_handshakes`. The accepted_peers set is a derived projection of the peer_handshakes log; the invariant ensures no accepted_peers entry exists without a corresponding ACCEPT log entry (preventing "orphan admission" where a peer slips into accepted_peers without having gone through the handshake gate). Structural witness in ProcessHandshake's action body: `accepted_peers' = IF new_status = "ACCEPT" THEN accepted_peers \cup {entry.node_id} ELSE accepted_peers`. So accepted_peers grows by from.node_id only on ACCEPT outcomes. This rules out: Init-time orphans (accepted_peers starts empty); REJECT-time leakage (RejectMismatchedChain / RejectIncompatibleWireVersion both leave accepted_peers UNCHANGED); InitiateHandshake leakage (the action leaves accepted_peers UNCHANGED) |
| `PROP_EventualHandshakeResolution` (temporal) | T-4 (Eventual Handshake Resolution). Under fairness on ProcessHandshake (+ RejectMismatchedChain + RejectIncompatibleWireVersion), every PENDING handshake eventually transitions to ACCEPT or REJECT. The forward-progress contract: no handshake is left in PENDING indefinitely. The Spec's fairness clauses (WF_vars on each of the three resolution actions) ensure that any PENDING entry is eventually picked up by one of the resolution paths. State-form witness: `<>(\E i: i > Len(peer_handshakes) \/ peer_handshakes[i].status /= "PENDING")` — every PENDING handshake at some log position is eventually resolved |
| `PROP_NoSilentAcceptOnMismatch` (temporal) | T-5 (No Silent Accept on Mismatch). Mismatched chain_id or incompatible wire_version always produces REJECT, never silent ACCEPT. The standing invariant restated as a temporal property to document the "no silent accept on mismatch" composition. The structural argument: ProcessHandshake's IF-THEN-ELSE on (cid_match /\ wv_compat) is the deterministic outcome predicate; if either check fails, the outcome is REJECT. There is no path in the action body that sets status = "ACCEPT" when either check fails. Additionally, RejectMismatchedChain and RejectIncompatibleWireVersion are dedicated REJECT-only actions — they do not have an ACCEPT branch at all. State-form witness: `[](\A i: peer_handshakes[i].wire_version > kWireVersionMax => peer_handshakes[i].status /= "ACCEPT")` — invariantly, no incompatible-wire-version entry ever becomes ACCEPT |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other thirty-one specs above). The recommended `HelloHandshake.cfg` (`WireVersions = {0, 1}`, `ChainIds = {"chain_a", "chain_b"}`, `NodeIds = {"n1", "n2", "n3"}`, `MaxHandshakes = 4`) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The four-action state machine (InitiateHandshake / ProcessHandshake / RejectMismatchedChain / RejectIncompatibleWireVersion) exercises every reachable interleaving of cross-chain admission attempts, wire-version-compatibility checks, and multi-peer handshake-triangle scheduling. Variables modeled: `peer_handshakes` (Seq of `[from, to, wire_version, chain_id, node_id, status]` — one entry per InitiateHandshake invocation; status is one of {"PENDING", "ACCEPT", "REJECT"}; ProcessHandshake mutates the status field at index idx), `accepted_peers` (SUBSET of NodeIds — the set of peer node_ids that have successfully completed handshake; grows monotonically — ACCEPT entries add from.node_id, InitiateHandshake / REJECT entries do not). Actions modeled: `InitiateHandshake(from, to)` (peer `from` opens a connection to peer `to` and emits a HELLO with its claimed identity tuple; appends a new [from, to, wire_version, chain_id, node_id, status="PENDING"] record to peer_handshakes; mirrors `peer->send(make_hello(...))` at `src/net/gossip.cpp:44` and `:65`), `ProcessHandshake(idx)` (server processes the PENDING handshake at index idx; checks wire_version compat + chain_id match; sets status to "ACCEPT" iff both pass, "REJECT" otherwise; on ACCEPT, adds from.node_id to accepted_peers; mirrors the `case MsgType::HELLO:` branch at `src/net/gossip.cpp:168-187`), `RejectMismatchedChain(idx)` (server rejects PENDING handshake because from.chain_id differs from receiver's chain_id; sets status to "REJECT"; UNCHANGED accepted_peers; models the cross-chain isolation contract), `RejectIncompatibleWireVersion(idx)` (server rejects PENDING handshake because from.wire_version > kWireVersionMax; sets status to "REJECT"; UNCHANGED accepted_peers; models the build-cannot-speak-newer-codec contract). The kWireVersionLegacy = 0 and kWireVersionMax = 1 constants in the spec mirror `include/determ/net/messages.hpp:90-92` exactly.

This spec captures the HELLO handshake admission contract that governs every Determ peer connection's pre-negotiation phase. HELLO is the first wire message exchanged on every TCP socket; carries `wire_version`, `chain_id`, `node_id` (and `committee_region` in production payload — abstracted at this layer; R4 region-aware committee selection is FB35 territory). HELLO is ALWAYS JSON — the binary codec at `src/net/binary_codec.cpp:327-331` throws when invoked on a HELLO message. The TLA+ state-machine layer abstracts the five sub-claims (chain-id agreement, wire-version compatibility, HELLO-always-JSON, eventual handshake resolution, no silent accept on mismatch) into four actions + five invariants + two temporal properties:

1. **Chain-ID agreement (T-1)** is captured by `INV_ChainIdAgreement`. Every accepted handshake has from.chain_id matching the receiver's chain_id — the structural witness of "no cross-chain peer admission" at the handshake boundary. The dedicated RejectMismatchedChain action handles the mismatch path with REJECT; together with ProcessHandshake's cid_match precondition they discharge the cross-chain isolation contract.

2. **Wire-version compatibility (T-2)** is captured by `INV_WireVersionCompat`. Every accepted handshake has wire_version <= kWireVersionMax. The build can only speak versions in {0, 1} per `include/determ/net/messages.hpp:90-92`; admitting a higher version would break the post-handshake codec negotiation. RejectIncompatibleWireVersion covers the wv > kWireVersionMax case with REJECT.

3. **HELLO-always-JSON (T-3)** is captured by `INV_HelloIsJsonAlways`. The spec models HELLO as always-JSON — the action set has no Encode-HELLO-as-binary disjunct. The HandshakeRecord shape excludes any binary-encoding flag by construction; the C++ correspondent is the unconditional throw at `src/net/binary_codec.cpp:330-331`.

4. **Eventual handshake resolution (T-4)** is captured by `PROP_EventualHandshakeResolution`. Under fairness on the three resolution actions (ProcessHandshake + RejectMismatchedChain + RejectIncompatibleWireVersion), every PENDING handshake eventually transitions to ACCEPT or REJECT. The forward-progress contract: no handshake is left in PENDING indefinitely.

5. **No silent accept on mismatch (T-5)** is captured by `PROP_NoSilentAcceptOnMismatch`. Mismatched chain_id or incompatible wire_version always produces REJECT, never silent ACCEPT. The structural argument: ProcessHandshake's IF-THEN-ELSE on (cid_match /\ wv_compat) is the deterministic outcome predicate; if either check fails, the outcome is REJECT. The dedicated reject actions don't have an ACCEPT branch at all.

**Out of scope** (consistent with this spec's §7 header comment):

- The byte-level serialization determinism contract that `test-hello-handshake-determinism` exercises in-process (the 6-scenario harness at `src/main.cpp:32411-32711` — replay determinism, round-trip identity, cross-instance byte-identity, field-binding completeness, HELLO-always-JSON contract, boundary values) is the byte-level witness for the serialization-purity claim. The TLA+ state-machine layer abstracts the byte-level determinism into the structural field-tuple contract; the in-process test is the byte-level witness.
- The wire-version negotiation `negotiated = min(ours, theirs)` at `src/net/gossip.cpp:182-184` is collapsed at the spec layer into the binary admission gate. The C++ side's actual negotiation logic is the analytic witness; the spec layer collapses the negotiated value into the admission outcome.
- The chain_id discriminator is the spec-layer projection of the production binary's (genesis_hash, region) identity tuple threaded through `set_chain_identity` at `src/net/gossip.cpp:17-23`. The production binary's chain-identity surface is multi-field; the spec collapses this into a single opaque chain_id field for state-machine clarity.
- The S-022 per-message-type size caps at `include/determ/net/messages.hpp:103-152` are NOT modeled here. HELLO is the consensus-chatter category (1 MB default cap); the spec layer assumes the HELLO message reaches the admission gate (the size cap is a precondition).
- The HELLO-exempt rate-limiter carve-out at `src/net/gossip.cpp:142-148` (HELLO is exempt from the per-peer-IP token-bucket rate limit so the handshake completes even under flood pressure) is NOT modeled here. The rate-limiter is FB25 RateLimiterEviction.tla territory.
- The post-handshake message-validation pipeline (the `peer_message_allowed` filter at `src/net/gossip.cpp:162` that gates per-message-type admission based on the peer's claimed (role, shard_id) tuple) is NOT modeled here. The spec covers only the handshake admission gate.
- The (port, role, shard_id, committee_region) fields of the production HELLO payload are NOT modeled at this layer. They are routing-policy discriminators consumed by post-handshake gossip filtering; their invariants are sibling spec territory.

Companion runtime witness: `tools/test_hello_handshake_determinism.sh` (the shell-level wrapper driving the in-process R32A5 unit test `test-hello-handshake-determinism` at `src/main.cpp:32411-32711` — the 6-scenario harness covering replay determinism, round-trip identity, cross-instance byte-identity, field-binding completeness, HELLO-always-JSON contract, and boundary values). The unit test is the byte-level witness for serialization-purity; this spec is the state-machine-level witness for the admission contract.

Cross-reference. FB26 `BlockchainStateIntegrity.tla` (S-021 + S-033 + S-038 composition — the chain-load-layer integrity gate; pairs with this spec via the cross-chain isolation surface — FB37 covers handshake-time admission gate, FB26 covers chain-load-time integrity gate), FB27 `JsonValidation.tla` (S-018 closure — the structural-validation arm for JSON envelopes; HELLO is always-JSON so any malformed HELLO field would fire through the FB27 validation gate before reaching FB37's admission gate), FB35 `RegionalShardingCommittee.tla` (R4 region-aware committee selection — the post-handshake region-policy enforcement; the committee_region field of the HELLO payload feeds into the R4 selection oracle, which this spec abstracts away), FB36 `RpcHmacAuth.tla` (S-001 closure cross-tenant arm — the RPC-layer authentication state machine; sibling spec covering the parallel RPC admission surface alongside this gossip-layer HELLO admission surface). FB37 (this spec — the HELLO peer-handshake state machine; the gossip-layer admission gate for the per-peer connection lifecycle). Together FB26 + FB27 + FB35 + FB36 + FB37 witness the multi-surface admission posture: FB37 covers the gossip-layer HELLO handshake; FB36 covers the RPC-layer HMAC authentication; FB27 covers the structural JSON validation across all surfaces; FB26 covers the chain-load-layer integrity gate; FB35 covers the post-handshake region-policy enforcement. The composition is implicit in the protocol architecture (PROTOCOL.md §9.1 wire envelope discipline).

### BoundedMempoolAdmission.tla → FA-S008-EvictionRBF (cap-eviction + RBF semantics companion to S008BoundedMempool.md; FB33 sibling)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `mempool` (SUBSET of MempoolEntry where MempoolEntry = [sender, nonce, fee, tx_hash] — set-semantics so per-(sender, nonce) slot is structurally unique by INV_RBFFeeMonotone), `eviction_log` (Seq(TxHashes) — append-only audit trail of evicted tx_hashes, only mutated by EvictLowest + Submit's evict-then-admit branch), `next_nonce` (Senders → Nat — per-account applied-frontier; mirrors `chain_.next_nonce(s)` at `src/chain/chain.cpp::next_nonce`; strictly monotone non-decreasing across Apply), `ops_count` (Nat ≤ MaxOps — total action-counter for TLC bound). The TxHashes universe is modeled as tagged tuples `[sender, nonce, fee]` so distinct (sender, nonce, fee) triples produce structurally-distinct hashes by TLA+ extensional equality — the spec-layer abstraction of the SHA-256 collision-resistance assumption (Preliminaries.md §2.1 A2) |
| `INV_CapBound` | T-1 (Capacity Bound, S008BoundedMempool.md headline witness). `Cardinality(mempool) <= Cap` at every reachable state. Structural argument: Submit's admission branches gate on `Cardinality(mempool) < Cap` for fresh-admit (b); the evict-then-admit branch (c) preserves the cap (one remove + one add); RBF preserves the cap (in-place same-slot remove-then-add of the SET); Apply / EvictLowest only remove. Direct lift of S008BoundedMempool.md L-5 (Global cap invariant under admission) into the discrete-state layer. Maps to the cap-overflow branch of `Node::mempool_admit_check` at `src/node/node.cpp:1980-1992` + `Node::mempool_make_room_for` at `src/node/node.cpp:2001-2017` |
| `INV_NonceGated` | T-2 (Nonce-Gating Soundness, two-stage defense). Every entry in `mempool` has `nonce >= next_nonce[sender]`. Two-stage defense: (a) Submit's pre-condition `n >= next_nonce[s]` rejects stale-nonce at intake (the FB33 sibling's AdmitTransaction (1) silent-drop branch carries the audit-log side); (b) Apply's nonce gate (`n = next_nonce[s]`) atomically removes the entry with the SAME nonce that next_nonce previously held; the advance `next_nonce' = next_nonce + 1` makes that nonce stale, but the entry is gone in the same atomic step. Maps to the stale-nonce drop at `src/node/node.cpp:2022-2023` + the strict-equality nonce gate at `src/chain/chain.cpp:739`. Composes with FA-Apply-3 / FB7 Nonce.tla via the once-advanced-never-retreats discipline |
| `INV_RBFFeeMonotone` | T-3 (RBF Determinism).
