When RBF replaces (sender, nonce), the new entry has STRICTLY GREATER fee than the replaced one — the "incumbent ties win" rule rejects the equality case. The structural witness is the action body's `new_f > existing.fee` precondition; the invariant re-asserts as a global discipline. The discrete-state form pinned here: invariantly, no two entries in mempool can share the same (sender, nonce) — per-slot uniqueness implies that if RBF fired, the old entry is gone and the new entry is present with the new fee strictly greater (otherwise the RBF action would not have fired). Maps to the RBF tie-break at `src/node/node.cpp:2041-2043` + `:3181-3185` |
| `INV_EvictionAlwaysLowest` | T-5 (No-Useful-Tx-Loss-Under-Pressure). Every entry appended to `eviction_log` was the lowest-fee tx in mempool at eviction time. The structural witness: EvictLowest's body binds `victim := min_fee_entry`; Submit's (c) cap-pressure branch does the same; no other action writes to eviction_log. The standing invariant collapses to a structural witness: every appended hash structurally encodes a (sender, nonce, fee) triple via tx_hash_for, and that fee was the min at fire time. Rules out the adversarial case where a high-fee honest tx gets evicted to make room for a low-fee adversary tx — the structural witness for S008BoundedMempool.md T-5's "honest-tx survival under flooder pressure" claim. Maps to the min-fee scan + erase pair at `src/node/node.cpp:2005-2009` + `:2014-2015` |
| `PROP_EventualApplyOrEvict` (temporal) | S008BoundedMempool.md liveness side: every tx submitted to mempool is eventually removed via one of the two terminal paths (Apply OR EvictLowest) OR via RBF-replace. The leads-to form: a tx in mempool eventually leaves mempool. The structural argument: Apply removes entries with `nonce = next_nonce[sender]` under fairness; EvictLowest removes the min-fee entry under cap pressure under fairness; RBF replaces a same-slot entry with a higher-fee version (the spec's set-semantics models this as remove-then-add). State-form witness: `(e \in mempool) ~> (e \notin mempool)` for every MempoolEntry e |
| `PROP_NoStaleNonceEverAdmitted` (temporal) | T-2 state-form (temporal-box restatement of INV_NonceGated). Invariantly across all reachable states, no entry in mempool has nonce < next_nonce[sender] — the standing discipline that the nonce-gate is not just a transition-time check but a globally-quantified state-machine property. A regression that admitted a stale-nonce tx (or failed to evict a tx that became stale post-admission) would surface as a violation of this box-clause. The spec's set-semantics + INV_RBFFeeMonotone same-slot uniqueness structurally collapse the FB33 EvictStale surface (FB33 covers the race case where a fresh-nonce tx gets stranded after another tx wins the apply race; FB38 abstracts the race away via single-occupancy per slot) |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other thirty-two specs above). The recommended `BoundedMempoolAdmission.cfg` (`Senders = {"a", "b"}`, `Nonces = {0, 1, 2}`, `Fees = {1, 2, 3}`, `Cap = 3`, `MaxOps = 4`) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The five-action state machine (Submit, RBF, Apply, EvictLowest, Stutter) exercises every reachable interleaving of fresh admit / cap-pressure eviction / RBF replace / apply-driven drain. Variables modeled: `mempool` (SUBSET of MempoolEntry where MempoolEntry = `[sender, nonce, fee, tx_hash]` — set-semantics; per-(sender, nonce) slot uniqueness via INV_RBFFeeMonotone), `eviction_log` (Seq(TxHashes) — append-only audit trail of evicted tx_hashes), `next_nonce` (Senders → Nat — per-account applied-frontier mirroring `chain_.next_nonce(s)`), `ops_count` (Nat ≤ MaxOps — TLC action budget). Actions modeled: `Submit(s, n, f, h)` (incoming admission attempt with three sub-cases — (b) room-available admit, (c) cap-pressure evict-then-admit when incoming fee > min-fee, (d) cap-pressure silent reject when incoming fee <= min-fee; pre-condition `n >= next_nonce[s]` enforces the FA-Apply-3 gate; mirrors `Node::on_tx` at `src/node/node.cpp:2019-2054` + the unified admission gate), `RBF(s, n, new_f, new_h)` (same-slot replacement with strict-greater-fee precondition; in-place set remove-then-add; mirrors the RBF branch at `src/node/node.cpp:2037-2044`), `Apply(s, n)` (apply head-of-mempool tx with strict-equality nonce gate `n = next_nonce[s]`; removes from mempool, advances `next_nonce' = next_nonce + 1`; mirrors `Chain::apply_transactions` strict-equality gate at `src/chain/chain.cpp:739`), `EvictLowest` (standalone cap-pressure eviction; pre-condition `Cardinality(mempool) >= Cap`; removes min-fee entry, appends to eviction_log; mirrors `Node::mempool_make_room_for` at `src/node/node.cpp:2001-2017`), `Stutter` (bounds TLC state space when ops_count >= MaxOps). The abstract `tx_hash_for(s, n, f)` operator is the spec-layer projection of the SHA-256-derived tx-hash; distinct (sender, nonce, fee) triples produce structurally-distinct hashes by TLA+ extensional equality on records.

This spec captures the CAP-EVICTION + RBF cores of the S-008 closure at the state-machine layer, COMPLEMENTING FB33 `MempoolAdmission.tla`. FB33 covers the FULL seven-disjunct admission decision tree (stale-nonce silent-drop branch, sig-verify gate, per-sender quota, five-reason rejection-log audit) but collapses the eviction discipline into a single AdmitTransaction (5b) disjunct without a tracked eviction_log. FB38 (this spec) narrows to the cap-eviction + RBF cores with the eviction_log surfaced as a state variable, making the S008BoundedMempool.md T-5 "no-useful-tx-loss" claim observable as `INV_EvictionAlwaysLowest` at TLC trace granularity. The five invariants + two temporal properties pin the four S008BoundedMempool.md theorems FB38 specifically formalizes:

1. **Capacity bound (T-1)** is captured by `INV_CapBound`. The mempool never exceeds the configured cap regardless of admission interleaving. Structural witness: Submit's three sub-cases (room-admit / evict-then-admit / silent-reject) all preserve `Cardinality(mempool) <= Cap`; RBF preserves the cap structurally (in-place same-slot swap); Apply / EvictLowest only shrink. Direct lift of S008BoundedMempool.md L-5 into the discrete-state layer.

2. **Nonce-gating soundness (T-2)** is captured by `INV_NonceGated` + `PROP_NoStaleNonceEverAdmitted`. Two-stage defense: Submit's `n >= next_nonce[s]` pre-condition rejects stale-nonce at intake; Apply's strict-equality `n = next_nonce[s]` + atomic next_nonce advance ensures no stale entry remains post-apply. Composes with FA-Apply-3 / FB7 Nonce.tla via the once-advanced-never-retreats discipline.

3. **RBF determinism (T-3)** is captured by `INV_RBFFeeMonotone`. Same-(sender, nonce) submissions converge to the highest-fee version; the "incumbent ties win" rule prevents resource churn. The per-slot uniqueness invariant is the structural witness.

4. **No-useful-tx-loss-under-pressure (T-5)** is captured by `INV_EvictionAlwaysLowest`. Every eviction targets the current min-fee tx — rules out the adversarial case where a high-fee honest tx gets evicted to make room for a low-fee adversary tx. The structural witness is the action-body binding `victim := min_fee_entry` in both EvictLowest and Submit's (c) branch; no other action writes to eviction_log.

5. **Eventual progress (S008BoundedMempool.md liveness)** is captured by `PROP_EventualApplyOrEvict`. Under fairness on Apply + EvictLowest, every tx in mempool eventually leaves via one of the two terminal paths (or via RBF-replace).

**Out of scope** (consistent with this spec's §9 header comment + the FB33 complementarity):

- The full seven-disjunct admission decision tree (stale-nonce silent-drop, sig-verify, per-sender quota, rejection-log audit) is FB33 territory. FB38 collapses the stale-nonce branch into Submit's pre-condition + Apply's atomic remove-and-advance; the sig-verify + per-sender-quota + rejection-log surfaces are not modeled here.
- The S-002 sig-verify gate at `src/node/node.cpp:2025-2028` (FB23 FrostVerify.tla is the upstream soundness theorem; FB33's INV_SigValidityNecessary lifts it to the mempool-layer; FB38 omits to focus on cap-eviction + RBF cores).
- The S-022 per-MsgType wire-format cap (FB36 territory). S008BoundedMempool.md T-4 composes T-1 (FB38's INV_CapBound) with S-022's 1-MB-per-tx wire cap to bound the total mempool memory; FB38 covers the count-bound side only.
- The S-014 per-IP rate limiter composition (FB25 RateLimiterEviction.tla territory). S008BoundedMempool.md T-6 covers the rate-bound + storage-bound joint analytical claim; FB38 covers the storage side only.
- Cross-shard mempool composition (FB32 CrossShardReceiptRoundtrip.tla territory). FB38 models a single-shard mempool.
- Per-tx-type apply semantics (TRANSFER / REGISTER / STAKE / etc.). FB5 AccountState.tla + FB8 StakeLifecycle.tla + FB9 DAppRegistry.tla territory. FB38's Apply action collapses per-tx-type routing into a single "remove from mempool + advance next_nonce" abstract action.
- The operator-tunable cap surface (FB33's AdjustCap action). The C++ `MEMPOOL_MAX_TXS` is a compile-time `constexpr`; FB38 treats `Cap` as a fixed constant.
- The EvictStale sweep at `src/node/node.cpp:1798-1803` (FB33's EvictStale action). FB38 collapses staleness into the Apply action's atomic remove-and-advance; the set-semantics + INV_RBFFeeMonotone same-slot uniqueness structurally rule out the stranded-tx race that EvictStale handles in FB33.

Companion analytic proofs: `docs/proofs/S008BoundedMempool.md` (the analytic proof this spec is the state-machine companion to — T-1 → INV_CapBound, T-2 → INV_NonceGated + PROP_NoStaleNonceEverAdmitted, T-3 → INV_RBFFeeMonotone, T-5 → INV_EvictionAlwaysLowest; T-4 + T-6 are sibling-territory composition claims), `docs/proofs/NonceMonotonicity.md` (FA-Apply-3 — the per-account nonce monotonicity theorem; INV_NonceGated's composition with the once-advanced-never-retreats discipline pins T-2 across chain-advance cycles), `docs/SECURITY.md` §S-008 (the closure narrative — operator-configurable cap + fee-priority eviction + per-sender quota + RBF + nonce-gate together constitute the S-008 mitigation; FB33 + FB38 are the two-pane state-machine witness).

Cross-reference. FB33 `MempoolAdmission.tla` (the FULL admission-decision-tree spec — the seven-disjunct gate + five-reason rejection-log + per-sender-quota + sig-verify; FB38 narrows to the cap-eviction + RBF cores with an observable eviction_log; FB33 broadens; together they are the two-pane state-machine witness for the full S-008 closure), FB7 `Nonce.tla` (the per-account nonce gate in isolation — apply-layer focus; FB38's INV_NonceGated is the mempool-layer projection of FB7's Inv_NoStaleApplied; FA-Apply-3 NonceMonotonicity.md is the analytic counterpart), FB23 `FrostVerify.tla` (the FROST-Ed25519 verify soundness theorem; FB38's tx_hash abstraction collapses the cryptographic-identity surface, treating each (sender, nonce, fee) triple as structurally distinct; FB23 + S008BoundedMempool.md S-002 composition is the upstream sig-verify gate FB38 abstracts away), FB25 `RateLimiterEviction.tla` (S-014 closure — the per-IP token-bucket rate limit that bounds the admission attempt RATE; FB38 covers the storage side; together with FB25, the S008BoundedMempool.md T-6 joint rate + storage bound is the composed analytical statement), FB36 `RpcHmacAuth.tla` (S-001 closure — the RPC-layer authentication gate that fires upstream of the mempool admission; sibling spec at the parallel admission surface). FB38 (this spec — the cap-eviction + RBF state-machine companion to S008BoundedMempool.md). Together FB33 + FB38 are the two-pane state-machine witness for the full S-008 closure: FB33 covers the admission-decision-tree coverage at full breadth; FB38 narrows to the eviction-discipline detail with the observable eviction_log surfacing the no-useful-tx-loss claim at TLC trace granularity.

### TcpKeepaliveReap.tla → FA-S026-KeepaliveReap (SO_KEEPALIVE dead-peer reap state machine companion to S026TcpKeepalive.md; FB25 sibling at the gossip-layer resource-exhaustion surface)

| Invariant | Maps to |
|---|---|
| `TypeOK` | shape of `peer_alive` (function Peers → BOOLEAN — TRUE = host reachable at TCP layer, FALSE = host unreachable; set to FALSE by PeerDie), `peer_present` (SUBSET of Peers — currently in peers_ map; grows on PeerConnect, shrinks on ReapDeadPeer), `last_keepalive_response` (function Peers → Nat — time of last successful probe-ACK exchange; refreshed by KeepaliveProbe on live peers, unchanged for dead peers), `now` (Nat — abstract monotonic clock; bounded by MaxTime) |
| `INV_BoundedDeadPeerLifetime` | T-1 (Eventual Dead-Peer Detection, S026TcpKeepalive.md headline witness). Every dead peer (`peer_alive[p] = FALSE`) currently in peer_present has been unreachable for at most `KeepaliveCycle = KeepaliveInterval × KeepaliveProbes` time units. Structural argument: ReapDeadPeer's pre-condition is `now - last_keepalive_response[p] > KeepaliveCycle`; under fairness, any dead peer reaching this bound is reaped. So an unreaped dead peer must have `now - last_keepalive_response[p] <= KeepaliveCycle`. Worst-case timing: a peer goes dead at t1; subsequent KeepaliveProbe actions do NOT refresh last_keepalive_response (the spec's KeepaliveProbe IF-branches on peer_alive[p]); the gap widens via AdvanceTime; at t1 + KeepaliveCycle + 1 the kernel-timeout predicate fires; under fairness ReapDeadPeer fires and removes p. Maps to the OS-level keepalive cycle at `src/net/peer.cpp:147-152` + the asio-completion error path at `peer.cpp:50-69, 72-105, 131-143` + the atomic `peers_.erase` at `gossip.cpp:320-327` |
| `INV_NoFalseReap` | T-3 (No False-Positive Reap). A live peer (peer_alive[p] = TRUE) is never reaped by keepalive — the structural witness for L-7 of the prose proof (false-positive impossibility on live connections). KeepaliveProbe(p) refreshes last_keepalive_response[p] to `now` whenever peer_alive[p] = TRUE; under fairness on KeepaliveProbe, a live peer's `last_keepalive_response[p]` is refreshed periodically, so the staleness gap `now - last_keepalive_response[p]` cannot exceed the inter-probe interval. Therefore the ReapDeadPeer precondition `> KeepaliveCycle` is never enabled for a live peer. The state-form: for any p in peer_present with peer_alive[p] = TRUE, the kernel-timeout predicate is FALSE — ReapDeadPeer cannot fire on p. RFC 1122 §4.2.3.6 — the kernel automatically responds to keepalive probes; the peer's Determ application need not be running |
| `INV_MonotoneTime` | Steady-clock monotonicity (Preliminaries.md §2.2 L-5). `now` is monotone non-decreasing — the structural witness is that every action's `now'` is either UNCHANGED or `now + 1` (AdvanceTime); no action decrements `now`. The state-form: `now \in Nat` (Nat-typed; the monotonicity is captured action-by-action structurally). Mirrors `std::chrono::steady_clock::now()` at `src/net/peer.cpp` whose monotonicity is RFC-mandated |
| `INV_ReapMonotone` | Reaped-stays-reaped-until-reconnect. Once a peer is reaped (removed from peer_present), it stays removed until a fresh PeerConnect re-adds it. Structural witness: ReapDeadPeer is the only action that removes from peer_present (PeerConnect adds, all other actions leave it UNCHANGED). A reaped peer re-entering peer_present requires PeerConnect, which sets peer_alive[p] = TRUE and last_keepalive_response[p] = now — a "fresh start" semantically equivalent to a new connection. Maps to L-5 of the prose proof (Peer-removal atomicity): `handle_peer_closed` acquires `peers_mutex_` and performs `peers_.erase(remove_if(...))` — the atomic erase under the mutex serializes any observer. After the erase the peer is observably removed |
| `PROP_EventualReap` (temporal) | T-1 temporal restatement. Under fairness on KeepaliveProbe + ReapDeadPeer + AdvanceTime, every dead peer is eventually removed from peer_present. The leads-to form: a dead peer in peer_present eventually leaves peer_present. Structural argument: PeerDie sets peer_alive[p] = FALSE but leaves the peer in peer_present; subsequent KeepaliveProbe actions on p leave last_keepalive_response[p] UNCHANGED; AdvanceTime widens the gap; eventually the gap exceeds KeepaliveCycle and ReapDeadPeer is enabled; under fairness it fires; p is removed. State-form witness: `\A p \in Peers : <>(p \notin peer_present \/ peer_alive[p] = TRUE)` — every dead peer in peer_present is transient |
| `PROP_NoLeak` (temporal) | T-2 temporal restatement. peer_present is always a subset of Peers (no orphan admissions — no peer enters peer_present without going through a PeerConnect). The structural witness: PeerConnect is the only action that adds to peer_present; the action's pre-condition gates on `p \in Peers`. The box-clause: `[](peer_present \subseteq Peers)` — invariantly, peer_present is a subset of the universal Peers set |

**Spec status:** written; TLC verification pending (consistent with the other thirty-three specs above). The recommended `TcpKeepaliveReap.cfg` (`Peers = {p1, p2}`, `KeepaliveInterval = 2`, `KeepaliveProbes = 3`, `MaxTime = 12`) is sized for an interactive TLC run in under 30 seconds on a single core. The five-action state machine (PeerConnect / PeerDie / KeepaliveProbe / ReapDeadPeer / AdvanceTime) exercises every reachable interleaving of attach, die, probe-or-no-probe, and reap-on-timeout cycles. Variables modeled: `peer_alive` (function Peers → BOOLEAN — TRUE = host reachable at TCP layer, FALSE = host unreachable; set to FALSE by PeerDie), `peer_present` (SUBSET of Peers — currently in peers_ map; grows on PeerConnect, shrinks on ReapDeadPeer), `last_keepalive_response` (function Peers → Nat — time of last successful probe-ACK exchange), `now` (Nat — abstract monotonic clock; bounded by MaxTime). Actions modeled: `PeerConnect(p)` (peer p opens a TCP connection; adds p to peer_present, sets peer_alive[p] = TRUE, sets last_keepalive_response[p] = now; mirrors the construction sites at `src/net/gossip.cpp:37-48` and `src/net/peer.cpp:151-167`; the Peer constructor flips SO_KEEPALIVE at lines 147-152), `PeerDie(p)` (peer p's host becomes unreachable at TCP layer — models A1 kill-9, A2 NAT eviction, A3 partition adversaries from S026TcpKeepalive.md §2; sets peer_alive[p] = FALSE; UNCHANGED peer_present, last_keepalive_response, now), `KeepaliveProbe(p)` (the kernel emits a keepalive probe — if peer_alive[p] = TRUE the response refreshes last_keepalive_response[p] = now; if FALSE no refresh fires; the staleness gap widens), `ReapDeadPeer(p)` (after KeepaliveCycle elapsed without a probe response, the kernel marks the socket failed, the next asio completion delivers ETIMEDOUT, on_close_ fires, peers_.erase runs; pre-condition `now - last_keepalive_response[p] > KeepaliveCycle`; removes p from peer_present; mirrors the atomic peer-removal pipeline at `src/net/gossip.cpp:320-327` under `peers_mutex_`), `AdvanceTime` (monotonic clock advance by 1; pre-condition `now < MaxTime`; mirrors `std::chrono::steady_clock` monotonicity per Preliminaries.md §2.2 L-5). The KeepaliveCycle = KeepaliveInterval × KeepaliveProbes derived constant collapses the C++ side's two-parameter `tcp_keepalive_time + tcp_keepalive_probes × tcp_keepalive_intvl` cycle into a single Nat-typed bound (sound over-approximation; the bounded-lifetime structural property is independent of the specific parameter values).

This spec captures the S-026 closure at the state-machine layer, COMPLEMENTING FB25 `RateLimiterEviction.tla` at the gossip-layer resource-exhaustion surface. FB25 bounds the per-peer-IP message admission rate via the S-014 token-bucket; FB39 (this spec) bounds the per-peer slot lifetime via the S-026 SO_KEEPALIVE-driven reap. The two operate on orthogonal axes:

| Dimension | FB25 (S-014 rate limiter) | FB39 (S-026 keepalive) |
|---|---|---|
| Per-peer property | Message rate per IP | Liveness status |
| Bounded quantity | Bytes / messages per unit time | Peer-slot count |
| Resource axis | Ingress bandwidth + CPU per IP | File descriptors + memory |
| Adversary surface | High-volume floods from active peers | Long-tail stale-peer accumulation |

The four invariants + two temporal properties pin the three S026TcpKeepalive.md theorems FB39 specifically formalizes:

1. **Eventual dead-peer detection (T-1)** is captured by `INV_BoundedDeadPeerLifetime` + `PROP_EventualReap`. Every dead peer (host crashed, NAT mapping expired, network partition exceeding keepalive detection window) is detected and removed from `peers_` within `KeepaliveCycle = KeepaliveInterval × KeepaliveProbes` of becoming unreachable. The structural argument: PeerDie sets peer_alive[p] = FALSE; subsequent KeepaliveProbes don't refresh last_keepalive_response; AdvanceTime widens the gap; ReapDeadPeer's pre-condition fires; under fairness the peer is reaped.

2. **No false-positive reap (T-3)** is captured by `INV_NoFalseReap`. A live peer (host reachable at TCP layer, kernel responding to keepalive probes) is never removed by the keepalive machinery. The structural argument: KeepaliveProbe refreshes last_keepalive_response on live peers; the staleness gap never exceeds the kernel-timeout cycle; ReapDeadPeer's precondition is never enabled for live peers.

3. **Time monotonicity + reap monotonicity** are captured by `INV_MonotoneTime` + `INV_ReapMonotone`. `now` is monotone non-decreasing (matches steady_clock); a reaped peer stays reaped until a fresh PeerConnect (matches the `peers_.erase` atomicity discipline under `peers_mutex_`).

4. **No leak (T-2)** is captured by `PROP_NoLeak`. peer_present is always a subset of Peers — no orphan admissions. PeerConnect is the only action that adds to peer_present.

**Out of scope** (consistent with this spec's §7 header comment):

- The OS-level keepalive parameter tunability (F-1 Windows defaults, F-2 cross-platform table per S026TcpKeepalive.md §6). The spec treats KeepaliveInterval + KeepaliveProbes as fixed constants; operator-tuning is an orthogonal concern documented in the prose proof.
- The application-layer slow-loris surface (F-3 of the prose proof — A4 adversary). SO_KEEPALIVE cannot distinguish a deliberately-silent application-layer attacker from a legitimate-but-idle peer; the attacker's host kernel still responds to keepalive probes. The spec models TCP-layer unreachability only (PeerDie sets peer_alive[p] = FALSE); a "silent application-layer attacker" would have peer_alive[p] = TRUE and never be reaped — exactly the F-3 limitation. Application-layer policy is required to defeat this.
- The S-014 rate-limiter composition (T-4 of the prose proof). FB25 RateLimiterEviction.tla covers the per-IP rate side; FB39 covers the per-IP slot-lifetime side. The joint composition is documented analytically in S014RateLimiterSoundness.md §6.2 + S026TcpKeepalive.md §5 T-4; no joint invariant is asserted at the FB39 spec layer.
- The S-022 per-MsgType wire-format cap composition. FB36 RpcHmacAuth.tla and S022WireFormatCaps.md cover the per-message size surface; the post-reconnect-after-keepalive-reap path runs the same per-MsgType cap-check, but the size cap itself is orthogonal to keepalive lifetime.
- The keepalive probe's zero-payload property (L-6 + T-5 of the prose proof — no cryptographic material exposure). RFC 1122 §4.2.3.6 — keepalive probes carry zero application-layer payload. The spec layer does not model the wire-format surface at all (the probe-and-ACK cycle is collapsed into KeepaliveProbe's boolean refresh); T-5 is documentary at this layer.
- The asio integration of SO_KEEPALIVE (L-3 of the prose proof). The portable `asio::socket_base::keep_alive` wrapper around `setsockopt(SOL_SOCKET, SO_KEEPALIVE, ...)` is collapsed at the spec layer into PeerConnect's atomic attach + alive-init; the spec does not model the setsockopt call explicitly.
- The error-propagation chain (L-4 of the prose proof — kernel timeout → asio completion handler → `on_close_(self)` → `GossipNet::handle_peer_closed` → `peers_.erase`). Collapsed at the spec layer into ReapDeadPeer's atomic peer-removal; the spec does not model the asio completion lambda layer.

Companion analytic proofs: `docs/proofs/S026TcpKeepalive.md` (the analytic proof this spec is the state-machine companion to — T-1 → INV_BoundedDeadPeerLifetime + PROP_EventualReap, T-3 → INV_NoFalseReap, plus structural witnesses INV_MonotoneTime + INV_ReapMonotone + PROP_NoLeak; T-2 + T-4 + T-5 are sibling-territory composition claims documented at the prose layer), `docs/proofs/S014RateLimiterSoundness.md` (FA-RateLimiter — the per-peer-IP rate-limiter analytic proof; T-4 of the S-026 proof composes with this proof's per-IP token-bucket bound), `docs/SECURITY.md` §S-026 (the closure narrative — SO_KEEPALIVE setsockopt at the Peer constructor + reuse of the existing on_close path together constitute the S-026 mitigation).

Cross-reference. FB25 `RateLimiterEviction.tla` (S-014 closure — the per-peer-IP token-bucket rate limiter with bucket-eviction; FB39 is the sibling at the per-peer-slot-lifetime axis; together FB25 + FB39 cover the gossip-layer resource-exhaustion surface — FB25 bounds per-IP message rate, FB39 bounds per-IP slot lifetime; both share the "bounded per-key resource lifetime" proof shape — FB39's INV_BoundedDeadPeerLifetime mirrors FB25's INV_BucketLifetimeBounded), FB37 `HelloHandshake.tla` (the HELLO peer-handshake state machine — gossip-layer admission gate at attach time; FB39 covers post-attach lifecycle reap; the two together cover the gossip-layer per-peer lifecycle), FB23 `FrostVerify.tla` (the FROST-Ed25519 verify soundness theorem; FB39 is at a different layer — the gossip-transport reap surface vs. the consensus-signature surface; documentary cross-reference), FB36 `RpcHmacAuth.tla` (S-001 closure — the RPC-layer authentication gate; sibling spec at the parallel admission surface; FB36 + FB37 + FB39 together witness the three admission/lifecycle gates across the gossip + RPC surfaces). FB39 (this spec — the SO_KEEPALIVE dead-peer reap state-machine companion to S026TcpKeepalive.md). Together FB25 + FB39 are the two-pane state-machine witness for the gossip-layer resource-exhaustion defense: FB25 covers the message-rate axis; FB39 covers the slot-lifetime axis. The two compose orthogonally without coordination — different state spaces (FB25's `buckets_` map keyed on IP string; FB39's `peer_present` set keyed on Peer ID), different enforcement points (FB25 at the gossip-message-receive entry post-deserialize; FB39 at the kernel-side TCP socket-liveness layer), different resource axes (FB25 ingress bandwidth + CPU; FB39 file descriptors + memory).

---

## Mapping to source code

Each invariant directly mirrors a structure or check in the C++ implementation:

| Spec construct | Source location |
|---|---|
| `Consensus.contribs` | `src/node/node.cpp::on_contrib` (Phase-1 commit gather into `pending_contribs_`) |

| `Consensus.Finalize` quorum | `src/node/validator.cpp::check_block_sigs` (MD: K-of-K full committee; BFT: Q = ceil(2·k_bft/3) within the shrunk k_bft = ceil(2K/3) committee — two-level shrinkage, see PROTOCOL.md §5.3). The spec uses `Keff = ceil(2K/3)` which only models the first-level shrinkage; this is correct degenerately at K=3 (Q=k_bft=2) and an over-approximation at K>=6 (safe direction for the Inv_OneDigest invariant; see Consensus.tla comment above the Keff definition). |

| `FeeAccounting.block_total_fees` | local `total_fees` accumulator at `src/chain/chain.cpp:720`, reset to 0 at the start of every `apply_block` invocation, accumulated per-tx via the `charge_fee` helper at lines 727-732 + the per-branch `total_fees += tx.fee` calls (lines 730, 767, 868, 1221), drained at the line 1286 distribution loop |

Shared with FB15 EquivocationApply and FB16 AbortApply — the composition spec verifies that the slash-accumulator monotonicity from both prior specs holds when the two sub-event classes apply within the same block |
| `MultiEventComposition.applied_receipts` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::applied_inbound_receipts_` (`std::set<std::pair<ShardId, std::string>>` at chain.cpp:204-206). Shape inherited verbatim from FB14 CrossShardReceiptDedup — the spec's DedupKey type and dedup-gate semantics are identical, ensuring cross-block dedup persistence holds under composition |
| `MultiEventComposition.accumulated_slashed` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::accumulated_slashed_` — the A1 conservation counter incremented at chain.cpp:1395 (`accumulated_slashed_ += block_slashed`) after the per-block abort + equivocation loops sum into `block_slashed` (chain.cpp:1327, 1348). The composition spec's ApplyBlock single-step transition collapses both contributions into a single `block_slashed_sum` summation over the abort_slash + equiv_slash arithmetic |
| `MultiEventComposition.accumulated_outbound` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::accumulated_outbound_` — the cross-shard outbound counter. The composition spec preserves this as a write-only zero (the outbound-emit surface is the source-chain's block-finalize step, not the apply path; the spec models only the apply boundary) |
| `MultiEventComposition.pending_block` | implicit: the C++ apply layer consumes from `b.transactions`, `b.abort_events`, `b.equivocation_events`, and `b.inbound_receipts` in canonical order within `apply_block`. The TLA model lifts the Block record's four sub-event fields into an explicit `pending_block` slot so the deterministic-pipeline contract (T-MC3) is observable as a state-machine invariant |
| `MultiEventComposition.ConstructBlock` | producer-side block-baking at `src/node/producer.cpp::try_finalize_round` — the validator-side aggregation of per-tx admissions + per-event aggregations + per-receipt bundling into the Block record. The TLA model abstracts the multi-source aggregation into a single non-deterministic ConstructBlock action; T-MC3 verifies that the apply order is independent of the construction order |
| `MultiEventComposition.ApplyBlock` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::apply_block` — the canonical apply pipeline at chain.cpp:734 (tx loop) → 1313 (abort loop) → 1344 (equiv loop) → 1363 (receipt loop) → 1286 (distribution loop). The TLA model collapses the five loops into a single deterministic transition because the canonical order is fixed at the C++ source-line level — TLC does not enumerate sub-event interleavings within the block |
| `MultiEventComposition.AdvanceHeight` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::Chain::apply_block` block-index increment — shared with all other FB-track specs; the temporal driver for Prop_EventualApply |
| `FrostVerify.key_pubs` | `include/determ/crypto/frost.hpp:61` (the `Point` typedef = `std::array<uint8_t, 32>` — the Ed25519 compressed group public key). The TLA model lifts the 32-byte array to a 32-element sequence over Bytes; the `static_assert(sizeof(Point) == sizeof(PubKey))` at `src/crypto/frost.cpp:113` pins the size equality with the underlying `PubKey` type from `include/determ/types.hpp` |
| `FrostVerify.signed_sigs` | `include/determ/crypto/frost.hpp:62` (the `FrostSig` typedef = `std::array<uint8_t, 64>` — the canonical `R ‖ z` Ed25519 signature shape produced by `frost_aggregate` per RFC 9591 §5.1). The TLA model lifts the 64-byte array to a 64-element sequence over Bytes; the `static_assert(sizeof(FrostSig) == sizeof(Signature))` at `src/crypto/frost.cpp:108` pins the size equality with the underlying `Signature` type. The `signed_sigs` set is the spec-layer model of the honest-signing oracle's output history — every (key, message) pair that has been signed produces a canonical triple in this set |
| `FrostVerify.valid_pairs` | implicit: the abstract Ed25519Verify acceptance relation — the spec-layer model of the EUF-CMA verify predicate from Preliminaries §2.2 A2. Captures `EVP_PKEY_ED25519` verify acceptance at `src/crypto/keys.cpp:79-91` (which OpenSSL implements per RFC 8032 §5.1.7). The TLA model populates `valid_pairs` only via `SignMessage` (honest signing); the EUF-CMA assumption that no polynomial-time adversary forges signatures is modeled as `<<adversary_forged_sig, ..., ...>> \notin valid_pairs` — a deterministic abstraction of the ≤ 2⁻¹²⁸-per-attempt cryptographic bound |
| `FrostVerify.tampered_sigs` | implicit: the byte-tampered-variant set. Models the adversary's `sig'` construction in T-1.1 (corollary of `FrostVerifyDelegation.md` T-1). The action's universal-quantifier clause `\A k2 ∈ generated : \A m2 ∈ Messages : <<key_pubs[k2], m2, sig_prime>> \notin valid_pairs` is the spec-layer enforcement of the EUF-CMA assumption — every tampered sig is structurally excluded from the verify-acceptance relation under any (pub, msg) combination |
| `FrostVerify.verify_log` | implicit: the observable history of `FrostVerify` calls. Indexed by scenario tag (`"canonical"`, `"tampered_sig"`, `"wrong_key"`, `"tampered_msg"`) so INV-1..INV-5 can be evaluated per-case. Lifts the runtime regression at `src/main.cpp` scenario 27 (`determ test-view-root`) — the five assertions there are the runtime witnesses of INV-1..INV-5; the TLA log is the state-machine projection of those assertions across the bounded universe |
| `FrostVerify.scenario` | implicit: a 4-phase marker (`"init"`, `"keygen"`, `"signed"`, `"verified"`) that sequences the workflow actions. No direct C++ correspondent — the C++ side has no explicit phase tracker because `frost_verify` is a stateless function; the TLA marker is purely a state-space-bounding device for TLC (without it, the action enumeration would be unbounded over the seq-of-verify-calls log) |
| `FrostVerify.GenKeypair` | implicit: not exercised by `frost_verify` itself (which consumes `group_pubkey` as an input). Models the v2.10 DKG ceremony's output (group_pubkey + verification_shares per `LocalShare` at `include/determ/crypto/frost.hpp:110-115`) — or, equivalently, a single-party Ed25519 keygen via `EVP_PKEY_keygen` at `src/crypto/keys.cpp:17-33`. The verify-side is structurally identical per RFC 9591 §3; the spec abstracts the keygen path into a single-step nondeterministic action |
| `FrostVerify.SignMessage` | implicit: not exercised by `frost_verify` itself. Models the v2.10 t-of-K partial-aggregation pipeline (`frost_sign_round1` + `frost_sign_round2` + `frost_aggregate` at `include/determ/crypto/frost.hpp:146-169`) as a single atomic step that produces a canonical aggregate. The joint extension `signed_sigs ∪= {<<k, msg, sig>>}` + `valid_pairs ∪= {<<pub, msg, sig>>}` captures RFC 9591 §3 Theorem 1's structural-Ed25519-sig property (the analytic proof's L-1). When v2.10 Phase D ships the real sign primitives, this action becomes the spec-layer abstraction of the multi-round protocol |
| `FrostVerify.Tamper` / `FrostVerify.VerifyTampered` | `src/main.cpp` scenario 27 assertion 2 — the byte-flip + re-verify sequence (`sig[0] ^= 0xff; assert(frost_verify(sig, group_pub, msg) == false)`). The TLA `Tamper` action models the byte-flip; `VerifyTampered` models the re-verify call. The structural EUF-CMA exclusion (`sig_prime \notin valid_pairs`) is the spec-layer reduction of the assertion's "expected false" expectation to a deterministic predicate |
| `FrostVerify.VerifyWrongKey` | `src/main.cpp` scenario 27 assertion 3 — `frost_verify(sig, wrong_pub, msg) == false`. The TLA action's `key_pubs[k_other] # key_pubs[k]` filter ensures wrong-key distinctness; `valid_pairs` only contains the signing-key triple, so the membership check returns FALSE by construction. Matches the analytic proof's T-1.2 reduction to Ed25519 EUF-CMA over the `pk'` key's secret |
| `FrostVerify.VerifyTamperedMsg` | `src/main.cpp` scenario 27 assertion 4 — `frost_verify(sig, group_pub, msg') == false` with `msg' ≠ msg`. The TLA action's `msg_other # msg` filter ensures message distinctness; `valid_pairs` only contains the original-message triple, so the membership check returns FALSE by construction. Matches the analytic proof's T-1.3 reduction to Ed25519 EUF-CMA + SHA-512 collision resistance over the challenge derivation |
| `FrostVerify.VerifyCanonical` | `src/main.cpp` scenario 27 assertion 1 — `frost_verify(sig, group_pub, msg) == true` for the canonical aggregate. The TLA action returns `result = TRUE` by definition: `FrostVerify(sig, key_pubs[k], msg) = Ed25519Verify(key_pubs[k], msg, sig) = (<<key_pubs[k], msg, sig>> \in valid_pairs) = TRUE` (SignMessage populated it). Matches the analytic proof's T-1 forward direction (L-1 + L-2 + delegation operator) |
| `FrostVerify.FrostVerify` | `src/crypto/frost.cpp:101-118` — the function under test. The TLA operator `FrostVerify(sig, group_pub, msg) == Ed25519Verify(group_pub, msg, sig)` is the spec-layer formalization of the C++ delegation chain at lines 107-117 (bytewise copy `FrostSig → Signature` + bytewise copy `Point → PubKey` + forward to `determ::crypto::verify`). The two `static_assert` clauses at lines 108 + 113 are lifted to `INV_TypeContract`'s sequence-length predicates |
| `FrostVerify.Ed25519Verify` | `src/crypto/keys.cpp:79-91` (`determ::crypto::verify` — the OpenSSL `EVP_PKEY_ED25519` wrapper) + RFC 8032 §5.1.7 (cofactored verify equation). The TLA model abstracts this to a `valid_pairs` membership check; the analytic proof's L-2 establishes the equivalence between `determ::crypto::verify` and the RFC equation; the FA-Crypto-Verify track gives the cryptographic tightness, and the FB-track checks the state-machine consistency of the delegation abstraction |
| `MakeContribCommitment.record` | implicit: the spec-layer accumulator for `MakeCommit` outputs across all enumerated input tuples. Lifts the runtime enumeration in `src/main.cpp` `test-view-root` (cited in `MakeContribCommitmentBackwardCompat.md` §7) to the bounded-universe state space |
| `MakeContribCommitment.generated` | implicit: SUBSET of InputTuple — tracks which input tuples have been enumerated by the `Generate` action. Gates the per-tuple invariants (INV-1..INV-6) from spuriously firing at the empty-Init state. No direct C++ correspondent — purely a TLC state-bounding device for the post-enumeration invariants |
| `MakeContribCommitment.Generate` | the runtime calls to `make_contrib_commitment` across the test suite (`src/main.cpp` `test-view-root` assertions at lines 9594-9648 + 10078-10152) — every call site materializes one input tuple, computes the commit, and validates it against the expected algebraic identity. The TLA action abstracts the per-call-site enumeration into a single non-deterministic `Generate` that picks any unenumerated InputTuple and stores its `MakeCommit` value into `record`. TLC explores every reachable enumeration order over the bounded universe |
| `MakeContribCommitment.Saturate` | implicit: post-enumeration stutter when every InputTuple has been generated. The bounded universe ensures TLC will reach saturation; the invariants are evaluated at every reachable state along the way. No direct C++ correspondent — TLC stuttering on a closed state space is purely a model-check tractability device |
| `MakeContribCommitment.IsZero` | `src/node/producer.cpp:242-245` — the `is_zero_hash` lambda: `for (auto byte : h) if (byte != 0) return false; return true;`. The spec-layer `IsZero(h) == h = ZERO` captures the predicate verbatim via the designated `ZERO` element of `Hashes` (= the value-initialized `Hash{}` per `[array.cons]` + `[dcl.init.aggr]`, which is `std::array<uint8_t, 32>{}` = all-zero bytes) |
| `MakeContribCommitment.AllViewsZero` | `src/node/producer.cpp:246-248` — the `!any_view` composite predicate: `bool any_view = !is_zero_hash(view_eq_root) \|\| !is_zero_hash(view_abort_root) \|\| !is_zero_hash(view_inbound_root);`. The spec-layer `AllViewsZero(eq, ab, inb) == IsZero(eq) /\ IsZero(ab) /\ IsZero(inb)` is the negation of `any_view`; when TRUE, the C++ `if (any_view)` branch at lines 249-258 is skipped and the implementation follows the v1 commit shape (L-1 of the companion analytic proof) |
| `MakeContribCommitment.V1Commit` | `src/node/producer.cpp:225-233 + 259` — the v1 commit shape (pre-F2 implementation, also the reachable path when `AllViewsZero` holds): `SHA256Builder inner; for (auto& h : sorted_tx_hashes) inner.append(h); Hash inner_root = inner.finalize();` (lines 225-227) followed by `SHA256Builder b; b.append(block_index); b.append(prev_hash); b.append(inner_root); b.append(dh_input);` (lines 229-233) followed by `return b.finalize();` (line 259, when the `if (any_view)` body is skipped). The spec-layer `V1Commit(idx, prev, txs, dh) == << "V1", idx, prev, InnerRoot(txs), dh >>` captures the four-element pre-image structurally with a `"V1"` discriminator tag for cross-family distinctness (L-3 of the companion proof). InnerRoot itself is the spec-layer abstraction of the inner SHA-256 at lines 225-227 |
| `MakeContribCommitment.F2Commit` | `src/node/producer.cpp:249-258 + 259` — the F2 commit shape (the v2.7 extension when at least one view root is non-zero): the v1 prefix at lines 229-233 PLUS the F2 branch body at lines 249-258 (`b.append(std::string("DTM-F2-v1")); b.append(view_eq_root); b.append(view_abort_root); b.append(view_inbound_root);`) PLUS the finalize at line 259. The spec-layer `F2Commit(idx, prev, txs, dh, eq, ab, inb) == << "F2", idx, prev, InnerRoot(txs), dh, "DTM-F2-v1", eq, ab, inb >>` captures the nine-element pre-image structurally with an `"F2"` discriminator tag. The `"DTM-F2-v1"` literal is encoded as a discriminator-level element rather than a byte-level append because L-3 of the companion proof gives the length-distinguishing argument (104-byte v1 vs 209-byte F2) that the spec layer captures as discriminator-distinctness |
| `MakeContribCommitment.MakeCommit` | `src/node/producer.cpp:219-260` — the function under test. The spec-layer operator `MakeCommit(idx, prev, txs, dh, eq, ab, inb) == IF AllViewsZero(eq, ab, inb) THEN V1Commit(...) ELSE F2Commit(...)` is the structural formalization of the C++ if-branch at lines 242-258: the `is_zero_hash` short-circuit at lines 242-248 evaluates to `AllViewsZero`, and the branch at line 249 picks between the v1 prefix (when `!any_view`) and the F2 prefix + extension (when `any_view`). The C++ header declaration at `include/determ/node/producer.hpp:117-139` with the three default-zero trailing args is what makes the v1 short-circuit reachable from legacy call sites (pre-F2 callers that omit the view-root args) |
| `MakeContribCommitment.InnerRoot` | `src/node/producer.cpp:225-227` — the inner SHA-256 over the sorted-deduped tx-hash list: `SHA256Builder inner; for (auto& h : sorted_tx_hashes) inner.append(h); Hash inner_root = inner.finalize();`. The spec-layer `InnerRoot(txs) == << "inner", txs >>` is the abstraction: a tagged tuple over the tx-list values, structurally distinct from any V1 or F2 pre-image (different tag). The inner-root is injective on distinct tx-lists by A2 (collision resistance of SHA-256); the spec layer captures this by tuple equality on the underlying `txs` value |
| `RateLimiterEviction.buckets` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:151` — `std::map<std::string, Bucket> buckets_` (the per-key bucket map; key = peer-IP string typed as `std::string`, value = `Bucket` struct). The TLA model lifts the C++ map into a function `ActiveKeys → Bucket` where the active subset of `Keys` is the spec-layer analog of `buckets_.find(key) != buckets_.end()` membership. The map's other entries are touched only via per-key operator[] references; per-key locality matches L-3 of the prose proof |
| `RateLimiterEviction.buckets[k].tokens` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:121` — `double tokens{0.0};` field of `struct Bucket`. The TLA model collapses the `[0, C]` interval (per L-1 of the prose proof) into a FULL/EMPTY boolean because the F-1 invariants depend on `last_touch`, not on the precise integer-fractional token amount. The token-bucket arithmetic at rate_limiter.hpp:109-113 (`b.tokens = std::min(burst_, b.tokens + elapsed_sec * rate_per_sec_)` + `b.tokens -= 1.0`) is captured by L-1's interval bound and is orthogonal to the F-1 mitigation; the spec abstracts to FULL after every Consume because that is the post-refill-clamp state under realistic configs |
| `RateLimiterEviction.buckets[k].last_touch` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:122` — `std::chrono::steady_clock::time_point last;` field of `struct Bucket`. Updated unconditionally to `now` on every Consume call at rate_limiter.hpp:108 + 112; the eviction predicate at line 135 uses this field exclusively (`now - it->second.last > threshold`). The TLA model uses Nat-typed time units; the C++ `steady_clock::duration` is bijectively mapped at the spec layer (Preliminaries.md §2.2 L-5 monotonicity preserved by the AdvanceTime action's `delta >= 1` clause) |
| `RateLimiterEviction.next_sweep_at` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:149` — `std::chrono::steady_clock::time_point next_sweep_at_;` instance member. The default-constructed value (`time_since_epoch().count() == 0` at line 96) is the sentinel for "no sweep has fired yet"; the spec models this as `next_sweep_at = 0` at Init. Advanced by the amortized-sweep branch at lines 99-101 (`next_sweep_at_ = now + sweep_interval_sec_;`); the spec mirrors via the Consume action's LET-bound `post_sweep_at` when `sweep_fires` is true |
| `RateLimiterEviction.now` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:89` — `auto now = std::chrono::steady_clock::now();` at the top of every `consume()` call. The TLA model uses Nat-typed monotonic time; the C++ side's `std::chrono::steady_clock` is RFC-mandated monotonic (Preliminaries.md §2.2 L-5 + C++ ISO/IEC 14882:2017 §20.17.7.4 [time.clock.steady]). AdvanceTime's `now' = now + delta` with `delta >= 1` enforces strict-increase, matching the steady_clock contract |
| `RateLimiterEviction.evicted_count` | implicit: the C++ side returns per-call evicted counts from `sweep_idle_locked` at `rate_limiter.hpp:128-143` (`size_t evicted = 0; ... ++evicted; ... return evicted;`) and `sweep_idle()` at line 82 — but does NOT maintain a cumulative counter. The TLA model lifts the per-call return into a chain-level cumulative spec variable to make INV-2 (`EvictionMonotone`) observable across the trace. Operators wanting to observe monotone eviction counts in production would need to wrap `sweep_idle()` with an external counter — the spec captures the desired contract |
| `RateLimiterEviction.was_evicted` | implicit: the C++ side has no equivalent set because eviction is destructive on `buckets_` (the `buckets_.erase(it)` at line 136 deletes the entry; subsequent `buckets_[key]` on the same key default-constructs a fresh entry per the std::map::operator[] semantics). The TLA model lifts the resurrection history into a spec-only audit set so INV-3 (`ResurrectionSafe`) can observe re-touched-after-eviction keys. Structurally equivalent to "would a logging hook on the per-entry erase witness this key" |
| `RateLimiterEviction.ActiveKeys` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:69-72` — the C++ side observes the size via `bucket_count() const { return buckets_.size(); }` (lifted as `Cardinality(ActiveKeys)`). The TLA `DOMAIN buckets` is the spec-layer analog of `buckets_`'s key set |
| `RateLimiterEviction.IsStale` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:135` — the strict-greater eviction predicate inside `sweep_idle_locked`: `if (now - it->second.last > threshold)`. The TLA `IsStale(k) == now - buckets[k].last_touch > EvictionThreshold` is the structural lift; the strict-greater comparison preserves the C++ side's behavior at the boundary (a bucket touched EXACTLY `EvictionThreshold` seconds ago is NOT stale) |
| `RateLimiterEviction.SweepIdle` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:128-143` — the `sweep_idle_locked` private method: short-circuits when eviction is disabled (`if (eviction_threshold_sec_ <= 0.0) return 0;` at line 129), then walks `buckets_.begin()..end()` erasing stale entries (lines 134-141). The TLA model's IF-branch mirrors the short-circuit; the active branch restricts `buckets` to `ActiveKeys \ StaleKeys`, bumps `evicted_count` by `Cardinality(StaleKeys)`, and unions the stale keys into `was_evicted` |
| `RateLimiterEviction.Consume` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:86-117` — the public `consume(const std::string& key)` method. The TLA model captures the sweep-before-touch ordering (lines 95-103 then 105-117) via the LET-bound `sweep_fires` / `post_sweep_buckets` / `post_sweep_count` / `post_sweep_was` / `post_sweep_at` intermediate state, then assigns `buckets'` to the post-sweep state with k touched + set to FULL. The boolean return (`return false` / `return true`) is not invariant-relevant for F-1 — it's covered by FA-T1 (bounded burst) of the prose proof |
| `RateLimiterEviction.AdvanceTime` | implicit: no C++ method advances the clock — `std::chrono::steady_clock::now()` is queried per-consume at line 89, and the OS provides the monotonic value. The TLA model lifts the clock advance into an explicit action so TLC can enumerate over time-step interleavings; `delta` bounded by `MaxTimeStep` keeps the state space tractable |
| `RateLimiterEviction.ForcedSweep` | `include/determ/net/rate_limiter.hpp:79-82` — the public `size_t sweep_idle()` method exposed for tests + operator monitoring. Wraps `sweep_idle_locked(std::chrono::steady_clock::now())` under the mutex; returns the number of entries evicted. The TLA model captures this as a no-op-when-disabled / SweepIdle-when-enabled action with `now` and `next_sweep_at` UNCHANGED (the C++ side does NOT advance `next_sweep_at_` on a ForcedSweep — only the amortized-sweep branch in `consume()` advances it at lines 99-101) |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.chains` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::blocks_` — the in-memory chain held by each node; the TLA model lifts it to `Nodes → Seq(Block)` since the spec models three nodes concurrently. The per-block fields (index, prev_hash, state_root, txs) are the state-integrity-relevant subset of the C++ Block struct at `include/determ/chain/block.hpp:460-484` |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.local_state` | the canonical post-apply state of each node, lifted into a single record per node. The C++ side spreads this across `Chain::accounts_`, `Chain::stakes_`, `Chain::registrants_`, etc. (the ten S-033 namespaces enumerated at `PROTOCOL.md §4.1.1`); the spec collapses to `[height, txs: SUBSET TxUniverse]` because the state-integrity invariants only need a canonical equality predicate on state (FA-Apply-1's determinism contract), not the per-namespace mutation semantics |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.chain_at_rest` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::Chain::save` output at chain.cpp:1944-1985 — the wrapped JSON form `{head_hash, blocks}`. | `BlockchainStateIntegrity.pending_inbox` | `node::Node::pending_blocks_` (the gossip-ingress queue after V1..V20 validator admission); the TLA model abstracts the wire-level signature verification and V-gate sequence into the implicit "any block in pending_inbox is admissible-pending-state-root-check" |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.apply_throws` | implicit: latches when `Chain::apply_transactions` throws `"state_root mismatch at block <h>: ..."` at chain.cpp:1432-1444. The C++ side propagates the exception out through `apply_block_locked` and the A9 atomic-apply rolls back the in-progress mutations. The TLA model lifts the exception propagation into an observable BOOLEAN sentinel because state-machine invariants need a positive marker of "an integrity gate has fired" |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.load_throws` | implicit: latches when `Chain::load` throws `"chain file: head_hash mismatch (tampering or corruption?)"` at chain.cpp:2046-2050 OR when `Chain::append` throws `"Block prev_hash mismatch"` at chain.cpp:54-58 during replay. Both throws sit on the load-time integrity path; the TLA model collapses them into a single BOOLEAN sentinel since the invariant target (INV_LoadDetectsTampering) is "at least one of the integrity gates fired" |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.tampered_at` | implicit: no C++ correspondent — the chain.json file on disk has no "I have been tampered with" flag (that's the whole point of the integrity-check ladder). The TLA model lifts the tamper into an observable spec-only audit field so INV_LoadDetectsTampering can observe the post-tamper state without requiring the model to enumerate over byte-level mutations. The 0..MaxHeight range identifies which block was tampered; "none" is the no-tamper sentinel |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.ProduceBlock` | `src/node/node.cpp::Node::try_finalize_round` at node.cpp:1024-1117 — the six-step producer flow (build_body / tentative-chain dry-run / state_root computation / self-apply / broadcast). The TLA model collapses the six steps into a single atomic action because the C++ side holds the chain mutex across all six; T-3 (Producer Self-Apply Consistency) is the structural witness that the gate-pass on self-apply is unconditional under this serialization |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.ApplyBlockOnReceive` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::Chain::apply_transactions` at chain.cpp:1421-1446 — the S-033 gate's central mechanism. The TLA model captures the prev_hash continuity check (chain.cpp:54-58, lifted into the `prev_ok` LET binding) AND the state_root gate (chain.cpp:1432-1444, lifted into the `gate_passes` LET binding). On either failure the apply latches `apply_throws[n]` and refuses to extend the chain; on success the chain is advanced atomically |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.SerializeChain` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::Chain::save` at chain.cpp:1944-1985 — writes the wrapping JSON `{head_hash, blocks}` form per S-021. The TLA model captures the head_hash population at chain.cpp:1949 (`out["head_hash"] = to_hex(blocks_.back().compute_hash())`); the action also resets the tampered_at sentinel to "none" since an honest save would overwrite any prior on-disk tampering |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.LoadChain` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::Chain::load` at chain.cpp:1987-2054 — the T-1 primary mechanism. The TLA model captures both integrity layers: the per-block `prev_hash` continuity check (via the `validate_chain` helper, mirroring chain.cpp:54-58 inside each `apply_transactions(b)` replay call) AND the head's wrapping `head_hash` recompute (via the `head_hash_ok` LET binding, mirroring chain.cpp:2046-2050). On either failure the load latches `load_throws[n]` and refuses to install the chain |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.TamperAtRest` | the disk-level adversary surface from `BlockchainStateIntegrity.md` §5 case (d) — no direct C++ source-line (the C++ side doesn't tamper with itself); the spec models the adversarial mutation of one block's `txs` field at an arbitrary height. The wrap header's stored `head_hash` is NOT patched (case (c) of T-1, which would require forging committee signatures per A1 / FrostVerify.tla, is out of scope for the state-machine layer). The next LoadChain MUST detect via interior prev_hash mismatch (case (a)) or head head_hash mismatch (case (b)) |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.DivergentTxPropose` | the Byzantine-producer adversary surface from `BlockchainStateIntegrity.md` §5 case (b) — node n submits a block to dest with a state_root that doesn't match the canonical post-apply state. The spec models this via an arbitrary `fake_state` choice constrained to differ from the apply-time computed state. The next ApplyBlockOnReceive at dest MUST latch apply_throws via the S-033 gate's loud-fail. No direct C++ source-line — the wire-level adversary would manipulate the body bytes between sig-gathering and broadcast; the apply-time gate is the structural safety net |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.state_root_of` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::Chain::compute_state_root` at chain.cpp:413-415 — the central S-033 primitive. The TLA operator returns the abstract-hash tuple `<<"ROOT", height, txs>>` as the spec-layer projection of the C++ side's SHA-256 over the ten-namespace sorted-leaves Merkle tree at chain.cpp:267+. Pure function: identical state ⇒ identical root; distinct state ⇒ distinct root (A2 / Preliminaries §2.1 lift) |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.compute_hash` | `chain::Block::compute_hash` — the per-block hash binding (index, prev_hash, state_root, txs); under the zero-skip backward-compat shim, state_root is included when non-zero. The TLA operator returns `<<"HASH", index, txs>>` (the spec's abstract-hash projection); the "HASH" discriminator separates this output namespace from `state_root_of`'s "ROOT" namespace, capturing the C++ side's domain-separation between block-hash and state-root |
| `BlockchainStateIntegrity.validate_chain` | `src/chain/chain.cpp::Chain::append` at chain.cpp:54-58 — the per-block prev_hash continuity check inside the replay loop. The TLA helper recursively walks the chain blocks checking `c[i].prev_hash = head_hash(prefix)` for every block index; mirrors the C++ "for each block, append it (which verifies prev_hash before pushing)" pattern at chain.cpp:1987-2054 |
| `JsonValidation.input_objects` | implicit: the spec-layer accumulator of admitted JSON inputs per surface. No direct C++ correspondent — the 5 surfaces (Wire / RPC / Snapshot / Keyfile / Genesis) each have their own admission paths (`net::Message::deserialize`, `RpcServer::dispatch`, `Chain::restore_from_snapshot`, `crypto::load_node_key`, `GenesisConfig::from_json`); the TLA model lifts them into a per-surface tracking surface for INV-3's surface-tag invariant |
| `JsonValidation.validation_log` | implicit: the spec-layer observable for INV-1 / INV-2 / INV-3 / INV-4. No direct C++ correspondent — the C++ side throws exceptions that propagate up the call stack; the TLA model lifts the per-required-field outcome into a logged sequence so the field-name-context contract can be observed as a state-machine invariant. The byte-level exception message (the `what()` string at the C++ catch site) is abstracted into the BOOLEAN `has_diagnostic` tag |
| `JsonValidation.fired_surfaces` | implicit: SUBSET of Surfaces tracking which entry points have been exercised. Purely a TLC state-bounding device for the SaturateSurface stutter; no direct C++ correspondent |
| `JsonValidation.RequireField` | `include/determ/util/json_validate.hpp:37-49` — the `template <typename T> T json_require(const nlohmann::json& j, const char* field)` helper. The TLA operator returns "MissingField" when `key \notin DOMAIN obj` (mirroring the `if (!j.contains(field)) throw std::runtime_error("S-018: missing required JSON field 'FIELD'")` branch at lines 38-40), "WrongType" when `obj[key][1] /= expected_type` (mirroring the `catch (const std::exception& e) throw std::runtime_error("S-018: JSON field 'FIELD' has wrong type: ...")` branch at lines 44-48), "Pass" otherwise (mirroring `return j.at(field).get<T>()` at line 43). The `json_require_hex` and `json_require_array` length-mismatch / wrong-array branches collapse into the same WrongType outcome at the spec layer |
| `JsonValidation.OptionalField` | `include/determ/util/json_validate.hpp` (no helper — the C++ side uses `j.value(field, default)` from `nlohmann::json` directly + the `if (j.contains(field)) { ... }` guard pattern). The TLA operator returns `obj[key]` when present, `default` when absent — captures the `j.value(field, default)` semantics structurally |
| `JsonValidation.ValidateMessage` | implicit: not a single function — every converted from_json (the 14-row inventory in `JsonValidationSoundness.md` §3.3) is a ValidateMessage invocation at its surface. The TLA operator walks a schema sequence invoking RequireField per entry; the C++ side walks the structural sequence of `json_require_*` calls in the from_json body. Both produce O(\|schema\|) bounded work |
| `JsonValidation.ValidateAtSurface` | the headline action — exercises the per-surface from_json invocation. The 5 surfaces correspond to: Wire = `net::Message::deserialize` at `src/net/messages.cpp:44` + per-message-type from_json (Block / Transaction / ContribMsg / BlockSigMsg / AbortClaimMsg / EquivocationEvent / CrossShardReceipt); RPC = `RpcServer::dispatch` at `src/rpc/rpc.cpp` + structured-payload args (`submit_tx`'s `"tx"`, `submit_equivocation`'s `"event"`); Snapshot = `Chain::restore_from_snapshot` collection wrappers at `src/chain/chain.cpp:1748-1850`; Keyfile = `crypto::load_node_key` at `src/crypto/keys.cpp:55-56`; Genesis = `GenesisConfig::from_json` at `src/chain/genesis.cpp:189-275` |
| `JsonValidation.ExtractOptional` | the optional-field extraction action. The C++ correspondents are the `j.value(field, default)` and `if (j.contains(field)) { ... }` patterns scattered across the 14-row consumer inventory (e.g., `ContribMsg::aborts_gen` at `producer.cpp` reading `j.value("aborts_gen", uint64_t{0})`; `Block::tx_root` / `delay_seed` / `delay_output` / `consensus_mode` / `bft_proposer` / `partner_subset_hash` / `state_root` at `Block::from_json` each wrapped in `if (j.contains(...))`). The TLA action leaves `validation_log` UNCHANGED — captures the silent-default-on-absence contract that backward-compat rolling upgrades rely on |

A reviewer who is suspicious of a particular invariant can:

1. Identify the source-code line that should enforce it (table above).
2. Read the code at that location.
3. Confirm the code matches the spec's guard or update.

---

## Counter-examples found (none expected)

If any TLC run produces an invariant violation, this section will record:

- The violated invariant.
- The trace TLC printed (state sequence leading to violation).
- The diagnosis: spec bug vs. real implementation bug.
- The fix.

**Current entries:** none.

---

## Known TLA+ spec limitations

These are *modeling* limitations — not implementation gaps:

1. **No cryptography modeled.** Signatures are abstracted as set membership. The FA-track analytic proofs (FA1, FA6) handle EUF-CMA bounds; the TLA+ spec only models the message flow.
2. **Single-height projection (Consensus).** The model checks one height at a time. Cross-height safety (chain growth, fork-choice) is a separate concern that follows from per-height safety + linear chain structure.
3. **No actual hashes.** Digests are small integers; the spec asserts no collisions trivially. SHA-256 collision resistance is an external cryptographic assumption (FA-track).
4. **Bounded state.** `MaxRounds`, `MaxTransfers`, `MaxBlocks` cap the model. TLC exhausts the bounded state space; analytic proofs (FA-track) give the unbounded result.

These limitations are *intentional* — TLA+ is for state-machine correctness, not cryptographic security. The FA-track and FB-track together cover both layers.

---

## CI integration (future)

The natural next step is wiring TLC into CI:

```yaml
# .github/workflows/formal.yml (sketch)
- name: TLA+ model check
  run: |
    cd docs/proofs/tla
    for cfg in Consensus Sharding Receipts AccountState Snapshot Nonce StakeLifecycle DAppRegistry FeeAccounting; do
    for cfg in Consensus Sharding Receipts AccountState Snapshot Nonce StakeLifecycle DAppRegistry SubsidyDistribution; do
    for cfg in Consensus Sharding Receipts AccountState Snapshot Nonce StakeLifecycle DAppRegistry GovernanceParamChange; do
    for cfg in Consensus Sharding Receipts AccountState Snapshot Nonce StakeLifecycle DAppRegistry CrossShardReceiptDedup; do
    for cfg in Consensus Sharding Receipts AccountState Snapshot Nonce StakeLifecycle DAppRegistry GovernanceParamChange EquivocationApply; do
    for cfg in Consensus Sharding Receipts AccountState Snapshot Nonce StakeLifecycle DAppRegistry GovernanceParamChange AbortApply; do
    for cfg in Consensus Sharding Receipts AccountState Snapshot Nonce StakeLifecycle DAppRegistry GovernanceParamChange AppliedReceiptRestore; do
      java -jar tla2tools.jar -config $cfg.cfg $cfg.tla
    done
```

This isn't shipped yet (no Java in the build container). When it lands, this document gets the actual transcript appended.

## Conclusion

The nine TLA+ specifications cover the state-machine layer of Determ's safety, atomicity, apply-layer, snapshot/restore, tx-replay-defense, stake-lifecycle, DApp-registry-lifecycle, and per-block fee-accounting properties. Combined with the analytic FA-track proofs (cryptographic layer), they form a two-track verification approach:
The nine TLA+ specifications cover the state-machine layer of Determ's safety, atomicity, apply-layer, snapshot/restore, tx-replay-defense, stake-lifecycle, DApp-registry-lifecycle, and block-subsidy-distribution properties. Combined with the analytic FA-track proofs (cryptographic layer), they form a two-track verification approach:
The nine TLA+ specifications cover the state-machine layer of Determ's safety, atomicity, apply-layer, snapshot/restore, tx-replay-defense, stake-lifecycle, DApp-registry-lifecycle, and governance-parameter-change properties. Combined with the analytic FA-track proofs (cryptographic layer), they form a two-track verification approach:
The ten TLA+ specifications cover the state-machine layer of Determ's safety, atomicity, apply-layer, snapshot/restore, tx-replay-defense, stake-lifecycle, DApp-registry-lifecycle, and cross-shard-receipt-dedup properties. Combined with the analytic FA-track proofs (cryptographic layer), they form a two-track verification approach:
The ten TLA+ specifications cover the state-machine layer of Determ's safety, atomicity, apply-layer, snapshot/restore, tx-replay-defense, stake-lifecycle, DApp-registry-lifecycle, governance-parameter-change, and equivocation-slashing-apply properties. Combined with the analytic FA-track proofs (cryptographic layer), they form a two-track verification approach:

- **FA-track**: human-readable, cryptographically tight, unbounded.
- **FB-track**: machine-checkable, structurally exhaustive over bounded models.

Both tracks cite the same source-code locations, so a reviewer can trace any property end-to-end: theorem → state-machine model → source code.
